O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, most dear son, I have completed this book which is the last of the science of medicine together with its fulfillment, and have made the end through its explanations and its interpretations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely 'surgery'.
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is very rare in our region and is greatly diminished throughout, therefore the science has been lost and scattered, and there remains nothing of it but small descriptions in books that have been moved by hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	"And from this comes error and vanity, and minds are closed and knowledge is neglected."
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	"I believe that I want to revive this work together with the ordering of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come together with the forms of the irons of cautery and other tools of the work with the arrangement of declaration and preparation of them, as it is necessary."
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	"And because there are no good surgeons found in our time, the art of medicine is neglected."
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	"And it is necessary for someone who practices this to climb up in the science of anatomy, as Galen said, so that they know the judgment of limbs and their forms, joints, separations, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and muscles and the number of bones, movements and veins moving and resting, and where they exit."
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	"And therefore Hippocrates said that a name without a deed is much, but with a deed it is little; and the same goes for the art of surgery."
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	"We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned before should guard himself so that he does not fall into error and kill people, just as I have seen many times those who practice this science abandoning their knowledge and experience."
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	"For I saw a foolish physician who cut off one aposteme of scrofula from the neck of a woman, and he cut the arteries of her neck; so much blood came out that the woman died in his hands."
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	"And I saw another physician who extracted a stone from the bladder of a man, and the stone was large; so he took with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died three days later."
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	"And I had already been called for to remove it, and I saw the condition of the sick man and the size of the stone, and I knew well that if they cut him he would die."
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	"And I saw another physician who took in charge one of our dukes who had his leg broken and wounded at the same time, and this physician, full of ignorance, tied the break on top of the wound with strong bandages, without leaving any ointment on the wound, and he left him like that for a period. And he commanded that it should not be untied, and it remained like that until the leg was completely swollen and the foot rotted away."
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	"I was called to go to him, and I hurried to come and untie his leg, and when I had it loosened, he was at peace and felt no pain."
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	"But all the way the corruption was already confirmed in the member, and I could not save it. And the corruption did not stop going through the member until the whole limb was lost."
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	"And I saw another physician who burst an inflamed aposteme and then cauterized it with the malice of his ignorance."
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	"For a chancre, when it is purified of melancholic humor, should not be touched with iron if it cannot be completely excised in that place."
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	"And therefore, dear son, you should know that the art of surgery is divided into two parts: one where there is danger in many dispositions. And I will show in each place in this book where there is fear and danger."
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Why you must guard yourself so that foolish physicians cannot speak ill of you Take up your weapons in haste And undertake your patients lightly and firmly And use the best way so that by God's grace you may attain salvation and be praised Leave fearful diseases to severe healing And cast aside your weapons from those who cause doubt And have faith in yourself so that you may come from this world to the next in glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen says in some of his instructions: "Do not take on serious illnesses unless you wish to be called a foolish physician.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have composed this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	"The first chapter is about cauteries of fire and cauteries of hot medicine, and it is arranged from the head down to the feet. And about the forms of instruments, and about the iron tools for cauterizing, and everything that is necessary in this work."
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	"The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and about cupping glasses and wounds, and about extracting splinters, and similar things. And it is arranged with the forms of instruments."
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	"The third chapter is about reducing dislocations and sprains, and similar things. And it is arranged from the head down to the feet, with the forms of instruments."
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	"Before we begin our discussion on surgery, it is necessary that I explain the quality of each humor and its harmful effects."
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	"I say that the qualities of the humors and their harmful effects are the longest speech and most subtle science and secret replies. And many wise men spoke about this and agreed on it. But I will be brief because I fear lengthiness."
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	"I say that cautery is useful for all humors where there is matter, except for two types of humor: hot and dry humor without matter."
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	"Some said that in hot and dry humor together with matter, cautery is greatly helpful. And others said the opposite: that cautery is not useful for an illness that comes from heat and dryness."
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	"For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be used to treat hot illnesses with heat or dryness. And he who says the opposite argues that cautery greatly helps hot and dry illnesses that occur in the body."
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	"For when you compare the body and its moisture to the nature of fire, you find the body cold."
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	"And I agree with this statement."
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	"For I have found it true through experience."
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	"And anyway, let no one meddle with it except those who have tried it and know the art of cautery through long experience, and who know the diversity of humors in humans, their dispositions, causes of illnesses, seasons, and ages. We are not afraid of other humors, especially cold and moist ones."
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	"And all physicians agreed and concurred about cautery."
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	"And know, son, that fire cautery is one of the secrets of healing, and has greater effectiveness than cautery with hot medicine."
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	"For fire is simple, and it only comes to the member that is cooked, and does not harm other members if there are none."
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Hot medicines travel from limb to limb in burning and cause serious diseases in the limbs. Sometimes they kill the patient because of their heat and goodness unless there is an excess present.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	"And this I have found through experience and the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it is based on the truth of things. And for this reason, I apologize for the length of my speech, as I do not wish to deprive you of the secret that is concealed in fire, nor its quality and how it overcomes illnesses of the body, as philosophers demonstrate. Now receive these thoughts."
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	"And know, son, that they agreed on when cauteries should be performed, and chose appropriate seasons."
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	"And I say that cauterization is necessary at all times, because the harm that arises is kept beneath it with the aid of cauterization; and especially if cauterizations are for painful wounds which cannot wait until greater evil comes to the limb."
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	"And do not think, dear child, as foolish doctors do; for the disease that is cured by cauterization has no relapse; and they say it thus: but it is not so as they believe, because cauterizations are not medicine which changes complexion, and dries up the humors which cause pain, and is worth more than medicine for its swiftness in value and power in working."
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	"And it sometimes happens that diseases come according to the complexion of the sick person and the location of the disease and its strength; and superfluities are gathered in him by the acquisition of foods and similar things, unless cauterizations are applied where there is little excess and moisture, such as dental cauteries for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return often; but this happens rarely."
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	"And many people do not understand why cauterizations are called the last resort of medicine, and it is true; but they do not believe that cauterizations are worth anything after medicines, their intentions are false, and cauterizations are the last resort of medicine because when we apply remedies for any disease and they do not work, then we apply cauterization, and it is effective."
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	"Therefore it is clear that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish doctors."
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	"The ancients said that cauterizations with instruments of gold are more effective than those of iron, and they said this only because of the quality of gold and its high substance. They also said that the place of cauterization does not cause corruption, but this is not true, for I have proven it and found that it is true in some people. And cauterizations with gold are more effective than those with iron, as they said."
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	"And even so, when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know how hot it is by the color of the gold, and it quickly cools down. And if one heats it too much, it melts in the fire, and thus there are many obstacles."
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	"And for these reasons we use iron cauteries that we have better equipped for our work."
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	"Now I have arranged this chapter from beginning to end so that the way may be easier to find."
dou cautere olivaire	"About the olive cautery"
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	**Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil:** This cautery is useful for dampness and cold affecting the brain.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	"The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged by a solvent medicine moistening the head for three or four nights, according to what the strength, age, and constitution of the patient can withstand; then make heat behind the patient's head."
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	"And then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on his knees; afterwards put the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; and where your middle fingers meet, there should he be cauterized with the 'olive-shaped' cautery, of which this is the form:"
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And place him on the line marked with ink, and make in descending and squeezing motion little by little while turning your hand; then lift your hand gently, and look at the bone if you see it a little bit; and if you do not see it, then start cauterizing again until you see the bone as I told you; afterwards take a little bit of wax, and put in woven and soft cotton inside, and place it on the wound, and let it stay for three days; afterwards put on clean cloth moistened in butter; and leave it on until the burn is healed; afterwards heal the wound with the ointment called 'tetrafarmacon' until it is healed."
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	"And the ancient ones said that when the wound stays open longer, it purges more; and therefore they encourage more wounds."
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	"And some of them said that one should leave the cautery on until part of the bone is burnt; then remove what is burnt from the bone and heal it."
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	"And others say that one should leave the cautery on and press it so hard as to abate of the bone about as wide as a thread that women put in their spindles so that the humors may flow out more freely; and the wound should be kept open for a long time; afterwards, it should be healed and dressed."
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	"And these two methods of cauterization do not seem to me to be entirely good in all cases except perhaps for some men who are fearful; and I believe that one should leave it alone because the flesh is weakened by continuous natural solutions, as we see in other members. And likewise when the flesh of the sick person is weak by nature, the first sign of cauterization is more saving and beneficial for me, and with this method I currently work together safely."
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	"About the ancient pain in the head"
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	"When there comes chronic pain in the whole head that lasts a long time, the sick person should use remedies and pills called 'cochiae', and also purgatives for the head, oils, and plasters. And if one does the cautery that we have mentioned earlier, it is not effective."
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	"Be careful if the flesh of the sick person is strong by nature and not too cold. In that case, cauterize with a little bit of the cautery that we have mentioned earlier."
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	"Afterwards, make cauteries on each horn of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and make one cautery where it is called 'vessels'; this is the place where cupping glasses are put. And lift your hand so that you do not see the bone: the sick person feels much greater pain in this cautery than in the others, and I will speak about it later; and the cauteries on the horns should be more subtle than those used for the middle of the head, and here is the form:"
dou cautere dou chief	"About the cautery of the head"
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain comes to a part of the head,
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The fire cautery is thus: you take a fig branch and remove its bark, chopping it into two pieces at the joints. Then make an incision on the temple where the pain holds in such a manner that you can place the fig branch underneath the skin; and when it is placed, bind it tightly and leave it like that for twelve hours; then untie it and draw out the fig branch, leaving the wound thus for two or three days. Then apply cotton soaked in butter until it seeps out.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the application of ointment, as long as it is healthy; and if you see fit to use any of the burning medications that I have written about in the second treatise on burning medications.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery follows this manner
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery of which this is the shape
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and is called "closed" because its head is made in the shape of a claw with a little curve, and in the middle has a small appearance. And put it on the painful area, and hold your hand so that you turn the fire lightly until half of the edge of the heart is burned; and lift your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is outside, and let an abundance of blood flow out
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After that, put cotton on wool thread, and place it on the wound for three days; then put cotton soaked in butter, and then treat the wound with ointment until it is healthy. And if you wish to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "cultellare", at its entire point, be careful not to cut the artery in this migraine which is not old.
de emigraine	Of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat migraine as we have said before in the divisions of illnesses, and it does not help, and you see that the cauteries mentioned earlier with medicine or iron do not suffice, then it is necessary to heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white. Then, swiftly place it on the painful area along a line half as long as two fingers, and lift your hand once, ensuring that you do not cut the artery and that you do not go right down to the bone; be careful of the mandible which moves when chewing, and ensure that the nerve does not look back so that the mandible does not spasm and cause discomfort, especially for someone who is not used to it and has no experience; leave the wound open in the middle. But I will tell you how blood is restrained when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it pertains to in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauteries do not suffice for the illness and the patient is suffering, then cauterize him on the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed. And if you wish, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two blades; this cautery is better and more helpful than the other one.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	Of earache caused by cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When there is pain in the ear due to cold, and various solvent medicines have been applied and other treatments as mentioned earlier in this division, but the pain does not subside, then heat this cautery called "pointe", of which here is the shape:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After making ten points all around the painful ear, or around both ears if the pain is in both, and then moving away a little from the root of the ear where you have made the sign, and having made ten points around each ear, then treat the wound until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	Of mouth ulceration
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Ulcers that must be treated by cautery are only those which move pus, as we have said in the divisions of illnesses. Do not perform cauteries on similar ulcers which come from heat and inflammation of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this ulcer which secretes pus from the ears and from evacuations of the head and gargarisms, and these do not help, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, another a little way out from the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips; place the cautery on the healthy part that opens up, and make the cautery just above the head of the ear a little below the ear lobe, and another one in the temple as long as a pea; leave the cautery there until half of it is burnt; this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And this is the shape of the cautery that we have mentioned earlier, but it is a little more subtle and the blade should be a little thicker. After making the cautery, treat the wound as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is ancient and you treat it as we have said before, but there is no improvement and the patient does not have a fever, then make four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one on the spot called "vessels" as we have mentioned earlier, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; treat them as we have said before.
de litargie	Of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this illness, give the patient large drinks and pills made from powdered mallow seeds for the brain. After that, raise the head of the patient entirely, and place on the occiput the plaster of mustard which is written about in the treatise on plasters; this is the manner of cautery: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is healthy thus, good; and if it isn't, apply three cauteries around the head descending to the neck with a space of two fingers between each cautery; and treat it as the others, and if you see it joining, and the patient bears it, apply one cautery in the middle; and if necessary, two more above the two horns, and treat until it is healthy; and let the cautery called "olivare" be used, as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	The head must be cleansed of years and the things that we have said before; then raise the head of the patient, then apply a cautery around the head and on each horn, and one behind and three on the nape of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient bears it, and the disease is strong, apply four cauteries on the back; and leave it until the most of the heart is burned, then remove your hand; then treat until it is healthy, and let the cautery called "olivare" that we have said before be used.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should only use the bloodletting cautery that is phlegmatic in nature, and it is first necessary to cleanse the brain of years and other treatments that we have said in the section when the patient is large and able to withstand taking medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot withstand it, perform gargling and chewing to cleanse the brain often with good foods; then raise the head in the middle, and apply one cautery according to what we have said before, and one on the vessel, and on each horn; and if the patient is strong and bears it, apply cauteries as I have said for those who have paralysis and flaccidity of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, apply one subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When excesses or corrupted moisture and thick phlegm are present due to melancholy, then apply the cautery with small cauteries as we have said for those who have paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if excesses tend towards melancholy due to the cause of melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give him to drink something by which the brain may be cleansed, according to what is said before in the section.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After raise the patient's head; after make one bandage of fine linen, like a circle, and put it on his head; and the patient sits crossed-legged, and is held well from all sides; after present the lint, and warm with old sheep butter; and when heated by fire temperately, so that the forehead can withstand it; after empty the circle inside the head, and let it cool; and do this to the patient once a week with good governance, until he is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you see cauterization being done, make several holes all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cautery moistens the head more greatly; then place cotton wet in butter and chicken fat on top.
de l’awe des eulz	of the awe of eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When awe first comes upon the eyes due to the signs I have mentioned, then begin and give the patient something cleansing the head, and ward off all dampness, and make him sweat or take many baths fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After he commands to raise his head, and makes a cautery on the head, and makes two cauteries on the two temples if the descent of awe is on both eyes together, or one if it is on one; and cut away with all the cautery all the veins and arteries that are below the heart, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple; and take care of decorrement of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stay it with such power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you about the extraction of arteries and the incision of cauterization how you should perform it; and sometimes one makes a cautery or cutting below the two rear bones.
dou cors des larmes	Of the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When tears from the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins or near the arteries that appear on the outside of the head, and one sees that they are cold humid superfluities, then make the cautery as I have said at the beginning of awe descending upon the eyes: one cautery on the head, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries on the hatchel below the two bones; and if there is need for more, then cauterize sanguely above the eyebrow with many small cauteries.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	Of the body of tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help at all, then give the patient three nights of cooked cocks' broth. Then raise his head, and make a cautery on the middle of the cautery olive; and make two cauteries called "clavilis" on the two eyebrows, a little below the eyebrows; and be careful not to cut the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery that is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the oil is softened by illness and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery called "olivary.
de coi ci est li forme:	of which this is the shape
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see fit to make two cauteries on the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrows are; and do not let your hand rest there except until about one-third of the membrane is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	Of the hair that points out the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes it happens that the hair of the eyes turns inward and points at the eye, and one makes cauteries in two ways: either by fire or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even. If they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they have grown and are even, then have the patient lie down on their back. After that, draw a figure on the paper of the eyes resembling the shape of the palm of one's hand, with the beginning of the mark near the hairs; then place moistened cotton in egg white and powdered myrrh on the eye, then heat the cautery which has this form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cauterize little by little many times along the figure you have drawn until the skin is burned in that place. The sign of success is when you see the paper recede and the hairs stand upright at the point of the eye. Then lift your hand, and leave it like this for three days, then apply moistened cotton with butter until the burning is gone; afterward dress with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if afterward the hairs come back and the paper is softened again then begin the cautery anew in that same place as you did at first; but if the hairs have fallen out, cauterize until the paper rises to its natural place, and is even, and does not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cautery of the burning medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even. Then make parchment in the shape of the leaf of myrtle; then take three parts each of French soap and live wax, grind them together well, and do it quickly so that it does not cool. Then spread it on the form that you have made like the leaf of myrtle, and place it on the paper of the eyes. And if the patient holds only one eye, then work in one, and if both, then both also. And place moistened cotton in egg yolk under the eye. And let the patient's flesh be on your hand, and put your two fingers pressing on the medicine, and press gently each time that the patient feels a bite of the medicine, for they feel the bite like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for some time, then remove the medicine from your hand.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the cauterization is complete, then lift up the skin's surface, and see if the paper rises as if it were lifted by fire's constraint or by incision; if so, it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, apply the medicine again on the surface where it has not opened until your work is equal and your eyes are focused; then place cotton wet in butter until the burn cools, afterwards cleanse the skin's surface with the ointment called "diaphoresis" and others until it is healthy.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you need to guard carefully against your work, take great care that it does not fall into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft afterwards, and the hairs prick in the eye, then begin the cautery again on that spot softened by the same paper, just as you did before; then continue the treatment until it is healed. This is the method of the mirror's bellows.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and littleness, and according to that let your constraints be; and do not reply the straight way to him who is engaged in this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	de la cure de fistule par cautere
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not help, then it is necessary for you to perform a cautery on it according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Command the patient to put their head in your hand. Then hold the patient's head between your hands so that they do not move or turn their head. Then place moistened cotton in egg yolk or in juice of parsley on the eye. Afterward heat the cautery which is shaped like this: and is pointed at the top like a roof tile, altogether the cautery should be pointed from one end to the other, and if you see it should be as long as the length of the cautery. But anyway, this one that is pointed will serve better for your purpose.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	Afterward press the fistula if it is open and draw out the corruption and dry it. And if it is closed then open it and draw out from its side. Afterward put on the heated cautery strongly, and hold your hand on the cautery at the part of the nose above the eye so that your hand does not make a mistake; then place the cautery in the fat of the eye and burn it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If at the beginning of the cautery you reach down to the bone, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then begin the cautery again once more, and if necessary repeat it twice, leaving it for three days. Afterwards, put moist cotton in butter on it, and continue with the healing ointment until it is healed. And if after forty days it has not healed, apply a corrosive hot medicine until the bone is exposed; and follow what is written according to this chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a method of cauterizing a fistula which some of the ancients spoke about.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understand a fistula and open it up; afterwards put into the opening a subtle little cone such as this is the shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And they make it of the quantity of three grains of pitch. And hold your hand on the camel's hair brush firmly and do not let the patient move their nose so that the melted pitch does not run into their eye. And it is necessary to place moistened cotton with egg yolk or water on the patient's eye. The pitch then burns in the place of the fistula, and heals it by marvelous healing.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have spoken of, that is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then it becomes necessary to administer a hole to the nose and bring the fistula back into its proper place within the nostril.
des crevaices en levres	de las fisuras en los labios
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times, cracks occur on lips called "hairs," especially on children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as we have described in the chapters above and the treatment does not help, then apply one small cauterizing iron according to this shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it quickly in those cracks until it reaches the flesh; afterward, dress the area with wax until it is clean.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the boil on the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When a boil appears at the root of the throat or tonsil, or palate, or at the roots of the teeth, and it causes putrefaction and rot and becomes filled with pus and forms a fistula; and you treat it as we have described in the chapters above but it does not improve: then you must have one cautery according to the size of the fistula; afterward, open the opening or hole of the fistula, and hold your hand until the hot iron reaches the bottom of it, and on the back side of the area; and do this once or twice, after that treat it with what we have described above until it is clean; and if it is cured in this way, then it is good; but if not, then you must uncover the area and remove the rotted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	on tooth mobility
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines but they do not help, then place the patient's head in your hand; afterward heat the cautery whose form will come hereafter in this manner so that you place a tube on the tooth; and put hot coals inside the cautery quickly, and hold your hand until the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; afterward remove your hand and begin the cautery according to your desire; afterward have the patient fill their mouth with salted water, and let them keep it for an hour and spit it out forcefully.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the tooth that was moving becomes fixed, and the softened gum becomes constrained, and the corrupt moisture dries up.
de la dolor des dens	from toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from coldness, whether it is visible or hidden, and remedies with medicine do not help, then there must be cauterization in two ways: cauterization with butter and cauterization with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cauterization with butter is done thus: take virgin butter and place it on the tip of an iron or brass spoon; afterward take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a tent stake, and dip it in boiling butter, and quickly place it on the aching tooth until it cools; do this often so that its virtue reaches the root of the tooth. And if you see that wetting the wool and cotton in cold butter does not help, then place an iron on hot coals until the fire reaches the cheek of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cautery by fire should be such that you take an iron or brass cane and make it thick so that the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient; afterwards heat the cautery, the shape of which will come later, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery has cooled down; do this often for the pain will be relieved on the same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fills their mouth with good butter at the time of this cautery and then wipes it off; and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery of whichever head you want, according to what you have power to do; and here is the form of the rod:
des scrophules	Scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofula are hot and of cold moistures, and not yielding to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery hair remover which follows here with two openings for smoke to exit from the other part of the cautery; and place the hot cautery on the abscess once or twice until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; if the abscess is small, place the cautery according to its quantity and leave it for three days; then put moistened cotton soaked in butter until the burn is healed; afterwards treat the area with ointments and dressings until it is clean.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the candle:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moistures prevail upon the channels of the lungs, especially when it is due to cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be made void first by dissolving medicines; afterwards make a cautery at the root of the throat, ensuring you do not come close to the throat itself and only slightly touch the skin.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards perform another cautery at the joint of the neck to the head of the spine, and let the cautery used be that called "clavile" for which we have the shape before; and heal the place as we have said earlier until it is clean.
de la toust	de la toux
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and every disease of the lung are of cold moistures, and the patient has neither fever nor heat, and the disease is ancient, then perform two cauteries on the chest in its hollow places; and another cautery within the breast between the two breasts; and let the cautery that is called "clavile" be according to the form mentioned above.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, perform cautery by pricking all around with the cautery called "poins" for which the shape is shown before in the disease of the ears; and let there be thirty or so points, or as many as necessary.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	Afterwards heal the place according to what is said before, and let the cautery be three fingers wide according to this shape:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And because the cauteries are lighter thus, you make them three together at once.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder blade
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the shoulder blade is dislocated due to moisture and it is put back in place but cannot remain there and returns constantly with even small movements, as we have experienced, then it is necessary that you first reduce the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards have the patient lie on their back and side; afterwards lift the heart that is inside the titillite with the fingers of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inside, then heat the cautery that has two inches with this form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	and cauterize the heart until it pierces to the side, and let the figure of the cautery come together with four cauteries; and because this is done with the cautery that has three inches, therefore there are six figures of cauterization; and they are according to the fineness of a thread, and this is the form of the cautery that has three inches:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And sometimes it is added onto one nerve, therefore there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Afterwards put on a poultice of bruised lentils with salt; afterwards let the patient rest, and do not move their limbs for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated upwards, which happens rarely, then perform cautery on the thickness of the cautery clavile, or many pricking cauteries.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For once the joint is closed and the moisture removed, the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and much moisture come to the stomach causing it to stray from its nature, and catarrh is multiplied in him, and despite usual treatments he derives no benefit, then the patient must be turned onto his back, extend his legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	For this, do as follows: make three cauteries on the inside of the armpit near the elbow with the quantity of two fingers' width, each cautery should be made like a key, and two cauteries outside the two sides such that the figure of the cauteries forms three angles, and there is enough space between them so they do not join together when they fester; and the cauteries should be deep enough to reach both parts of the heart, and the figure of the cauteries should follow this form without adding or reducing.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see that a large cautery is necessary in the stomach according to this form, and whoever fears this cautery should make a small prick and press on the stomach for one point according to the quantity you need to do; then cauterize the whole cautery which is called "the point".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment that we have spoken of before has been completed, as long as it is healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver causes pain due to coldness and moisture and excess wind, so much that it is severely changed from its natural complexion by superfluities; and if the patient is treated with what we have said in divisions, but does not improve, then the patient should be placed on his back on his bed. Sign of this is three cauteries according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, avoiding the hypochondria, where the ribs come together; and let there be the thickness of two fingers between each cautery; and let the cautery be long enough for the body, and do not press too much with your hand throughout the cautery. Burn only half the length of a finger, and let the patient lie on his right side on his feet. If he cannot do this, then let him lie down on his back and stretch out his legs, raising his arms. This is the form.
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if you have the ability to do so, cauterize these cauteries with the scalpel, if you are skilled and wise in the art, and be careful not to burn all of the heart, for you would dry out the whole body; and let it not come close to an artery, for the heart is very subtle there, and especially at the root.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When he has an abscess in the liver,
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And then when this treatment is performed by the physicians, so it is necessary that the patient lies on their back; and then seize with a cloth the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which resembles a ray, of which here is the form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize with the cautery until the heart is burned, and come up to the syphac, until all the pores are entirely opened; afterwards treat according to the treatment of the veins until it is healed; and indeed only those who have long studied in the art of medicine should use this cautery, by whom many such diseases have been cured.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	So then he can bravely operate, although it seems to me that it would be better for him to leave it alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	of the cautery for pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one should perform for pleurisy cauteries of roots of artichokes, and in this manner: take a root of artichoke, the largest that you can find, dry and as thick and long as your fingers; and moisten it in oil, and heat it in the fire, and perform one cautery between the navel and the neck, and two small cauteries a little way down in the part that is under the beard; and two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, leaning back a little; and one cautery in the breast, and another on the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two on the sides of the breast away from the cautery that is between the two shoulders; and do not press your hand, but do it openly, just as one does when smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And some ancient authors said that someone used a cautery like a razor, heated it and placed it between the ribs until it reached that abscess; and immediately the pain ceased, as we have mentioned regarding the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear where the patient dies now, or a fistula occurs which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse with the methods that we have said under the division of cures, and it is not helpful, then there are three ways of cautery that are all good:
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.
