Of these, one manner is such that you make three or four cauteries, aligning them according to the length of the mouse (back), following the figure of the liver cautery we mentioned earlier; and do not rush your hand through the entire cautery, and have the patient lie on their back; and another manner of cautery is such that you heat the cautery which has two nereids (embers), as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the heart which is near the mouse (back), where the rib of the patient comes towards the left, and let the elevation by which you lift the heart be according to the heart, according to the length of the body, and let the cauteries be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	Afterwards, place the two burning embers there until the heart is pierced from the other side, and then pull out the cautery, and thus there will be four. And if you wish, cauterize with three embers throughout the entire cautery.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After treatment when gangrene has been expelled after a long time, this is better than any of the other treatments mentioned earlier.
de ydropisie	Dropsey
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautery is not useful for dropsy except in the manner called "ascites".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the methods we have mentioned in divisions, and your treatment does not help at all, then you must perform four cauteries around the belly, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the navel, two behind the back over the spine, and one near the breast; and let the cauteries be close to the heart's surface.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Afterwards leave the cautery open for expelling putrefaction over a long time, and do not neglect the treatment of the patient after the cautery; and healing will hasten, and both intentions will be together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the belly is like the key that we have shown before; and those for the back are olive-shaped, according to what has been shown above.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in someone with dropsy and filled with yellow water, you must cauterize on the back of the foot between the little toe and the ring toe; lift your hand along with the cautery without turning it.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not go too deep into the flesh, lest the yellow water escape, and let the cautery be according to this shape:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	Afterwards make two cauteries on each leg at the point of the shin bone; and let one cautery be below the knee in front and the other behind it on the back of the leg; and leave the cauteries on for a long time without dressing until the water comes out, afterwards cleanse with the other cures that we have said.
de la menoison	of the dismemberment
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the humor of the belly comes from coldness and moisture so that the retaining virtue and digestion which is in the stomach and intestines is weakened, and cannot be cured by methods of cures; and you see the sick person well suffering and of strong virtue, then make one great cautery on the stomach according to what has been said before about the cautery of the stomach, around the navel cautery; and four cauteries around the mouth subtly at each one cautery clavicle subtilly, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the humors abundant and the sick person suffering, make a cautery on the point of the hip, and one cautery on each side, and two small cauteries on the stomach near the great one, for the cure is beneficial when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are at the fundament, one or several, and are old and large cold and moist corrupted humors, and they are treated as we have said in sections, but there is no benefit from it, then apply cauteries: three on the spine of the back, that which is directly below the neck, poked bit by bit in a triangular shape; two under the buttocks; and if you think that his stomach is cold, and the flesh does not cook, and one sees the face swell up, then put one large cautery on the stomach as it is said before, and another on the liver, and another on the navel at the center of all the cauteries; leave the cautery on for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treating, cleanse the wound until it is healthy.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshy growth called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut a vein, heat the cautery that resembles a razor, and then place it burning on the cut vein. Leave your hand there until the cautery reaches the base of the vein where blood flows. Do this once or twice. If there is much flesh, cauterize each one as we have said. Afterwards, treat with ointments until they are clean. And if you cauterize a large vein with a hot cautery, it will have greater benefit.
de plaie mal curee	From poorly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	If the patient cannot tolerate incision or opening, which we will discuss later, then this disease comes about which cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a fistula comes to someone and it is inflamed and gives off corrupt moisture and corruption, then you should probe it with a subtle tent, and ensure that you know the entire length of the tent.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heating the cautery that resembles a razor, insert it into the fistula according to how much it has entered. Then resume cauterizing until the corrupted flesh is burned once, twice or three times, depending on what is needed; and beware of burning the nerves that are near, and the large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder or the intestines, be careful of these places, and only perform cauterization on solid flesh, thinking that it is not permeable. Afterwards, treat the area until it is clean. If the area is scarred and the matter has been removed for a long time, know that the area is entirely healed. But if the matter has not been removed, know that the area is damaged, and the bone at the front is rotting. And thus one of these things that we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	About kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	If pain and coldness come upon the kidneys accompanied by great windiness, and there is no menstrual flow in women, then you should perform cautery on the kidneys on both sides with the cautionary iron that we have mentioned earlier. If we cauterize it in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a line, which will provide greater relief.
de la vessie	About the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak due to coldness and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then perform cauterization on the part situated above the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, with one cautery on the right side and one on the left, each cautery being as long as a wheat grain; and perform one cautery behind the back or two if necessary; and make the cauteries pointed according to the shape mentioned earlier.
de la marris	of anger
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the womb is cold and moist, preventing conception and causing corrupted flowers with delayed menstruation, accompanied by pain during menstruation: then perform three cauteries around the vulva as we have said in relation to the bladder cautery, and two cauteries behind the back; make the cauteries pointed as mentioned earlier.
de la hainche	of the beard
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When moist viscous humors descend to the beard's bag, causing its displacement and resulting in one thigh appearing longer than the other upon measurement, with the separation point being discovered: then cauterize the patient above the beard's bag using one cautery resembling a circle, enclosing the bag before reaching the displacement, so that the bag is within the circle; make the cautery such as those used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauteries are not available, then perform three large olive-shaped cauteries, making each cautery as deep as the rest of the heart cauteries; and continue treatment until it is healthy again.
de la dolor de la hainche	of beard pain[TOOL_CALLS]Quant li cuide a la boiste de la hainche, adonques covient que tu face .ij. cauteres parfont et longs, l’un sus l’autre, au dessoubs del leu dou departement del coude, et les autres .iij. cauteres entre les .ii. premiers ou se tu les as faiz; et soient li cauteres tels com cil dont on cauterizeit la boiste de la hainche.
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain occurs in the small of the back, and it is due to coldness and moisture, and the patient has been treated for this condition as we have described earlier but the treatment is ineffective, and the ailment is chronic: then you must purge the patient of thick humors using foul-smelling pills or similar good pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	Afterwards he performs cautery; and the manner of cautery is according to two ways: namely, together hot medicaments, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is according to many ways, of which one way is such that you cauterize upon the boil of the haunch three triangular cauteries according to this form, and make them deep and broad, and let there be between each cautery the width of two fingers, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; sometimes one cautery is made in the middle upon the top of the haunch, whereby there are four cauteries according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	"And if you see it, then cauterize with the cautery of the circle that we have mentioned before in the dislocation of the hip joint; but do it in such a way that the circles contain all the hip joint, and all the edges of the heart are burnt."
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And that is the manner in which it is done for sciatica, when the pain holds only to the haunch and does not reach the thigh nor the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes to the thigh and the leg, make two cauteries where the patient says the pain holds, and one cautery above the ankle four fingers' breadth on the left side; let the cauteries be cutellar-shaped, and burn the thickness of a heartstring; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two toes or near them, cauterize there three points or four at the point called "poins".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	"And if necessary, do more; and if the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, make a cutellar or circular cautery, but be very careful in all your cauteries that you do not burn too deeply and injure the nerves and large arteries, and do not cause the patient excessive harm and contraction."
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who made a fire cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they left it so long that the leg became entirely swollen, and the foot also, and it was pierced and corrupted all over.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After an abdominal inflammation which caused death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in both parts together, make a cautery on one and the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise men say concerning the cautery of the groin, here is the manner: make it such that it is made of iron and its head is as thick as a hazelnut or slightly less, and it is perforated and let there be spaces between the holes equal to the thickness of a barleycorn; and let the holes be evenly distributed on both sides and shaped like nuts; and let there be one handle well-made of iron. This is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated until it is entirely red and brightly glowing, then place it on the boil of the sick person, turned toward its healthy side; and cauterize once with one cautery, leaving it for three days; then make an embrocation of butter, allowing the wound to remain open for a long time; afterwards treat with ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasis says that few of these cauteries are used due to fear of their appearance, and yet we see few who use them. Nevertheless they are good cauteries, those who can bear them.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cauteries of medicine are made thus: make an instrument with holes in which the edges of the door descend, and it should be long on one side and made of brass or iron, and at the top there should be two nuts separated by the thickness of a finger; and let them be open at the front and above, and they should join together according to this form.
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After place the box of hot coals on the patient lying on his sound side; then press your hand strongly on the box of hot coals; afterwards throw between the two circles of the hot coal which has been heated in the fire one handful, and let it sit for an hour's time, and suffer the patient the heat and burning of it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For he will find biting like fire there; and when the biting has passed, lift your hand with the instrument and remove the hot coal of sweet hay, leaving it thus for three days, and put on butter until that which is black from the burn is removed; and let it lie for three more days so that corruption draws out; and this would be the final aid after the treatment of ointments until it is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread to the thigh or to the leg, make one instrument that takes hay according to what you have done in the hot coal, and this is the manner of the hot coal, and I have written it in the treatise on the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take quicklime and live chalk, an equal amount of each, grind them together, and place them in a nine-day pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	so that there is a small hole at the bottom so that the point of a razor can enter; and place another well-sealed pot on top of this pot, and put sweet almond oil on top of the quicklime and chalk until you have enough to comfortably hold it in your hand; then leave it like this until water and steam condense and drip into the lead pot below. Then take all that has collected, and apply it to chalk and quicklime as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be very hot and useful in many medical operations and cauteries for other limbs. For it works like fire, and there are other medicines with which one can cauterize the hair well, such as pitch, honey of anacardium, chalk with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a cure where a man was cured of the pain in his hip and sciatic vein, and greatly praised it, saying that no other treatment was used, and he was immediately healed upon this treatment being performed, as he bathes himself as instructed hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says in this manner: You shall take fresh and dry green copper ore, grind it much with a mortar of fat, place it on the hip, thigh, and leg where the pain resides, cover it; leave it for three hours until the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	Then have him enter a bath until his body is slightly warmed, and then have him lie in bed, and all the pain will leave and he shall be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use such medicines as cautery unless after evacuation of flesh.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat dung, it helps much; and the cautery should be done in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and soak it in old oil, then place it on the hollow between the big toe of the foot and the one called 'foscile'.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	Afterward, take dry goat dung and burn it until it becomes charcoal. Put it on the linen and let it heat until it's extinguished; repeat this process again until you believe by sensation that the heat reaches the hip area and the pain stops. This method of cautery is called 'cautere de chievre'.
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from falling or from an impact, or from excessive evacuation, or from the appearance of dispersed cold matter, in none of these cases is cautery useful except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary that after the patient has been emptied of fetid pills or other such things, one makes on his back, where the pain holds, three lines marked with ink, each line containing five cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can bear; and let the cautery be made according to the cautery called "point"; and if you see, make three or four cauteries at the middle clavicle bone according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often occurs in young children, and its beginning is indicated by their having difficulty breathing when they rise up, and fear. And you find behind the spine of the back and on our appearance that which comes upon the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and wish to treat it, cauterize with the cautery of the backbone according to this form:
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery evenly scorches each part of the spine.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see fit, scorch around the spine with the cautery point twice or thrice, and let the points be close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	Then heal the wound until it is clean according to what we have said, and beware not to apply cautery in any gibbosity near a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	Of joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pains are caused by moistures that have spread to each limb of the body, and when pain comes in the foot, which doctors properly call "podagra," and when it is from a cold cause and cannot be cured with medicines, then it can be cured by cautery in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary that you press upon the face of the foot, make cautery with all the cautery called 'point'.
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains reach down to the knees and other joints, which happens often, make cautery with three cauteries or four on each knee, with every olive-shaped cautery; and if you need more, then do more, but hold your hand back so that the point of the heart's blade is not burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and the back, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make two puncture marks around the wrist; and if there remains any pain on the arms, then make punctures on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains reach to the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good care to the patient and take medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you administer good care and purge phlegm, it shall be healed with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	"about the dislocation of the hip socket"
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When gout comes to the ankles, and the bulls descend to the joints newly, it is necessary that when you see him curing, he should not chew anything that day; and let him use things that leave the belly so that the feces descend from his belly. Afterwards make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his tail until the eyes are repaired, then bind it with your two hands, and press firmly under the gout near the bone of the wrist, and there is a sign like half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery which is here:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	Until it is white and casts shadows.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the bowels to their place; and the minister keep his hand upon them so they do not slip back; and open the patient's thighs well, and put one cushion beneath him and another behind his knees, and a third behind his back where you will hold his hands; then place the cautery on the sign of Leo with your right hand, until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, try again until you do; and be careful that the bowel does not slip out when you apply the cautery; so as not to burn it; and ensure that by doing this the patient does not die or suffer another harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that if you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your efforts are worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And the cauterization of children should be subtle according to their size, and for adults it should also be large according to theirs; afterwards three days after the cauterization, apply butter until the blister is removed; afterwards apply other ointments until it heals, and let the patient lie on their back for forty days until the wound is well healed; and their bandages should remain on for a long time so that the eyes do not jump out when they try to get up from bed.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when they want to get up, let them provide a well-made bandage and keep it on for another forty days. And they should rest well, so that they do not work too much, guard against excessive drinking and eating, and from raising their voice too high; and if they follow this instruction, they will be entirely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	I will now tell you the treatment for cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	Chapter on Laparotomy
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow any further, cauterize it with the cautery according to its quantity, and burn one-third of the heart; afterwards heal it according to what we have said; and some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized at three angles in this form.
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the spot of entrance and draw a line across its width above the rupture, and another below it, and hold your hand firmly throughout the entire operation.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cautery is lighter and gentler.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	Of old pain in some limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any limb, either from falling or striking, and that pain lasts a long time, and remedies of medicine are not effective, then it must be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and the cautery should be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and strength and location of torsions and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If the patient is without wound from the first cautery, that is good; but if not, begin another cautery on top of it, for such is the custom that the member nearby must change, therefore you must perform cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	"Of dislocations"
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	Warts are helped sometimes by cautery with great benefit, especially those that come from the corruption of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	When you wish to cauterize the eye, beware if the disease is at its beginning, and if it has been cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not spread or remain, and you doubt that corruption may spread throughout the whole patient. Then make five cauteries on the head: one between the eyebrows, another towards the forehead at the end of the eyebrows; two on both horns, and one behind on the nape of the neck; and let your hand rest until the cautery reaches the bone, and until the skin blisters come out so that the vapors of thick humors can escape from them. And cauterize it on the face according to what is before [you].
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	"And if the dislocation is spread everywhere and it is clearly apparent, then you should cauterize it with these cauteries that we have mentioned on top: one at the nape of the neck, and two on the spine of the neck, and six on the spine of the back, and one large one on the hip and another near it, and two on the shoulders; and two on the ribs, and two on the tendons of the breast, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful not to burn the nerves that are behind the heel; and sometimes one cautery is made on the bone of the wrist, and one on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver."
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more cauteries you perform, the greater help you give, and the more benefit they [the patient] receive; and know that the sick person does not feel pain from the cautery as a healthy person would, because the body is already entirely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauteries be large and small according to the limbs and joints, as you will find them described in the methods of using irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treatment, apply a poultice made from wheat flour with honey, along with other remedies until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling occurs in any limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and poultices but is not healed, then apply cauteries to the limb according to its size; let the cautery be a little deep into the flesh where the heart is located; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes cauteries are applied to the hand and foot and back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the limb, and similarly if the swelling has been removed; and nonetheless no one should meddle with it unless they are knowledgeable about limbs and the exits of moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	Of Albarras
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the illness called "albaras" is advanced and remedies of medicine are ineffective, then cauterize with a cautery that penetrates somewhat deeply, according to the quantity of the space of the heart until the swelling is removed and its color is changed; then treat with flour of vetches and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of a pigeon and blood of an owl, each one part; and mix it all together, and tie it up in a cloth, and apply it to the place until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	For the cure of chancre by cautery:
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a boil begins to form, and you see it stop, then cauterize it with the fire cautery at its base, all around the boil.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	Moreover, wise men say that one should also cauterize the middle of the boil. However, this does not seem good to me, for I fear that it may be ulcerated and corrupted, as has happened before. It is more proper that it should be cauterized around, with the cautery called "circule," as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of swelling that cannot subside
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has an illness called "adubelati" and it is slow to heal either because of the excessiveness of its discharge or because of the frailty of the patient due to old age, or because of thick blood, or because of time; and you see that it is hastening towards death: then cauterize around it with many small cauteries, prickingly; afterward leave it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she rushes to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	"And if you wish to pierce it entirely with the cautery, heat the cautery which is described here:"
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand on the center of that disease called "adubelati" until the cautery pierces through to the heart; let the cautery be such that the patient feels its power in this way, so that the course of the putrefaction is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	"The cure by fire with iron"
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another manner of disease exists which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than an eating away of limbs, for it consumes the members as fire consumes dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a place that can tolerate fire cautery, then heat the cauteries, both small and large, according to what is needed for the location where the disease is; afterwards, cauterize it on all sides until you remove all corruption, and let nothing remain of it, so that everything that is corrupted is taken away.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and put on the cauterized places a poultice made with oil until the burns of the fire are healed, and all corruption is gone.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After treating with ointments that generate heat.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if after three days you see no healthy flesh growing, then it is good. But if not, then recommence the cautery on that which has remained from corrupted flesh.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this wound has sometimes been cured with hot medicine in place of fire cautery. However, fire cautery is more helpful, and I have already mentioned the cure for hot medicine in its section: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	"of swellings that come on the feet"
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often, at the feet there arises a disease called "clos" in our understanding, which is a large, broken thing that wounds the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauteries for this disease are according to two methods.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is when you heat a cautery iron like a vault-pen, made of good iron to the size that it can surround the nail on all sides with subtle edges. Then place it hot on the nail and turn your hand all around the nail until you reach the top of the nail. Leave it there for three days until it begins to emit pus. Then make an poultice of wild mallow leaves crushed with oil, and leave the poultice on all night, and the nail will fall out and be removed from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cleanse the location of ointment until it is free from flesh.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted away from the body, and this happens many times in hands and feet, then you must bring cautery of hot water to it; and this is done in such manner: take a pipe of brass or iron, or a quill of goose feather, and place it on the nail and its base, which means warts; and place the pipe around so that it encompasses everything entirely, then pour some hot water into it, and hold your hand steady, and press your hand in turning so that the edge of the pipe comes to the root of the nail, and can find a deep path for the hot water to reach the root; and let the patient endure the biting of the hot water for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will deroot itself entirely with all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus does one after another, until you remove all those which are on the body, then treat them with herbs that produce flesh.
li cure dou trembler	And the treatment for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone is trembling from coldness of the nerves, or from quartan fever or other fever, then you should make for them four cauteries or five on the spine of the back, one between each spine; and one on the foot, and one on the stomach at the olive-shaped cautery; this will stop the trembling, and the health of the body will be restored from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	And of stinking pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Never do boils or foul pustules appear on the body which come from corrupt, thick matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	Therefore, when they first appear, one must perform a cauterization on each head of the boil with a fine cautery made from myrtle wood or long-rooted Aristolochia, heated in fire, or with a lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And they are sometimes cauterized at the beginning when they appear in this manner, and they cannot grow further from then on but the excess matter whence they come is removed, and they become clean. However, this should be done after evacuating blood.
quant li artere est copee	When an artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great flows of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the outside, or at the incision of the boil, or at the cautery of the member, and in similar things; and it is very difficult to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And moreover when this happens to anyone, one should quickly place their two index fingers on the wound's opening and press very hard until the blood is pacified beneath your fingers and no more drops come out; then put on the fire olive oil cauteries of various sizes both large and small until they are all red hot; then take either a large or small cautery according to the wound and the place where the artery runs, and place the cautery upon that vein where you hold your fingers, holding it there until the bleeding stops.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if blood suddenly flows forth when you lift your fingers from the wound and the cautery has expired, quickly take another one of the cauteries that are on the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease doing this one after another until the bleeding is stopped. And take care that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes upon the sick person. And know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be well stopped except by one of the four ways that we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction if it is not too large, or by tightly binding a thread, or by medicines applied that have power to stop bleeding; and let it be bound and pressed appropriately.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever brings about stopping by tying very tightly with cloths or putting hot things upon it, or similar things, it profits little if at all.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and he has neither surgeon nor medicine present, one should place their index finger on the wound's opening as we have said, and press very hard until it is stopped above the wound and the vein; and do not move your finger, but moisten it with cold water often and make it very cold until the blood is congealed and thickened and stopped. And then do what is necessary with cauteries and medicines afterward.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of the remedies for wounds
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	In the first chapter we have told you about every disease in which it is necessary to cauterize with fire or hot medicine, and the causes and instruments and forms of cauteries; and I have placed that chapter at the beginning for ease of finding what one wants. And now I will go along the same path in this chapter so that one may find more easily what they desire.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And before I begin this chapter, dear friend, you should know that in this one there is more danger and fear than in the first about cauteries, and therefore greater caution is necessary.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the practice of this chapter there are many times evacuations of blood when opening wounds and making incisions on boils and treating wounds, and extracting splinters and making incisions on stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many people die thereby.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I advise you not to do anything foolish.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come seeking treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	Among them are those who cherish their illness so much that they die easily due to the foolishness they find in their sickness and the severity of their madness. One should fear these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And among these there are those who give it meaning and say: 'wait, I am cured'; but the disease is treacherous.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not necessary that you consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put greater caution in your honor than in your greed, and do not open foolishly but wisely those from whom you are certain, and from whom you can gain praise and fame; and use prognosis and diagnosis in treating your patients so that health may be restored; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear beloved son, May Our Lord grant you good understanding and uprightness, and if He wishes to inspire you with His holy breath, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	"Or I have arranged this chapter in sections, dividing it into chapters according to what is before the chapter on cauteries that I have already divided from head to toe, so that you may find more easily those things of which you will have need."
dou chief plein d’aigue	"head full of water"
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	**Know that this ailment often comes to children at birth, and when the mother squeezes too hard on the child's head; sometimes it happens due to an unknown cause.**
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	**And I have never seen this ailment happen outside of children, and for all those that I have seen, the jaw is dislocated; therefore it seems to me that it would be best if I left aside the rest of my work in such cases.**
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	**And I saw one child whose head was full of water, and each day it swelled so much that he could hardly bear it; and the swelling increased so much that it reached the mouth, and this swelling is collected beneath the bone above the spleen, between the heart and the bone; and if the swelling is between the heart and the bone, and the tumors are small, you should make a cut in the head that is wide, and as long as two fingers, wherever the swelling reaches. Here is the shape of the spatula:**
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	**If the swelling is greater, and the tumors are larger, then make two cuts in the shape of a cross, like this:**
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	**And if the swelling is beneath the bone, and you see that the angles of the head are raised on each side, and water gushes out when you press it with your hand inside, but there is no response: then you must make three cuts in the head in this manner:**
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all the moisture outside.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After applying compresses and powders, put wine and oil on it, and leave it like that until the fifth day; then untie it, and dress the wound with bandages and ointments, and let the limb rest evenly, and give the patient dry food with little moisture until the member is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	**And another way of incision is to look where the greatest part of the tumor opens and where the water is collected; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.**
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	**Therefore cut where the tumor opens and where the water is collected, and make the incision according to what you can do; but beware that you do not cut the artery; for if a vein bleeds profusely, then the patient will die from loss of blood and evacuation of swelling.**
de reume	**de reume**
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When one has a disease called "catarra" in the eyes or the foot, and the disease is chronic, and medical treatment does not help at all, then the final remedy is fire cauteries with the application of two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary, therefore, when you cover the eyes that the patient turn their head back; afterward rub the place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then have the patient hold their neck with the cloth; next observe where the vein was and the places of both are after the ears, and they are ready to be opened; then mark the places with hot cautery, then cut both with a sharp spatula in two parts so that the cut vein reaches the bone, and this should be done near the wide part of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, place the spatula under the artery and cut above it, cutting about two fingers' width across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	Once the vein is severed, blood flows out continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the arteries do not appear upon feeling, then you must measure the quantity of space of three fingers, then mark with hot cautery and cut until the bone; and as much blood as should be let out is six ounces, but sometimes a little more or less according to what the patient can bear and the fullness of the artery. Then examine the wound: if there remains on the bone point of the syphac, then cut it so that no abscess may come, then press the wound and bind it, and apply ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	de emigrainne
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient migraine comes on, and catarrh is present due to the moistness of tears and heat in the temples, causing ancient madness and similar symptoms, even when treated with various remedies, if no improvement is seen, then extract the arteries from the temples using cauterization, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The manner of extracting them is that the patient should shave the hair from their temples and locate the artery which opens into the temple, for it is quite visible due to its pulsating motion, although in some people who are very cold it may be less apparent. If it is not apparent, the patient should wrap a cloth around the neck to restrict blood flow, then rub the area with a coarse cloth and wash it with warm water until the artery becomes clearly visible. Then take the spatula shaped as follows:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then lightly scrape the skin until you reach the artery, then grasp it with pincers and carefully cut away the surrounding tissues from each part; and if the artery is thin, twist it with the point of a nail file, then cut off that part according to the amount of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	But if it is not cut, the blood will not flow entirely out.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw six drops of blood until three; and if the artery is large, then you should tie it in two places with a strong silk thread so that corruption does not come before the wound heals, and let blood flow freely; then cut away the excess flesh between the two ties at this same hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize with a cutting cautery until the bone is reached; and this is the main work, if the patient has no fever and is of warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery aids in finishing moisture: therefore it is of greater aid against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where, for the extraction of arteries, one should fill the place with old cotton and put on well-made dressings; and when they are removed, cure them with dry medicines that cause flesh to grow, and dressings, until it is healed. And if blood flows from the artery as many times as you work there, hasten to cauterize with a copper cautery, or fill the place with vitriol and hold your hand steady until the blood is stanched; and if this is not present, put your fist on the place until the blood congeals, and wash the place with cold water until the blood stops, and press it as it should be. And that which is quicker and lighter in extracting an artery is to cauterize the vein with a cutting cautery of two parts, but let the cuts be well spaced to retain heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	But when the instruments are too thin, they hold less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be a space of one finger's width between the two knives, and then when you have marked both places with incisions, and you measure with the heated iron until it reaches the bone, cut the vein at both places; and they should be distant between the two incisions for this cautery is not continuous throughout. And this is the shape of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are descending from the veins that are above the forehead of the head, and it does not help to apply medicine there, and you see the face becoming redder, and feel on the forehead a trembling as if from shivering; and if the eyelids are thin and moist so that the hairs of the eyelashes have fallen out, and the eyelashes are heated and scraped by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called this wound in old times "a bruise", and it is to be treated thus: make three incisions on the forehead of the patient who has this illness, evenly spaced according to the length of the forehead; one incision should be as long as two fingers, running downwards from just above the eyebrows to the nose, and the other two should be placed on either side of the temples, above the eyebrows, being careful not to cut the arteries located on either side of the temples; keep your hand away from the line connecting the two jaws, and each wound should be the width of three fingers joined together; then prepare a sponge and many cloths for wiping away blood, and use the spatula shaped thus:
