des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	And scrape away all the skin that is between the two incisions down to the temple bone, then remove this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Then insert into the first incision an instrument called a "cultellarium," which is very sharp on one side and smooth on the other without being sharp; this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the sharp side of the knife towards the flesh near the heart, and the blunt side towards the bone, and press until it reaches the middle furrow.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous up to those that open near the heart, and then repeat on the other side; then draw out the blood evenly, and press the wound to stop bleeding; then place in each furrow a bandage of old cotton, and cover with cloths moistened in wine and oil and hyssop, and ensure no abscesses form; and on the third day remove the bandages, and apply abundant water from tansy plants, then treat with basilicon ointment mixed with rose oil, and other treatments for wounds until healed.
dou reume des eulz	Of the treatment of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	If catarrh often comes upon you, and you see the eyelids thin and small, and your vision is weakened, and the eyelashes are burned; and the hairs fall out, and deep pain in the head, and the patient sneezes; then know by these symptoms that this matter and this catarrh come from many veins, and the cure for it is this:
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is necessary that you instruct the patient to lie on their back, then make a deep incision in the middle of the forehead, and another one wide at the temple.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	Beginning from the left temple's crease to the right temple, let the incision reach the bone; keep your hand away from the temple nerves that move during chewing; once the bone is exposed, absorb all the blood with a sponge, then open the wound's two lips and insert old cotton and linen strips. Next, bind it with cloths moistened in wine and oil, ensuring no hot abscess forms. After removal, rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat it with drying agents.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony, mix them together, and apply this plaster to these wounds to stimulate the growth of flesh everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Here is an illustration of the instrument described in the text:
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of four things:
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	If something like a stone falls into the ear or otherwise enters but does not fit and does not grow within the ear, then place the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then distill some drops of violet oil or sesame oil into it, then attempt extraction. When doing so, make them sneeze with condisium, and plug their nostrils when they sneeze, and place cloth or wool pieces around the ear; stretch the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often fire comes from this treatment; if it does not come by itself, bring about extraction with delicate pincers, of which here is the method:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it does not come out with forceps, that is good; if not, bring about extraction with a fine needle of small thickness. And if it does not come out that way, make a cane of straw and put the head of the cane into the hole of the ear strongly, and stop up what is around the cane with soft wax so that wind cannot enter with the cane; then draw fire very vigorously, for often fire comes in this manner as we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, take glutinous substance which birds use, and put some on an instrument which is sharp for this purpose, and put a little cotton around; then press the glut on the stone or whatever thing it may be, and draw fire.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out from all these things that we have said, then hurry to cut the ear before aposteme comes and spasm. And the manner of cutting is this: first let the sick person be bled from the cephalic vein according to his strength, then make the sick person sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small crescent-shaped cut in the root of the ear where it depends; then pull out the stone according to your power, and suck it quickly into your mouth. And continue the treatment until he is cured.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grains that are inside and the ear becomes swollen, bring about extraction accordingly. And if it cannot come out, bring about extraction with a thin, subtle spatula according to this shape:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	And make an incision into that boil.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this if you think the boil is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many incisions; then extract it with delicate pincers and tweezers, as we have said, so that the extraction is complete.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	Therefore, in the water that falls into the ear, the patient must use sternutation with conditions first, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie on his/her same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it then breaks out through this boil, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, then take many needles according to the length of your thin and light fingers, heat them slightly in fire; and let the patient insert one or two of these needles into his/her ear hole, allowing another end to stick out on the other side, and strike with another needle on the needle that is in the ear; do not stop doing this until all the water flows out, and thus it will all flow out; if you see, then take a piece of juncus grass, insert one end into the ear and hold the other end near fire until the end of the juncus grass is burned; then repeat this with other pieces of juncus grass until all the water flows out, as we have said about the needle.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of an animal, if it is small-bodied, such as a flea or something similar, treat it as we have said in the division. But if it is large-bodied so that you can feel it, bring about extraction with forceps; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of earthworms in ears, when you treat them as we have said in the division and in treating distillations, and if the treatment does not help, it is necessary to examine the ear in sunlight: if any worms are visible, extract them with fine forceps; but if they cannot be seen, take the pipe of which this form is here:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	Place the most subtle head of the funnel into the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then suck strongly until all the veins empty; do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey coming out, then plug around the funnel with cotton as I have said in the stone; and if they do not come out as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the expulsion of worms, and you will find them in the chapter on distillations; and distill your oils and medicines into the ear through this instrument, of which here is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it should be of silver or bronze narrow below with a small hole, and above open for distillation; and for pressing within the distillation, one well-made brass instrument for this purpose, and if you wish take one razor and wrap cotton around its point neatly; then pour your oil or juice, and what you wish of your medicines into the tube, and the tube should be in the ear; then place within the razor with all the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled cleanly from the ear; and let the patient feel it within, and let the distillation be one small heated vessel on the fire beforehand when it is distilled into the ear; and guard that it not be too cold, for the medicine will not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Here is an illustration of the instrument described in the text:
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a hole in their ears; the same thing happens to adults due to injury of the ear or flesh growing inside it, and these blockages sometimes occur deep within the ear so that one cannot see them; sometimes there is only partial obstruction of the hole.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, when it occurs deep within the ear so that one cannot see it, it is difficult to treat in many ways. But in cases where you can see the obstruction, you should place the patient's ear in the sun and look inside: if you see the dark spot clearly, then perform the operation described below:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and cutting before and behind entirely full, so that it does not wound the ear; if the obstruction is of flesh born in the body of the ear, hold it with fine pincers, and cut it lightly, until all that flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the wax is deeply embedded in the ear, then take a fine razor blade and heat it slightly over the fire, then place it on the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the wax which the patient feels great pain in hearing, pierce it lightly, and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear; then put in the ear a wick according to the width of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for several days until the wound is healed, or else take a tampon and moisten it with rosewater, and sprinkle powdered vitriol upon it. And if you see that the ear is swollen, then it is necessary to remove the tampon and replace it with another one moistened in cerote which is made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling has subsided; then cleanse it until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if there is a discharge of blood coming out, then plunge a sponge wrapped in cold water and place it on the ear, and use other remedies that stop the flow of blood which are found in treatises on distillations.
de la char des papieres	Of the flesh of pears
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the remedy that comes from the flesh of pears when they are moist and then become dry: you should stretch them with forceps and pincers, and cut it with a scalpel at its roots; then sprinkle powdered vitriol on it.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if they continue to grow without being cut down, then cauterize them with a lenticular cautery instrument, and the cauterizing afterwards cuts off more of their roots. And often they need to be retreated several times because some thing remains from their roots; but when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not grow back again.
de la gresle	Of hailstones
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times, papers come from the eyes containing things that appear like hail in shape and hardness, and therefore this illness is called "hail," being a gathering of thick moisture on the paper above and below; the treatment is such: be careful if the hail moves from one side to another, which is easy to know; then make an incision wide enough, then scrape off each part lightly, then take it with tweezers, and cut it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	But if you cannot cut it without piercing the paper somewhat, it does not harm the patient; and if the split is large, then join it with a suture, and treat it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not use force, for the eyelids will soon restore themselves and close over it.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hail is descending into the ear towards the upper part, then turn the skin and stretch it with pincers and cut out the hail, pressing on both sides. If the skin is stretched by the incision, do not worry about it; but once the hail has been cut out, rinse the wound with salt water, and treat it with ointment that brings new flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	Of the fat of the ears
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that infiltrates into the tissues of the eyelids above, and this happens more often in children than adults, causing great pain to their eyes, and they have cataracts in the mornings, and cannot look at sunlight because tears quickly gather in their eyes; and therefore they lie on their backs all the time, sleeping like that, with their eyelids moist beneath their eyebrows, and the swelling and appearance are covered by exinach that opens into the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press there with your two hands and feel it come out.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of treatment is as follows: the patient should put their head in your hand. Then take one linen cloth and prepare it like a circle according to the quantity that contains the eczema on each part. Then place it over them and press with your fingers on both sides so that the eczema collects within the circle. Then make an incision in the middle of the moisture with a scalpel, making it no larger than the wound made for bleeding. And cut deep into the skin until you reach the eczema. And in several positions, eczema will come out of the incision, resembling a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then extract all at once with a piece of cloth between your fingers, squeezing it back and forth from left to right until it is dispersed. And be careful not to squeeze too hard against the incision so that you do not draw out the scalpel or cause bleeding.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	"And if the exit does not open at the beginning of the slit, then slightly widen the slit lightly until it opens; then extract as we have said, then soak cloths in warm water and vinegar, and place them on the wound, and bind with bandages."
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are such men who grind salt and place it on top to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal until they are healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot boil comes to the place, then treat it with soothing plaster until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	"of the hairs of papers"
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	"When hairs grow on papers besides their natural ones and are entwined, they harm the eyes and cause diseases like habitual tears and softening of the papers and opacity, to such an extent that it causes destruction of the eyes; and there are four ways to treat it: either by cauterization with fire together, or by hot medicine according to what is written in the cautery chapter, and it is done either by incision and suturing or by caustics, depending on what I will say."
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	"It is necessary that you place the head of the sick person in your lap, then turn the paper away from the eye with your left hand; if it turns, it's good; if not, insert a needle at one thread above it; and whether it is near the edge of the paper or where the hairs are growing next to these hairs, and draw one thread up along the entire paper, and turn it towards the razor; then cut into the part below the paper, below the attached hairs, with all the spatula coping, from the large larmier to the small; then extract one thread, and place a small tent of cotton and cloth under the paper, then press on the paper with an incense burner, like a mirror glass, and in any case, the figure should be according to the quantity that you see raising the paper that is divided into two."
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is need to cut off a large quantity of paper according to how moist the paper is; then cut along the two lines that you have marked out, starting from the large opening down to the small; and let one of the cuts be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert one of the points into one of the corners of the heart, then peel off all the skin; then sew up the two lips with a needle and a thin thread of silk, and wipe away the blood, and tie up the excess threads on both eyebrows with any sticky substance you see fit to use; if not, do not worry about it, then leave the stitches and threads for three or four days; then treat the wound without stitching with drying and constricting substances, for the paper relieves the joining of the wound and its assembly, but stitches are harmful (as the ancients said), and this is work without fear; and there is another way: and it is that you mark the paper with a figure that is like the leaf of a laurel tree, as we have described, with three points opened according to the shape that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	"Then cut what is above the small circles evenly according to the shape that is here:"
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you lack the power to hold the forceps, and the matter is not even, then take a needle with thread, and insert it into the figure. And insert another thread near the large bell, and the second thread near the small one, and bring them together evenly between your two fingers; then raise your hand evenly, and lift all the skin where you have marked, as we have described, then close the two lips of the wound by stitching, and cure it until it is clean. And if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes it happens that the hairs of the paper are turned: so you must use what we have said about the incision; but the stitches in both are more artful.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The care of the canines is in this form: and it is that you turn the paper and make the cut inside according to what I have said, then make two canines by art, and two thin threads as long as the paper and the width of the spatula; then cut at the two ends of the two parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other finely on top of the paper of the eye, and strain the two canines from the two parts firmly; leave it thus for some days, and the skin that is strained will wrinkle and harden and whiten, until it shrinks by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is delayed, then apply forceps once, then cure until it is clean. And when the wound is healed and the paper lifted off, and the hairs will no longer prick; and this is the shape of the two canines that you should make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The procedure is as follows: Take a fine needle and insert one thread of soft, thin silk; then tie the ends together finely, and let the length of the threads be a palm long. Then prepare another thin silk thread briefly, and tie its end to the threads; then have the patient place his head in your hand, and stand near the sun so that the procedure is clear, for it is a subtle and fine procedure. Then insert the needle all the way into the hairline next to the root of the hair, and pierce it quickly through the paper until you pull it out above the natural hair; then pull the hair up to the chase, and insert that hair, if there is one or two or three or more; then pull your hand back so that all the hairs come out of the chase into the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase has been completed but the hairs do not come out with it, then pull the chase down from underneath all the thread that you have prepared, until the chase comes out of the hole above and you can see it with your eye; then pull the chase and the thread, close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair settles in its place and flesh grows over it. And if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from the natural eyebrows and lift it up with that one, so that it is separated and then lifted up.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the rottenness of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease called "aleacrati" or decay occurs in the eye, it comes in two ways: natural and unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, cut, or cautery, or similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the way to treat it is that you should cut open that scab, separate its lips, and place cotton made of linen inside, until it becomes clean. Do not use things that dry out and constrict in treating it.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease returns worse than before. But there are things that soften it, such as fenugreek; and rosewater or alehoof cooked with linseed, and eye ointments made from diacylon melted in one of the oils should be used for bandaging it.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	The goal of this treatment is to ensure that the wound does not heal in the same shape as it was before. The treatments we have mentioned are only remedies for this disease and not a guarantee that it will not return in its original form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of flesh coming into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is underneath is truly called "axacrati" and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wound and split and cautery and similar things; and the way of working in this is that you take a needle with double thread, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left eyelid towards the right, so that the threads come out in two holes of the flesh; then stretch the flesh above all the needle, and cut with one wide spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what it should be, that is good; but if not, then take one razor and place it in the split, and turn the paper, and make two splits on the inside edges of the paper; and let the holes of the two splits be at the two angles of the incision that you have cut, and make one angle so that when they are assembled, the figure is like the figure of a letter called "I Greek"; then remove that flesh according to the quantity of its sides and below what supports the paper, then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a wool thread; then perform the care that we have said about softening medicines, and dressings, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a cut or stitches or cautery, you should make a full-length incision under the hairs of the paper, following what was said earlier. Then separate the two leaves of a wick between them, as I have described before. The operation must be done according to the shape of the disease, for it is very varied in form. Skilled masters devise various means with all their power to make the figure return to its natural shape. And the sick person himself, according to what is needed in treatment and instruments, may vary his operations in many ways.
dou soudement de la papiere	Regarding the sudden tearing of paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this sudden tearing happens to many people in such a way that the paper above is stuck with the white of the eye, and cannot move nor perform its natural operations, then you must insert the point of a razor under the paper and lift it upwards. Then stretch it with tweezers until you cut what is stuck with a fine spatula that is neither too large nor too sharp, so that the sick person cannot bear if the spatula were too large or scratched the eye. Make your incision light so that the paper returns to its natural shape. Remove all that was stuck and sometimes apply saltwater to the eye, then rinse it with fresh water and collyrium. Then place a linen wick between the paper and the eye, and put wet wool moistened in egg yolk on the eye. After the third day, use collyrium and other warming substances until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Regarding the corner of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the corner of the eye can appear in two ways: one is nervous and resembles a hard, dry skin; the other is not nervous but resembles a moist, congealed blister. When touched with iron or attempted to be grasped with tweezers, it cannot be taken. Both kinds start near the large tear duct and gradually increase until they cover all of the eye's vision and movement.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	The manner of incision is as follows: the patient places their head in your hand, then opens their eyes. You lift the paper with your hand and coil the corner with tweezers of fine double edge, stretching it upwards. Then take a needle and attach one horse hair or cow hair or ox hair to it, along with a strong thread. Double the point of the needle slightly and insert it into the corner, pushing it through entirely. Tie the corner with a thread and stretch it upwards. Remove all of the skin along the side of the corner that covers the pupil and sclera up to the head using a fine spatula and small forceps. Leave the natural tissue in the tear duct so that tears can flow naturally after the incision. Sometimes, the corner is stretched only with tweezers and thread, as mentioned earlier. Then remove it entirely with a soft spatula of this form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And make sure that the spatula does not touch the delicate tissue and tear it, nor should the pupil be pierced. After the incision, sprinkle some crushed mallow on the eye and apply collyrium made from litargirum, leaving it overnight. Then treat as necessary until healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the corner is not nervous and you cannot insert the needle nor can tweezers grasp it, many times this kind of corner is cured with medicines. As I have mentioned in the division, they appear like this, and if you see one that needs to be removed, open the eye of the patient and use a light spatula shaped like this:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the finger gently, and if you see it does not decrease in width and reason presses on it, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collyrium made of litharge and red ochre and crushed salt, and stop up the eye until the next day; then resume the other work according to this same operation, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	But if something opposes you in the eye, such as an inflamed sore, then use milk, and first cure the hot sore until it is healthy; then resume the operation as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of flesh in the eye causes great harm to the eye, then suspend it from a goat's horn and cut off a portion of it, but not all, so that tears do not come forth; then distill into the eye red collyrium made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Eyes of some men are sometimes born with red hair,
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless, it is necessary that you alleviate the cure of each weak eye by natural means; and as for accidental cases, perform surgery with iron; and do not put your hand into any of these operations until you see that these members can endure this operation.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Before veins appear red which cover over the eye, they render sight ineffective and weaken the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is then your task to first examine the eye in which the white of the eye appears, and if there is no other visible disease besides the white; therefore proceed in this manner: instruct the patient to place their head on your lap, then press these veins gently all around according to your skill, and make the lap subtle double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And there shall be two onions placed degree by degree in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then twist these onions subtly with force, and squeeze the blood afterwards one after another until you see those veins move outside of the eye. Be careful not to cut the eye with the points of the tweezers, and perform this task at midday before the sun, and be very careful in your work so that you only affect those veins. Once you have done this, distill green and red vitriol oil into the eye to corrupt what remains of the sebaceous material.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	"And if you are unable to capture all of them at that time,
de la fistule de l’oil	Fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The surgeon calls a fistula of the eye «arissati». When you cure it using cauterization and hot medicine according to what I have said before, but it is not healed, there must be something inside that makes you cut open the boil where it should burst, and drain all the moisture that is there until the bone becomes visible.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone becomes visible and you see corruption and blackness there, then prepare all the instruments of which this is the shape; it is called «aspre chief» (sharp head), and should be made of iron with one blunt end, and should be pointed like a file as it appears in the present shape
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the bone that is corrupted, then twist it between your two fingers and press down a little until you know that all the corruption has been removed. Do this several times, then apply medicinal powders to dry out the wound.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the place is solid, and flesh grows, and the body of the rib remains solid like this for 40 days, and it does not change or become an abscess, and no bad accident occurs, know that it is healthy; but if not, then there is only one option: to bring the fistula back to the opening of the nostril according to this form. And so you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with hot medicines, and when it is uncovered, take a drill according to this form, and make the head of the iron at three angles, and thin out the shaft until its tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the ear, and move your hand away from the eye and cheek, then turn the drill until it pierces the bone, which the patient will feel due to the wind entering there if they hold their hand over their nose. Then restore the wound with dry medicines as I have instructed, and when the flesh grows and hardens the place, then the matter goes to the nose; thus it is easier for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	Regarding the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the eye opens wide all around and nothing disturbs the nose or makes it smaller, then you must bandage the sick person. Then wash them, then place cupping glasses on their head without pricking them to suck out the blood. Then put a poultice made of acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcolac on the eye, then compress the eye and cover it with bandages and cloths. And the manner of the cloths is as follows: take soft cloths and double each one four times, then place them on top of each other according to the amount that the eye needs. Then compress it firmly with a hard bandage from above, and then recommence the cupping glasses without pricking to suck out the blood. Then remove the cupping glasses and leave the eye compressed day and night. And if the poultice melts, you must remove it. Then remove the poultice after the day and night, and if you see that the eye is healing, that is good. But if not, then recommence the compressing and bandages and poultice and cupping glasses until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Regarding the rupture of a blood vessel in the eye
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a rupture occurs in the blood vessel of the eye and it opens and blood comes out like a grain of resin, and it is frightening to see. Then if you see this happen, do as follows: take a needle and insert it into the root of the lower part of the eye up to the upper part. Then take another needle with a doubled thread at the lachrymal gland area and make it pierce there, leaving the first needle in place. Then tie one part of the uve around with the doubled thread and compress it well. Then remove the needle and place wet linen dipped in egg yolk on the eye. Leave it until the blood coagulates with the uve. Then treat the eye with comforting substances until the wound is healed. And sometimes the wound is constrained by the uve on each side with a circle of cloth until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye has a large appearance, then pierce it with a thin spatula that comes out from deep within the eye and remove the moist albugo and let the eye descend, and enter in as quickly as possible. Then remove it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	Regarding the bowing of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This illness called "alcunnati" is nothing but a vein gathered in the eye, resembling descending water, and it is not water. The manner of its appearance during surgery is as follows: have the patient sit on an upright chair prepared for them, then take their head between your hands from both sides, and move it until you see the vein come up to your eyes. Then pierce it with a needle, ensure that it does not descend and block light, and let the patient see things as they usually do; if it does not descend below, know that it is watery matter, and if the descent of the vein is not as we have described, then it is watery matter.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If the patient sits between your hands, then take the fine spatula and make an incision through the connective tissue with the corneal layer and the crown until the boil bursts; and once it has burst, distill hot water mixed with honey or fenugreek boiled in water into the eye, then dress it with another dressing until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	Regarding the waters of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have shown here the likenesses of waters in their divisions, and what should be pierced; thus we work according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from light for the sun, and hold the healthy eye tightly; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or right hand if it's right. Then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, or left hand if it's right, the instrument called "almagda"; then place the tip of the instrument near the crown along the thickness of a grain from that blister of the eye towards the lesser lacrimal part; then gently push the instrument called "almagda" and twist your hand until it pierces into the blister of the eye, and feel when almagda reaches empty space. And the measure of the path of almagda must reach as deep as the measure from the pit of the plum to the end of the blackness; and that is the crown of the eye. Then you will see the bone through that paper due to the clarity of the corneal layer, then place the instrument up to where the water is, then press it below one vein after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If water descends now, then the patient sees before them and the tool in their eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a moment, if the water rises again along the second path, place the funnel with the tool. When it is inserted and it does not rise, gently extract almagdum in a circular motion little by little with your hand. Then add a drop of hot gemstone oil to the eye and remove the eye from the eyelid inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then place over the eye a plug of wax or wet linen in rose oil and egg yolk, and bind it with a sound eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Nowadays, we and those of our time use ground comfrey mixed with egg yolks.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, as there are some men whose eyes are too hard, you must take the tool called "alberit", of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then carefully pierce the conjunctiva only, not too deeply but make it subtle, then insert almagdum as we have said. At the completion of the work prepare for the patient a suitable attendant who causes them to sleep on their back in a dark room; and keep them steady from all movements, let them eat light foods, do not move their head to the right or left, and bind them according to their condition until the third day; then untie them in the same dark room, test their sight, and make them see certain things. Then reapply the binding until the seventh day. Do not perform this during or immediately after the operation but rather earlier so that water does not rise hurriedly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If an abscess appears, then on the seventh day, untie the eye before it, and apply a poultice that softens abscesses; once it has softened, untie the bandage and place over it a compress of lint to cover for some days, and keep it constantly in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	Then little by little leave the house, and return to your usual habits; know that no disciples should interfere in this matter.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And there came to us one from the land of Iraq who told us that in their country they used almagda to pierce, and then suck out the water, but nevertheless I have never seen any such thing in our land nor read about it in the books of the ancients; perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And here are the likenesses of the forms of almagda so that those who do not know them may see them, and they should be made of pure gold:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the heads of these be of this same subtlety, and the rear ones at three sharp angles.
de la char sor le neis	To cauterize flesh on the nostril:
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes various kinds of discolored scars appear, among which some resemble many-legged scorptions; there are also those with flesh colored like fox fur, and others with soft flesh of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	For those soft scars that are not inflamed, seat the patient between your hands facing the sun; open their nostrils and sprinkle them with a drop of incense on those scars, then rub them vigorously; afterwards take what you can hold on the tip of a thin, sharp spatula on one side until you know that all the flesh is scraped off.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there is still something that cannot be scraped away, open it with one of the sharp instruments lightly and completely until nothing remains. And if without pain or heat, cover the wound with cotton, and if it is malignant sores, cauterize them quickly so that the blood stops flowing and all the flesh is removed. Then apply a poultice made of oatmeal and vinegar to the bone.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nose opens and moistures reach the palate, know that it is healthy; but if moistures do not penetrate as they should, know that there is flesh grown into the bone above, to which the instrument cannot reach: thus you must insert a thread of fine linen, about the thickness of your little finger or less, dampened with warm water and spiced with one grain of incense between each knot; let the patient hold the head of the thread in his nostril with moderate force, and draw it through while smelling until it passes into the mouth; many children do this at school, and it is easy for whoever wishes to perform it; then hold the head that emerges from the nostril with one hand, and the other head that emerges from the mouth with the other hand, and pull them apart gently as we have shown you.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the knots have rotted away the flesh, then pull out the thread, cleanse the blood, and moisten it with Egyptian oil; replace it in the nostril as before. Do this for 3 days or more until the oil has corrupted all remaining flesh; then insert a cake of lead into the nostril for several days until it is healed. If there is need for drying medicines, use them accordingly. This is the form of the instrument used to purge the head, with which oils and medicines are distilled into the nostrils.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be made of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp with a tube like a candle wick, and the tube should also have many holes at its tip for purging the nostril; and if you wish to use a closed tube, make sure that the instrument is full of liquid for purging the head. And let it have several small openings at the top so that one can hold it securely while heating the oil or any other liquid.
de la char sor le neis	To cauterize flesh on the nostril:
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" arises at the head's top,
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose is cut and cauterized
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when solution continues to come forth from one of these worked cartilage joints, it is profitable little, save for some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then when this happens to anyone, see if the wound is fresh in all its blood; and then join the two lips together with a suture, then dress it until it is healed; and if the lips are already torn on both sides, then you must scrape away all parts of their core until they are clean, then join the two lips together with a suture, and tie them, and powder over the powders dragon's blood powder, and crushed incense; and place over the powders a piece of strong plaster or other sticking plaster, and leave it on until it falls off by itself, then dress it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of stitching is thus: either by needles, as we have said in the belly stitching; or by thread, as I have taught you.
des apostemes des levres	Chilblains on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many people have hard chilblains on the lips, resembling grains of wheat, small and large. Therefore, you should turn the lips and cut each nodule with scissors and remove it with tweezers by cutting in every part. Then apply powdered vitriol to the incision until the wound is clean. Afterward, wash the area with warm water and dress the wound with dry substances until it heals.
de la char des gencives	Of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, attached flesh appears on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus"; therefore, you should hold it with forceps and cut it at its root, allowing the blood vessel or vein to flow. Then apply powdered vitriol or other restrictive and drying powders to the area. If the flesh returns after the incision, which often happens, cut it again and cauterize it; afterwards, it will not return. These are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	Of boils
