Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes, rough and sharp scabs appear on the gums in the mouth between the teeth, and sometimes the teeth are black, yellow, or worm-eaten, causing corruption to reach the gums and making the teeth smell bad. Therefore, you should have the patient sit with their head in your lap and raise their lips so that nothing remains on the teeth. Do this for blackness, greenishness, yellowness, and other stains until they are cleaned. If what caused it is removed at first, it is good; if not, resume cleaning on the second and third day until everything is clean. Know that teeth require various forms of instruments for cleaning according to what the work shows, as those used to scrape the outside of teeth have different shapes than those used to clean between them. Have all these forms and others ready with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you are treating a toothache, you should delay extracting it as much as possible, for this should never be done. For it is a very high and delicate substance until there is no other option but to remove it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained by toothache, you must be certain of the painful tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain leaves the patient, and they think it is in the healthy tooth, and have the good tooth pulled; but still the pain does not depart for this reason, because the evil one has been removed, for we have often seen this happen to these saints. And when you are certain of the painful tooth, then you must scrape around the tooth with a strong spatula to protect the gum from all sides; then move it with your two fingers or with fine tongs little by little until it is well loosened, then firmly grasp it with the tongs; and keep the patient's head between your knees, and hold yours still so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these tools and gently insert it on each side, and use the lever tool as you have done previously.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is perforated and wobbly, you must fill the hole with lint where it is pierced; and gently hold it with forceps so that it does not break while extracting; and much bleeding will occur around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful that you do not break it, and if any part remains, it will return to the patient with greater pain from the root than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act like ignorant surgeons who through haste and recklessness sometimes break the jawbone, and do not use what we have described here; but often cause great illness in people due to remains of roots or broken jawbone, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the area with wine, vinegar, or salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, fill the wound with powdered vitriol; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments used for extracting teeth first should have long points and thick handles so they do not double over when pulling the tooth. These are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of large members so they do not bend when pulled, and of iron well-made, and toothed for moving them.
de la racine des dens	From the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains at the wound, you must place moistened cotton with butter for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 until the place is softened, then insert the tweezers called "algefri," making it appear like a sparrow's beak; and they should be shaped inside like a file.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with these tongs, then you must uncover the flesh all around the root, and put the tool called "althali", that is to say, pliers, this is its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out with these, good; if not, then help yourself with all the tools, of which the shapes come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this tool with two handles, this is its shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments which are in front of the reason for teeth, and this tool that resembles large tongs, here is its shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these tools be strong so they cannot break; and know that there are many instruments for teeth, and also others which are not counted. And the clever master finds his own instrument according to what his works and sickness show him, because there are such diseases where the old did not teach any instrument due to their diversity. And if one breaks something of the cartilage or other bones, then search among those tools which are necessary, as I have told you, and help yourself with gestures; this is its shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and hold well to hold the bone so it does not escape but can hold and remove it; then restore the place with appropriate medicine, and if there is rot in the bone and it is small, then remove it with all this tool.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When teeth appear not according to the natural body shape and their appearance is ugly, especially in maiden women, it is necessary for you to know if the tooth is next to the tooth and not in the right place, and one cannot be set or smoothed: then cut; and if it is adherent with the tooth, take this tool of which here is its shape, resembling a small beak, and made of iron sharp at the end.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And hit it gently day after day for the hardness of the tooth and so as not to move the others; and if it is apparent that one can smooth it, then use this kind of file, of which here is its shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file with which one makes needles; and file the tooth gently day by day little by little so that it does not fall too much; then smooth it at the end with any rasp; and if the tooth is too sharp and hurts the tongue, then smooth its sharpness until it is even so that it neither hurts the tongue nor impairs speech.
quant li dent lochent	When teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth are loose due to blows or falls, and the patient cannot chew food without choking, even after treating them with constricting medicines without success, you must constrain them with a gold wire. The wire should be neither too thick nor too thin according to the space between the teeth. If you need to align the teeth, take the wire and wrap it double around two healthy teeth. Then place the wires between the loose teeth, one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side. Start again with the wrapping up to where you began, holding your hand steadily so it does not move. Make sure the knot is at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then grasp the heads of the threads with a pair of pliers, and bring them together, and place them between the healthy teeth, so that it does not wound the tongue; then leave it as tight as possible until it can remain in place. If it comes loose or the thread breaks, hold it down with another thread; let it stay thus for its entire time, and this is the shape of the teeth and the arrangement of the two healthy ones, and the two molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is replaced in its place little by little, as we have said; and let not those who are not wise and skilled meddle with it. And sometimes the shape of a cow's tooth bone is made and placed in the place where there is a gap, and it is tightened as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the tie of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this tie comes naturally from under the tongue at birth; or by accident of a healed wound. The procedure is such that you open the patient's mouth and hold their head in your lap, lift up the tongue; then grasp the nerve ligament near its root until the tongue is freed from its attachment. If there is hardness or stiffness there due to the healing of a wound, use an awl and cut through it at the root. Be careful not to cut too deep for the artery that lies underneath. Once you have done this, rinse with rosewater and sage, or cold water, then place a linen cloth under the tongue each night so that the tie cannot heal again
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding begins, crush vitriol and place it on the wound; and if the blood continues to flow, cauterize with a slow-burning cautery that is good for this purpose; then treat with other remedies until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it with red or black color or hard and the sick person does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a chancre. And if it tends to ooze pus, and there is moisture, use a lancet and carefully make an incision with a spatula, and deliver it on one side and the other. If blood flows from your operation, put powdered vitriol on it until it stops flowing, then return to your operation until you remove all furuncle. Then wash the wound with sage and celandine, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes lumps called "godath" appear in the throat, properly known as tonsils. If they do not heal after treatment, as described earlier in this section, take note: if these are hard swellings with a dark red color and small size, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron; likewise for bleeding. But let it remain until it becomes black and ripe, then you can remove it, or else it may burst on its own. And if it is white in color and has a fine root, have your instrument ready to cut it out, but first make sure that the abscess feels warm to touch and is quiet.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Now make the patient sit before the sun, and let his shoulders be in your hand, and let him open his mouth and let the servant take it between his hands, and press the tongue from below with all the instrument, of which this is the form; and it should be made of silver or subtle gold like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue against all this instrument,
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument available, then take the forceps,
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And let it be incised on one side and named on the other; and when you have cut one of the almonds, so cut the other according to the same manner, and afterward the patient should gargle with hot water and rue, and hyssop, and if blood flows, then the patient should gargle with water in which pomegranate peels or bay leaves have been cooked, and similar things, until the blood is stanched; then care must be taken until it is healed. And sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two almonds, so cut them then just like the two almonds equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman who had an abscess that was almost inside her throat, namely an abscess of little sense; and I had nearly closed the entire throat so that she could not breathe due to the blocked passage, nor could she eat or drink, and would have died if left thus for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had grown so much that it had filled up the entire space inside.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hurried then and inserted a knife into one of the openings, then drew it out and removed a large portion of the boil; then I inserted the knife into the other opening in the throat, opened her mouth and pressed down on her tongue; afterwards I inserted the knife into this abscess and cut off part of it, and only a little blood came out; thus the passage of the woman’s throat was cleared out, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I kept cutting away at that boil for a long time; but the boil kept growing back and filling up the space that I had emptied, until it became very large again. Then I cauterized it with a hot iron inside her throat: thus it remained without growing any further. And I left this region, and I do not know what God did with her afterwards.
de l’uve	And when you wish to treat a man or woman whose eye is inflamed externally, take some of the powdered plant called "maiden's breath" (*Veronica officinalis*) and mix it with the yolk of an egg; apply this mixture around the eye on the eyelids. Then take a bandage made of linen and wrap it around the head so that it presses gently against the eye, but not too tightly. Leave the bandage in place for three days and nights without removing it to allow the patient to sleep comfortably. After three days, remove the bandage and wash the eye with warm water. Then apply some of the ointment made from rose oil mixed with wax to the eye, taking care not to get any of the mixture into the eye itself. Repeat this treatment for nine days, during which time the inflammation should decrease and the eye become healthy again.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When it extends towards the eyelid and it is inflamed and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below and thick and rounded, it is called "uvéa".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cut as we have said in the division and the cure does not help at all, and you see that the skin around it is quiet, and it is subtle, then you must scrape it; and those that are rounded together and not long; and they are sanguineous or dark colored or black, then you must avoid cutting them.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient from this.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it according to its appearance and length, you must make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument we mentioned earlier; then insert the needle into the eyelid, draw it underneath, and scrape it with one or two of the instruments I mentioned for cutting through two membranes.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut any more than the surplus that is beyond its natural limit; for if you cut more, you harm the voice and speech; and after incision, use what we have said in the incision of two testicles, until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears being cut, then you must use an instrument for cauterizing their sense of fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The manner of applying the cautery is hot and dry.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient places their head in your hand, and then you press their tongue with the instrument we mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and pour on boiling water quickly, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and in applying this instrument gently, here is its shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And at the top there is a small hollow where one puts the medication, as if it were a spoonful of the medicine, and places the instrument entirely on the eye humor. And the patient should lie on his side so that saliva and mucus runs out of his mouth instead of the medicine entering the throat or the eye. Then hold your hand over the medicine and press it onto the eye for about half an hour until you see it is darkened and the medication bites are apparent. And if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument entirely with the cotton into the canal above until the cotton touches the eye humor. Do this often until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry and fall off after four or five days. And if you need to restart the cauterization with medication, do so, and afterwards clean around the eye with cotton dipped in rose water, and clean what is around the medicine; and rinse with cold water and cure with gargarisms until healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is better than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner: take calamint, hyssop, origanum, rue, chamomile, lavender and similar herbs, and assemble them all together in one pot. And add some of these herbs to the pot and let it boil well covered with thick earth. And there should be an iron instrument in the shape of a small spoon inside the pot:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And let it be of silver or brass, and one of its ends should be placed in the patient's mouth until steam rises to the eye through the canal, until the eye is killed; afterwards begin again often, until the eye dries up, and ensure that you do not do this at the beginning of the appearance of a hot boil, for many things can happen then; and do not do this further than the decline of a hot boil.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a sieve and put an egg-shell into the head so that the mouth of the patient does not become too hot; for the egg-shell does not let steam burden the mouth, and this is good treatment together.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times something sharp like a bone or fish spine, or any other thing gets stuck in the throat; so it is necessary that you remove what you can see and press the tongue with the instrument towards the sun until you see the object move. And what you cannot see but is stuck in the throat must be made to vomit by the patient before the food becomes cooked in the stomach; perhaps then the object will come out through vomiting. Or else the patient should swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a piece of lettuce root, or a small piece of dry bread; and tie one thread to the sponge, and then swallow it. And when it reaches the location, it will rise up, and then you can pull it out. And if it does not come out from what we have said, then take an instrument made of lead in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And the instrument should be curved at its end so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have its top lifted up. And make sure not to touch the epiglottis with it, nor push the bone too far in, but move the instrument gently until the patient feels where the object is stuck; then have them insert the instrument deeper or pull it out evenly until the object comes out completely.
de la sansue de la gorge	de la sansue de la gorge
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	No bloodletting is done, as I said in the division, through medicinal treatment; and if that does not help, then observe the throat of the patient towards the sun, when you press the tongue with the instrument I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see a vein, then tie it gently all around with a small thread or with fine tongs that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if bleeding does not help, take a heated sieve and place it in the throat of the patient, then place the end of the sieve into hot iron, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is seized by water all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, pour it in without letting them swallow, and move it with their hand often; and as soon as the blood feels the water, it falls.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida using the instrument mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will fall without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	The manner of the fumigation is thus: take a pot that has live coals within it, and let the pot's cover be pierced with a small hole in its center, through which insert the head of the instrument. Then cast your fumigation into the pot, and have the patient place the end of the tube in their mouth, closing their mouth tightly so that no smoke escapes but reaches deep down to the sinus; and the sinus will fall now, and if it does not fall, then recommence the fumigation many times. Let the patient abstain from drinking water and eat salty foods and suffer thirst.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which to treat the cinder is this: when it can be seen, it resembles curved tweezers for entering the throat. It should resemble a goose's bill and have sharpness like a file so that whatever it grasps, it cannot let go. And here is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many kinds of abscesses exist, according to what is remembered here from one and the other in this book, and they are diverse in both perforation and incision; and there are two ways [to treat them], the first being similar in appearance, and those that hold moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for places where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head differ from those at the base, and the ones on fatty tissue differ from those that occur in joints, and each should be judged individually.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And there are abscesses which one should not pierce until the bowels have completed their movement; and there are some that must be pierced when they have grown large, even if they do not complete according to their course, such as those near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses occur near joints and are left until they burst open, sometimes the ligaments and nerves of the joint become corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the abscess is near the main limb, if you delay its perforation until it's mature, it will harm the main limb. If it's near the base, pierce it before it matures. Do not pierce a ripe abscess without completing digestion, except for those near the base to prevent it from breaking inside and forming a fistula that cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	"And you should know the hour of piercing an abscess that is dead according to its fulfillment, and that is when the pain has ceased, and the separation of fever, and the decrease of pain and redness, and from softening and hardness at the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you should make the perforation where it depends more hanging down than the abscess, and where it opens most; and let the perforation be long enough for the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints and near nerves and arteries, and in all places smooth without fold."
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	When it pleases to rain upon that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in its mature stage, it is good that you let the incision remain until it has consolidated with completed digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	But if you prick it before its time, the body will be filled with its venom, and it will be full of much filth; and sometimes the edges and depth become hardened.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is any abscess that should be opened according to its size in relation to the body, depending on what the member needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you should make small holes for small abscesses, small incisions; and for large abscesses, large holes and many slits according to the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses where it is necessary to press down with a heart-shaped probe or cover; when they have become as dry as parchment and weakened, then one should proceed like the treatment for boils: And there are those that are slit into three angles, and there are those where you cut like the miter valve, like abscesses of the angles; and there are those where a round incision is made, and other incisions with similar cuts.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have no head, such as soft superficial abscesses, you should pierce them completely; and when the abscess is large, and it has collected much bile, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the bile at that moment, but draw out a part of it; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out some more; do this repeatedly bit by bit, until all the bile comes out. Similarly, if the patient is of weak constitution, or pregnant woman, or small children, or elderly men, do so.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	If the bile suddenly gushes out with the release of the abscess, which by chance might cause the patient's death, and you were unaware of it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	So proceed with this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, then let the wound open up, and examine if the wound of the abscess is small. And if it's a clean cut, bring cloths made of linen or old cotton; and if it's a large abscess and there are many holes in it, then it is necessary to place in each one a bandage so that they come together against each other. And if you have cut off a piece of skin from the abscess and have removed it around, then it is necessary to fill it with dry cotton or linen cloth without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it, and dress the wound with ointment until it's clean.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if evacuation of blood occurs during your operation, then bring cold water and basin, wet the cloth, and place it repeatedly on the bleeding area.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, bring gauze and bandage, and apply the powders mentioned earlier in this book to the area. If it is wintertime and the affected area is very sensitive, you should place warm moistened cloths soaked in wine and oil on it. If it is summertime and the area is fatty, you should place cloths moistened in cold water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, on it until the third day, as we have said before; then remove the bandage, cleanse and dress the wound until it heals completely.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	"And this one must know universally in the cure of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed with the cure of abscesses, and here is this chapter."
des soros	"of sores"
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Warts on the head come from small abscesses and are like warts that are found in linen, similar to those of a hen's egg, and there are many such similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	It has some that are fatty and such that have moisture like poultice; and there are also those that are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery opposes it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of cutting is that you examine all the instruments called "entromissoire", from which the form comes afterwards, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, strike it lengthwise on top.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is emptied, scrape it clean without leaving any skin that contains this moisture, because it returns immediately if anything is left behind; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment if present; if not, use water and salt, and apply it to the wound, leaving it until the next day; and this will chase away what remains of the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then recommence with the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third day, until you know well that nothing remains of the night; then dress the wound with suitable ointment until it is clean.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the boil is thick with flesh, cut it according to this form, long; sprinkle your feathers there, and scrape all around it, and make sure to draw out all that lies beneath its skin. And if the artery opposes you, do what I told you later.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And likewise do for a boil if it is hard, cutting and draining as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision of a hard and moist boil is easier because they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these boils have a head without moisture, or the hard boil that I cut from the head of an old woman; and I found the boil like a hard, rough, white stone, unbreakable; and if one had tried to break it, they would have made just as much wound as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	Other boils coming to the head, especially those that come on the heads of children and at the roots of ears, should always be opened in the lowest place possible so that they may empty easily, and treat them as is necessary.
des scrophules	Scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur at the neck, and under the buttocks, and in the armpits, and sometimes they appear elsewhere on the body; they are many, and often interconnected.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	Each boil is properly inside its skin fold, like the one on the neck and the abscess on the head, as we have said; there are many types of these boils.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and others that are malignant which do not wish to yield to treatment
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that one which you see with good placement to touch, and is similar in color to the skin, and moves on each side and is not hard near the nerves of the neck or the artery or vein, and is not deep; then you must cut it from above and scrape it from both sides, and expose the two lips of the heart, if necessary, as we have said for abscesses on the head; and treat it little by little, and make sure that you do not cut into the nerve or vein, and be careful not to use a curved or pointed knife, so that the hand does not slip, and do not cut too deeply, lest you cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not allow you to work, then place crushed vitriol powder or some powders that stop bleeding in the wound, and press on the wound; leave it until the abscess is soothed, the wound softened, and begins to decay.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the bleeding is stopped, return to your task until you complete it. Then check your index finger for any small scabs, cut them off and remove them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scab, do not cut off that scab at its root but tie it with a strong double thread and let it fall off without harm. Then dress the wound with Egyptian oil-soaked cotton, then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut off the entire scab, then join together both lips of the wound and sew them now, since there will be no surplus left due to the size of the scab.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you must understand how to grasp its root and draw forth fire, then cut as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrophules that hold excessiveness, pierce where it opens mortally; and pierce thus as the aforementioned one, dependingly, then bring forth tents with ointment and similar things so that it corrupts what remains of corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, then cure with anointing around flesh until it is healthy.
de squinance	The term "squinance" does not appear to have a standard medical definition or usage in medieval or early modern surgical texts. It is possible that it was a regional or colloquial term used by surgeons of the time, but without more context, it is difficult to determine its meaning with certainty. If you can provide additional information about where this term appears and in what context, I may be able to provide a more accurate interpretation.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	This quote translates to: "The ancients spoke and discussed the operation of cutting for the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who performed it, and this is written in their words."
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who are strangling/choking, it is necessary that the opening of the throat called "epiglottis" be cleared away; and one should not offer assistance by this method because all the veins and the membranes of the patient are hot in the mouth or throat or in two lumens.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the vein, it is necessary to lift the epiglottis to avoid suffocation from choking.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary that we do so below three circles or four, with a small cut across, between two circles or according to the quantity of the syfac's cut, not in the cartilage; and those places are suitable for cutting the epiglottis where there is no flesh.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, then it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat all around, then cuts into the heart until it reaches the pharynx; and avoids the blood vessels, if you see any, and then grasp the syfac as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the pharynx's artery that spurts fire from the place that is broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a short time.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour of doubt about strangulation has passed, bring together the two lips of the wound in the heart and sew it closed without including the cartilage; then apply medicines that promote healing until it is sound again.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely closed up, and the patient is judged to be near death, and the harm is done
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cut the epiglottis because the patient cannot swallow and breathes through the wound. And thus death is prevented. And so the ancients ordered that the wound should be left open until the malady has passed, which takes three or four days. And then they commanded that the wound be sewn up and dressed until it was healed. And I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young woman took the knife and stabbed herself in her throat, cutting part of the windpipe. And I was called to heal her, but found her already dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	Upon examining the wound, I found that blood had flowed from it, and I knew for certain that she had not cut her veins or opened a passage through which air could escape, but that wind was escaping through the wound
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sewed the wound, healing it until it was healthy. And the young woman suffered only temporary loss of voice, returning afterwards to her normal state. Therefore, I say there should be no fear in cutting the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of a thick throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called 'throat hernia,' and it appears as a large swelling of the color of a bruise. It occurs most commonly in women, and there are two kinds: natural and accidental. The natural kind has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And accidents occur in two ways: one is similar to fatty tissue, and the other manner is like an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear involved, and it is not necessary to operate with fierce fire except in those cases that are small, and prove and search throughout the incision: if you find it as I described fat, and it cannot reach any vein, then cut it, just as one cuts fatty tissue, and scrape it completely, even its surface, if there is any; and examine everything thoroughly, and treat it as it should be treated until it is perfectly healthy.
des nous	From us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many kinds of fatty tissue exist, all of which I will describe their similarities; and now I must explain the entire difference between fat and exudate.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that dislocation is hot and has fever until boiling passes, and putrefaction is completed; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	Fatty tissue has no heat, fever, or pain, and contains fat that is its own sac, having the color of the body, starting like a bag and growing large; and there are two kinds, either fatty or moist, most having the colors mentioned in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the treatment of the knot, you must first examine and inquire with all the instruments called "trocar," according to what its shape will be as described in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of examining abscesses in the nose is that you take the moistest part of the abscess and gently twist your fingers little by little until you know that the probe has pierced the core, then according to the size of the abscess; then remove the probe, and be careful lest anything spurt out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If there is running moisture, whatever its color, then cut it as I said for other abscesses; and if after the probe no moisture comes out, know that it is hard, so cut it in a cross shape, grasp it with forceps, gently scrape each side and guard the skin where it lies so that you draw it out whole with the root; and if you cannot draw it out whole, then draw it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	But if something remains, the nose will return many times; and if a little remains and blood troubles you, then cover the wound with some hot corrosive powders, and hold the wound together, and place warm soothing ointments for an abscess on it, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed; and if the nose is large, cut the two lips of the wound, and cure what is around the flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	"And if the beating vein is against you or another, then hurry and apply the powder of vitriol ground, and let it lie for two or three days until the wound rots, and the ebullition of blood calms; then return to cut those that remain of the knot."
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the shapes of the foreign bodies inserted into [the body], and they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small. There are three squares called 'albaret', and one called 'breb'. They also come in three sizes to encircle fistulas: large, medium, and small. These are like the needles used for stitching sorceresses, made of citrine copper, iron, or silver. The ones that are yellow are more valuable, but black lead is preferred for encircling fistula cups. They come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the holes.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the forceps are in many likenesses: large, medium, and small. There are also forceps with two cups in three ways; those with three cups are likewise in three ways. Those with two cups and single-cup forceps are also of three kinds. All these are necessary in their places.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of this tool is sharp-edged, and there are some that only cut on one side, from which the hairs are scraped off so as not to nick the vein or nerve. These kinds of instruments are often hidden in hands, so the patient does not perceive them when opening abscesses; they come in three sizes: large, small, and medium, as you see. And such tools are used mainly in thick flesh, such as legs, arms, breasts, armpits, and similar places. Sometimes another tool is made that resembles a fist's cuticle, shaped like this, with which blood is wiped away.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	"And it is sometimes placed at the site where there is danger of cutting veins and arteries, and sometimes they are large in size:"
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to decay, appearing like women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to treat them should do so according to this form from line b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape away the fat, and dress the wound with medicine inside it, then bring together the two lips of the wound to stitch, and care for it until it is healed. And if the nipple leans downwards, and is enlarged by its size as happens in women, then make two incisions above into the ribs through two similar slits; so that one holds onto the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from line .b. up to line .g.. Then scrape away the skin that is between the two lips and remove the fat, and prepare as we have said for stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the care until it is healed. And if it is not healed or if the incision is not complete because the patient will not rest, or due to bleeding, then you must fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive ointment. Leave it until it has softened the remaining fat, then care for it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	Of armpit fistulas
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	"These fistulas that come under the armpits are of the type of hard scrofula with lumps, and some contain moisture."
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture must be cut according to this shape, from line .b. to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And when the entire lump in the fistula has been emptied, fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and heal it with appropriate ointment until it is sound."
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	"And if the fistula resembles scrofula, cut it like we have said for scrofula incisions; and if the wound gapes open, apply a caustic as we have mentioned before."
de la routure de l’artere	Of arterial rupture
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is injured and the skin above it is scorched, abscesses often form, and likewise when a vein bursts and an abscess forms. And one can recognize this thus: if it's for the artery, the abscess will be long and deep; you'll feel a pulling sensation with your fingers. If it's for the vein, there will be obvious swelling. It is foolish to cut into such an abscess, especially when it's under the armpits or angles or at the neck, or in many other places; these are very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, one must avoid cauterization with fire, especially the head. For an abscess caused by arterial inflammation, make a long incision through the skin; open the wound widely and carefully separate the artery from the tissues until it's exposed. Then insert a needle under one side and pierce it through to the other side. Tie the artery with a double thread in two places, as I've shown you for extracting the two arteries in the temples. Then use an intromissoir to press on the point between the ties until the blood drains out, and remove the abscess. Then dress the wound with compresses so that the bandages remain clean. If the abscess is caused by a vein injury, then take hold of it with your hand, pierce a needle under the point you're holding, pass the thread through to the other side, tie the abscess as I've described, using one of the two knots at each end of the thread. If you're unsure that the stitches are secure, insert another needle along the entire length of the first stitch and tie it in four places. Then cut open the abscess until all the excess fluid drains out. Cut away the excess skin around the heart but leave the tied portion intact. Finally, apply a warm, moist compress soaked in wine and oil, then dress the wound with gauze and ointment until it's healed.
des apostemes des ners	"Abscesses of the nerves"
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly, abscesses can come to the artery and vein, abscesses also come to the nerves when they are injured or from excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.
