And this happens more often to shoulders and hips, and in all places where there are joints, and it is the worst abscesses, their color seems like that of the body, and they are in many dispositions without pain; but when it is squeezed strongly, the patient feels pain, not deep within the body, but below the heart. It moves well in all directions, neither forward nor backward, nor up nor down. And one who is in joints should not be covered with iron: there might be contraction; and those that are on the head or forehead make the skin thin at the temples.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, take it with tongs and cut it at its root; if it is large, suspend it with a hook, scrape it out, then open it and sew up the wound. And treat it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	"Hanging boil sores"
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it happens in the belly and not elsewhere. It is an illness called 'fungus' because of its resemblance to mushrooms. The roots are thin but the heads are large; some are small and others very big. I saw a man who had two on his belly that resembled fungi more than anything else, with no difference between them. They were white and had fine roots, cracked open, and moisture flowed from them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I weighed them and found one to weigh XVIII ounces and the other VI Z., and the work of the incision is such that you should observe if the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is pale and moist with a subtle root; then cut it with a wide spatula, and have the cautery ready in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For during cutting, there are often too large flows of blood, and if the blood overcomes you, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient frightened and afraid of the incision of iron, then take a well-made string of lead, and tie it around the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; then tighten it, and do not cease pulling on the string of lead until you cut the artery, and remove it without effort. And if the roots are large, there is fear in cutting itself for the belly, but you can well cut half of it, then cauterize so that it does not return. Then dress the wound, and ensure that you do not cut the thelul which is of fox color, poor sense, and produces milk.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	"For this is an enchanted abscess, and I will come to the treatment of cancer later on."
quant li boude ist fuer	"When the boil bursts"
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the swelling of the belly comes from cautery of a wound or split of the bladder, and is on the abdomen, as it happens in other ruptures, or from blood flowing from veins or arteries according to what is before mentioned, or from flatulence; and if it's from the rupture of the bladder and the outlet of bile, then the color of the abscess is like the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and there are various outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	"And if it is due to the outlet of the intestines, then it appears more diverse. When pressed between two fingers, it pops up and then returns. Sometimes it is hard, and grows larger at the entrance of the anus with great effort."
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is light and well-defined when you press it with your hand, it does not constrict at all; and if it is due to blood, then the abscess appears large and hard, and is fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to flatulence, it is soft to the touch, and its appearance tells you whether it is from arterial or venous blood, or flatulence.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If thou must leave the treatment
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, concerning the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or for the eye, thou must command the patient to stretch out his arm straight, then grasp all around the wound; then have him lie down smoothly between thy hands, then go around the place that thou hast marked with the spatula, then stretch half of the abscess above completely; then bind it around with a strong thread or a tightly twisted silk cord, and let the knot be well tied; then open half of the abscess stretched out upon the ligature, and insert thy index finger, and seek the intestine; if thou findest it caught by the ligature, untie it and place the intestine outside the belly; and if thou findest the eye, take it with a hook and cut off the superfluity; and if the artery or vein opposes thee, go gently around, then return to thy work and take two needles, and thread them with two strong threads, and insert the two needles crosswise where thou hast made pierced; then hold the abscess in four places upon the needles, and if it swells, remove the needles, and let the place remain until it rots, and scrape off the dead flesh; or cut it when it is ripe and rotted, then dress it as it ought to be done, and open the abscess as we have said; then extract the blood or moisture that thou findest, then dress the place as it ought to be done, and sew up the place.
dou chancre	"Regarding cancer"
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	"We have discussed the appearance of cancer and how to treat it with medications in our division. We must also be cautious when treating cancerous ulcers in the marrow or large ones that are difficult to excise, such as those found in the breast, thigh, and similar locations. The ancients advised removing them completely when they first appear, but once they become large and old, it is not advisable to approach them as I have never seen anyone cured of cancer, nor has anyone else before me."
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And when the cancer is located in an area where it can be removed, as we have said, you should purge the patient with black bile once or twice. Then let him fast if he shows signs of repletion. Next, prepare a good operating site to perform the surgery. Then grasp the cancer with your thumb and index finger, cut it off from all sides, and remove it completely without leaving anything behind. Allow the blood to flow freely, wipe the wound clean with your hand or any other object, and if bleeding from the incision of an artery or vein opposes you, cauterize it until the bleeding stops. Then treat the wound with other remedies until it is healed."
de ydropisie	Dropsey
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have previously spoken in the division about the similarities of dropsy, how water is gathered, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: only 'eclites' is mentioned; and one must not touch with iron in these two semblances: namely tympanites and yposarche, for it is deadly; therefore when you treat this semblance of dropsy called 'eclites' with medicines, and the cure does not help, look if the patient is weak, or if they have another disease besides dropsy, such as wind and bloating and similar things; do not touch them with iron, for there is doubt; and if you see that the patient has great strength, and they have no other disease but dropsy alone, and they are neither too young nor too old, then you should act thus: lift the patient upright onto your hands, and the ministers press the belly, pushing water towards the lowest part of the breast, then take the spatumile espinous according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be cut into two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And pierce with a point, but not so deeply that it reaches the intestines when inserted, lest it cause injury. Then observe if dropsy has entered towards the intestines: if so, make an incision three fingers' breadth below the navel on the right side; if dropsy is due to liver disease, make the incision on the left of the navel; if due to worms, on the right. Ensure the patient does not lie upon the incision so superfluities do not flow into that weak spot. Then pierce all the skin with this instrument and withdraw it. Place your hand at the level of the skin and fat, as in flaying, to the depth of a fingernail or somewhat less. Then pierce the fat until the spatula reaches the empty space, which is the location of water. Withdraw the spatula and insert this instrument; this is its form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it resembles a thin silver chain, and is made of bronze or lead, light, with a small hole at the bottom part; and on one side, three holes; and two on another side, and one on the other; and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision that writers use to cut a feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	And at the top is the alembic, so that when the instrument reaches the water, it now descends onto the instrument; empty it then by one half or a third part, for if you empty more than is needed at that hour, perhaps the patient will die from the resolving of his spirit from the wound, or he falls unconscious, or approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of its power, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's virtue signify, and his pulse; then draw out the instrument and retain the water, and it is retained now by the heart that stops up the hole that is on the phlegm, about which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then recommence the instrument the next day, if you see the patient enduring these things, and draw out a small quantity of water; do this for several days, and guard yourself from being too hasty so that it does not remain but a drop of water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and leave much water on it, cure it with hot sand burial, often rubbing or bathing in sunlight, and dye of drinking; and cure it with drying medicines until it is dry, cauterize the stomach, liver, and spleen after extracting the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stoppage of the wand
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born without a hole in the penis, or with a small hole, or one not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary, pierce it at once with a very fine spatula according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then place a thin plug of lead into the hole and tie it securely for three or four days. When it wants to urinate, remove the plug and let it do so, then replace it. Sometimes this may not be necessary, as the urine will not leave through the closed opening.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	Those whose hole is small should use the lead plug medication, as we have said, so that it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	They who do not have the opening in its proper place are blocked, for some are born with the opening at the head of the penis, which prevents them from urinating unless they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot empty themselves because the matter cannot reach the bladder, and this is a serious illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of performing the operation is that the patient lies on his back, then stretch out the head of the penis and cut it off like the shape of a pen's nib so that the hole falls in the middle as it should; but be careful not to cut too much, because many times blood comes out, and if this happens, then stanch the blood with whatever stops bleeding, and cure the wound until it is sound.
des pustules de la verge	of the sores of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these albatrosses appear on the member, and it is an ugly appearance of flesh; and there are malignant ones and non-malignant ones; so you must take them with a subtle pincer, cut and clean all, then place moistened cotton in Egyptian ointment; then treat with diaphoretic ointment until it heals.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the wound is malignant, of foul color and foul-smelling, then you must bring fire cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it out, and if the wound is on the penis, with part inside the foreskin and part outside, then you must first remove the flesh that is inside; and when it is sewn up, then treat the outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat them together, the head of the penis may not be properly healed, and blackness and corruption come to its inside and the vulva; so you must cut away all that is black and corrupted, then apply a plaster made from pomegranate peel and resin mixed with honey and flour, and then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if there is an onset of bleeding, then apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And the cauteries help in two conditions together: namely, for the flow of blood and corruption. And if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, then you should insert or conduct through it a reed of lead, and let the patient urinate through it. And when the skin at the head of the penis that occurs in those who have not been circumcised becomes hard due to wound or abscess, then you must scrape it with the shaving instrument until the foreskin is loosened and the head of the penis is delivered from all sides. And if it is difficult to separate them, then you should scrape some off the head of the penis and skin with the spatula, then gently dissect between the two, and place a subtle linen cloth moistened in cold water, so that it may soften again.
de la circoncision	"of circumcision"
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	"Circumcision is not a continuous dismemberment like other wounds; nonetheless, when we perform this operation willingly and properly on children, it is necessary to make the best and easiest work for salvation."
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	"I say that the ancients did not circumcise their children, for it was not used in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience."
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	"Because I have seen most masters and senior surgeons performing circumcision with only one dal, without forceps, and using just one novacula; thus it happened that the skin remained torn because there were two layers, and sometimes they cut the upper one and leave the lower one."
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	"Otherwise, they cut it again, and the pain is doubled; moreover, at the time of cleansing the wound from the dal, the point of the member is not securely protected; also, during cleansing of the nail, sometimes the iron slips and damages the work, and many times it happens that there is no need for cleansing, which I have seen."
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	"Concerning the cleansing that is done with forceps and with the entire length of thread, I have found through experience its goodness because the forceps cuts evenly both above and below."
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you press your hand thus and cut evenly in one single movement; but let the thread be well pulled tight around the skin; and so it should happen that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are doing nothing but tying the thread around the stick only, then make him laugh in all ways you can; then make him stand upright between your hands, and hide the threads between your hands or under your feet so the child sees neither them nor any of the tools; then place your hand on the stick and blow into the heart, and pull it upwards until the head of the stick is inside; then clean it well from the dirt that has gathered there, then tie the left sign with a double thread, then tie it under one knot to the other; and hold it with two fingers by the second knot at the wrist and the index finger, and cut between the two knots, then quickly raise the heart up and pull the head of the stick; then let the blood flow from pocket to pocket, for that is the matter; and put powder on it and over the powder a cloth stuck together with a mixture of cooked egg yolk not diluted with rose water, well confited with good fresh rose oil, and leave it until the next day, and treat him further until he is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	"The shape of the forceps for cleansing should be like this: the two jaws should be thin and sharp, and the jaws should be as large as the middle finger, evenly."
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	"The error in cleansing is when the skin inside is stuck to the incision; therefore, it is necessary that you stretch it with your fingernail before the edges stick together and cut it evenly. And if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, then hold it with forceps and cut it."
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	"And if it has passed three days and the skin underneath the penis is swollen, let it be until the inflammation is calmed down, then carefully scrape it off; cut as much as you can without damaging the penis itself."
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Then treat the wound with powder for sudden wounds, as we have mentioned in our treatment of powders. And if you cut too much from the skin and it goes upwards, it will not harm at all. Then treat it as we have said until it is healed."
dou retenement de l’urine	"Regarding the retention of urine"
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is caused by obstruction due to a stone, or congealed blood, or mucus, or flesh newly born, or similar things, which we have mentioned in the division. If urine is not released and you see that there is an obstruction because of a stone that has grown or lodged at the neck of the bladder, then the patient must be made to crouch on his knees; let his feet rest on his back, extend his belly on the part above his back, and have the patient hold himself up as much as he can. Then the neck of the bladder will be compelled to expel the stone upwards, so that urine is released. If it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction using all the instruments called "syringe," which is shaped like this: let it be made of thin silver tubing, light like a bird's feather; let its tube be one and a half palms long, and let it be sharp at the end.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	Now the method of issuing urine is as follows: take a doubled thread and tie it to the top of a wad of wool or cotton, then put the thread's end into the syringe. Cut off any excess wool from the wad, then place it up to the syringe's tip. Then anoint the syringe with oil or butter mixed with egg yolk. Have the patient sit on a chair, and gently raise their bladder and penis using moistened oil and olive oil. Then lightly insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then fold the penis upwards towards the navel. Next, push the syringe forward until it reaches the bladder, which the patient will feel when it's empty. Then pull out the thread along with the wool wad, allowing urine to flow along with it. After that, remove the wad and continue using the syringe until the bladder is emptied, relieving the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	Maladies de la vessie
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	"If blood or pus comes into the bladder, or if there is putrefaction gathered there, and you see that water and medicines are being distilled, then use all the instrument called 'clasp', and this is its form:"
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the holes raised so that the medicine cup fits tightly without any addition, so that if needed, it can draw out moisture and introduce what is necessary; and when you see your medicines entering the bladder, place the spout of the siphon in the moisture, and draw out the fluid inside; then you will draw out the moisture into the siphon, and then strongly push the tube back in; thus the moisture enters inside, and comes to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it; and this is the form of the subtle enema used to administer an enema to the bladder:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is made of silver or brass, and the spout is higher; and below there is one seam where the tube falls; then take a bladder from a sheep and put in the moisture with which you will enema the bladder, then tie it between two breasts firmly with doubled thread, and heat this moisture on the fire; then place the tip of the enema into the tube, then press your hand on the bladder until all the moisture arrives at the bladder, so that the patient feels it has reached the bladder; and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment and make a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then strongly insert the thread into these holes, then join the circle as one joins a sieve, and put inside what you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it onto the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	"de la pierre"
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	"We have previously stated in the division the methods of stone, and their extraction together with medicines; and I have mentioned the difference between stone lodged near the kidneys, and all its signs, and in which stone one must operate by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you this clearly and briefly."
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	"I say that stone which is lodged in the bladder happens more often to children, and it is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder appearing like water in its subtlety; and it makes the patient's penis appear harenaeous, and he feels great pain and frequently urinates, and then stiffens; and many of these cases have a foundation; and the healing of children is easy until they are four years old, and it is very difficult for the elderly, and it is moderate for youths, for those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one."
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, first it is necessary to cleanse the patient with a clyster, to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For sometimes it obstructs the stone-searching.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and lower them and move them below so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes it ascends from its high place; then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands are under his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely inclined downward; then seek and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, hurry now to cut on the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall at the touching of all, then moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand if the patient is a child, or your middle finger if the patient is fully grown; and put it in his anus, and seek the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, guide it to the neck of the bladder; then press on it with your finger, and push it out where you see to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and he commands that he stretch out his right hand upwards and remove the skin that is below the thighs in the part where the cut is made, then insert the spatula thus shaped.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make an incision between those that are between the thighs and the fundament, not in the middle but on the side of the left hip bone; and let it be straight upon the stone, and your two fingers always on the fundament, and let the knife cut so that it is wide at the front and narrow within, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure will cause the finger that is on the fundament to slip out without labor; and know that there are such stones that have angles and edges: they are difficult to remove; and there are also those that are smooth, resembling a lentil, and rounded, from which the exit is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	For those that have angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not slip out, then you must extract with forceps that are like a file at the end, to move the stone so that it does not escape; or you put beneath it a subtle curved instrument at the head; and if you cannot thus catch it, then widen the hole around the passage, and if blood flows out, stop it with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, first place the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut above it, then let it slip forth, and afterwards extract the smaller ones if there are many.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it [the dislocation] is very large, then it must be cut deeper, making a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	But if two things happen to the patient: either he dies or urine flows constantly from where the wound cannot heal; nonetheless, strive to draw it [the dislocation] out with forceps or cut it into pieces until you have completed your work. Then dress the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, bandage it, and place a moist cloth soaked in oil and wine (or oil and rose water and cold water) on top to soothe the inflamed abscess. Then bind the patient tightly around his neck, and do not remove the bandages until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you untie him, then wash the wound very well with oil and water, then apply the ointment of diacynthion and the ointment of basilicum until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if hot abscesses appear in the wound and corrosion occurs, and blood clots form in the bladder, causing urine to be retained in such a way that it flows without control: then boil some of your own dough in the wound, and remove that blood, for if it remains there, it will harm the bladder and corrupt it. Then wash the wound with water and rue and celandine, and aid him [the patient] in all ways that you know until he is healed. And it is necessary that during every session of treating him, you tie his two thighs together, and apply medicine to its proper place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small and it lies in the passageway of the penis and is stuck there, preventing urine from flowing out; then follow the treatment I mentioned earlier, cutting it many times until it is pierced through by this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already tried it this way.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron awl shaped thus and having three prongs forged into one stake:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the penis below the stone so that it cannot move backwards into the bladder. Then insert the drill into the penis gently until it reaches the stone. Turn the drill in your hand against the stone bit by bit, until you can pierce the stone from the other side. Then urine will come out soon. Finally, press your hand on what remains of the stone that is still inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it breaks soon and is flushed out with the urine, then the patient is cured. But if you cannot do this for some reason that prevents it, then tie a thread below the stone and another above it. Then cut the penis near the stone between the two threads. Remove the stone by pulling it out, untie the threads, clean the wound of any congealed blood, and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	Of women's stones
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that stones are dislocated in women's cases, and if it happens sometimes, its treatment is difficult, and it is forbidden for three reasons: the first one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second one is that one cannot find a knowledgeable woman who exposes herself to doctors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is such that sometimes one cannot find a woman well-versed in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman lies deeper than the stone of the man, therefore a deeper cut must be made there, with great fear involved. And if you need assistance in this matter, then it becomes necessary for you to procure a competent midwife, and if none can be found nearby, seek one who practices subtle arts; present her with an intelligent female companion knowledgeable about women's lives or a woman familiar with some aspects of the art, instructing her to perform what you command regarding the examination of the stone. Pay close attention whether the woman is a virgin: then she must place her hand on the fundament and search for the stone. If she finds it, she should press down upon it with her hand, and recommend that she place her hand in the patient's vagina, feeling and pressing strongly with her left hand over the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, then it is necessary to move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder downwards until it reaches the root of the thigh; then cut against the stone at the root of the thigh opposite the middle of the thigh bone where it appears displaced, and feel for the stone in that part; and do not move your finger above or below the stone, and let the incision be small at first; then insert the knife into the incision if you feel the stone so close to the wound that the stone can come out fire, and know that there are many kinds of stones: namely, small and large and sharp and smooth, long and round, and those with roots.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	Know the similarities to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood faints, then put powdered vitriol in place and hold it there for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your work until the stone is out, and have tools ready as I told you for extracting stones from men to help you in your task; and if the blood faints and it is from the artery that has been cut, then apply powder on the place and tie it with bandages and do not begin again cutting there, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, lest by chance the patient dies; then dress the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased and the wound can bear it, then return to your work until the stone is out.
de hernie carnouse	Here is a possible translation for "de hernie carnouse":
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	A hernia is nothing other than a gathering of moisture or white seed that is under the heart of a cock, which contains the egg; and it is called "seed," and sometimes it is properly inside the skin of the egg, so that one might think it is another egg. It is the skin of the cock between the white seed that we have mentioned, and this only happens if there was no pouch.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the cause of this hernia is weakness in the cocks, which causes this matter to spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the joints, and this moisture has many colors: either it's colored declining to yellowish, or it's without redness, or black, or watery white, and such things happen more often; these are the signs by which one recognizes this gathering, for if it is of a whitish hue as we have said, then the abscess is ripe, about as long as the shape of an egg, and does not open the joints, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the proper cloth, then the abscess is ripe with part of the yolk, and therefore one thinks that it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the whitish surface, it is felt quite well. Therefore, when you wish to know the color of the moisture, test it on all parts of the square intromitter, as its shape is shown here before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Therefore, based on what comes out after squeezing, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we cut it with iron, the patient should be sound according to his strength and the fullness of his body. Then lay him on his back, upon something slightly high, and put many cloths under him. Then sit on his left side, and command the assistant to sit on the right, and extend the staff to one of the two ribs where the heart is located. Then take the spatula lightly, and cut the skin among the ribs near the thumb, and let your cut be straight downwards, dividing the skin until it reaches the white fat, and scrape it subtly according to your strength. Then pierce the fat full of water with one wide hole, and drain all the water, then put on your bandages, and stretch the fat upwards; And do not touch the heart's ribs, but only the fat itself; cut everything or in pieces softly, so that if you don't cut it smoothly, water will return. And if the egg slips during your work, fix it back in its place when you have completed the work on the fat. Then sew together the two parts of the heart's ribs with a stitch, then heal it like other wounds until it is sound.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find that the egg is corrupted by some other disease, then ligate the vessels that are suspending it to stop the flow of blood. Then cut through the entire suspension ligament and remove the egg, treating the wound as previously described.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	If water collects in two parts together, knowing that these are two branches; cut off the other part as you did the first evenly, then squeeze out the blood, and place in the wound clean wool moistened in rose oil. And place another wool moistened in wine and oil on it, and lay doubled cloths over it, and tie it all together according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths and fill them with wool lint according to this shape and they should be sewn together at the waist of the breeches, and one of the heads takes up the fundament up to the back, and the other at the fist joint; and the two ends over the two angles, and all the restraint is gathered in the loop of the breeches. And sometimes this branch is treated with cautery instead of iron cutting, and it is that you take one subtle cautery knife and cut into the skin of the joints, and heat it up as we have said so that the white sac containing the water is exposed; then take the cautery in this form and pierce that sac several times, and scrape it clean with this hot subtle cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And cut in all the ways that you can, until you have removed everything; and ensure that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more beneficial; and move carefully to avoid blood loss, and make sure the surgical cuts are clean; and if anything goes against you, whether it's a boil or blood loss or something else, then treat what goes against you, according to what is written before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this procedure due to its harshness, perform perforation as I instruct you. And when you are certain that the water of rain is present there, according to the signs we have mentioned earlier, then have the patient sit on a raised seat; cut the boil at its base with a broad spatula and insert the perforation tool deep into the body; make the opening large enough so all the water flows out. Then place cotton on the site and tie it, leaving it for the rest of the water to flow out. Then dress the wound until it is healed. And if the bandage does not allow the water to exit through the mouth of the wound, you must insert a feather or the instrument used to treat hydrops, whose shape is shown earlier. Widen the wound opening and know that the water will return and gather again after six months or so. Once it has gathered as before, the patient will recover.
de l’aposteme des coions	"Abscess of the thighs"
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	You should know that in the case of this branch [of medicine], there is fear and more often misdiagnoses, therefore it seems to me that it would be better if one left it alone. I will tell you the workings and similar things about an abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many gangrenes occur in the body, and especially on the testicles; and this happens often.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to be known that an abscess comes about from sharp and burning acidity, which spreads through the joints or by percussion; and the colour of the abscess follows the colour of the body; and it does not cause pain, and it is a serious abscess; and sometimes there are abscesses that are hard and full of pus, with yellowish colour, and some come from an artery or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it comes from an artery, it is recognised by the hot disposition of the abscess when you press it with your two fingers; and you must not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	That which comes from swelling of a vein is known by its disposition upon expressing the touch of two fingers, and one can well make an incision upon this kind, and on others; and it is that you cut along the joints, then stretch the egg upwards, and strike off the white skin, and free it from all around the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already solid with these fresh wounds, then you must draw out the egg and cut it open; and if it is air in the face or in those that are inside the vessels, then you must remove all of this tension completely and roundly cut the opening.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	"And if the birth canal is located at the back, then you must cut all of it and remove the womb, as we have said."
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And once your task is completed, fill the wound with wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then apply other dressings until it heals."
de l’aposteme des coions	"Abscess of the thighs"
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping resembling wool, with softening of the joints, and the patient cries out when he walks; and the treatment for this disease is just as fearful as the one mentioned before, yet we will tell you about its workings according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You must have the patient sit on an elevated seat, then place the suspension band for the joints below your two arms, close to all the vessels near the groin; tie it with a knot and stretch it firmly. Then cut with a wide, sharp scalpel across the vessels until they are exposed, and scrape away from each side as we have described in the extraction of arteries in the temples. Then insert a needle with double thread where the vein first appeared, and tie it at both ends. Cut evenly down the middle according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted moisture. Then dress the wound like others where an arrow has entered, so that no vessel bleeds that nourishes one of the joints. For through this there comes no harm, but if the vein comes from all vessels, then draw out both joints from all vessels; so that the bone does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and let them dry and be unable to help.
de la routure dou syfac	"about the dislocation of the hip socket"
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The occurrence of this rupture comes from the bursting at the side, or the stretching over the belly in the region of the hips, causing the intestines to descend from that tear towards one of the kidneys; and this tear is either in the side, or due to stretching of it, and these two ways come from many causes: such as blows, falls, coughing, lifting heavy weights, and similar things; and the sign when it's from the stretching of the side, is that it happens little by little over a long time, not suddenly; and the abscesses are even until deep down because the side presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	"And when it occurs due to separation of the hip socket, there is sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscess appears diverse and prominent under the skin, due to the exit of the intestines and the body behind the hip socket."
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	"Sometimes loops of intestine also descend with it, becoming trapped and causing great pain for the patient, especially when they are pressed upon."
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	"And in these iron treatments, one should avoid cautery."
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	You will do the operation thus: instruct the patient to put their hand inside the wound if they can reach it. Then have them lie on their back with their legs raised. Next, expose the kidney by cutting away the long connective tissue covering it. Then insert uncines into the wound according to your needs to open it enough for the kidney to emerge. Next, peel off the fat around the kidney until the white fibrous capsule is exposed on all sides. Insert your index finger into the space behind the kidney between the two layers of the renal fascia and separate them. Then use your right hand to press down on the kidney while using your left hand to lift up the fascia towards the spine, exposing the entire kidney towards the flank. Instruct your assistant to hold the kidney up and release any attachments behind it. Check with both hands if there is any bowel adhering to the fibrous capsule of the kidney, and if you find any, push it back into the abdomen. Then take a needle with a thick thread made from several strands and insert it into the rear part of the fascia after the kidney. Cut off the excess threads so that there are four remaining. Tie them together in a cross-shaped manner to secure the fascia underneath the kidney, using two tight knots. Next, tie the loose ends of the threads tightly with two knots to prevent any vessels from entering and causing an abscess. Then place the knots according to the first knot along the length of two fingers away from it. After these knots, leave enough space for the kidney underneath the ribs equal to the span of one's hand. Finally, close the wound by applying moist wool soaked in oil to the incision and tying it with the thread mentioned earlier.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	"And sometimes the white bone of the hip socket that we have mentioned is cauterized after the incision to prevent bleeding."
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens, and he lets the lien fall until it falls by itself; and if it takes time to fall, then let it be warmed with hot water, and place what we have said on it until it falls; then treat the wound with another treatment until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	Here is a possible translation for "de hernie carnouse":
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	I never saw anyone in this region who dared to perform the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Moreover, the ancients said that it is done like the branch that grows together with the vine, so you tie the vessels lightly after cutting above them slightly below; then cut into the middle and treat the abscess from what opens until the vessels fall away; and treat it as we have said until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.
