Sometimes a rupture occurs in the anus as we have said, and the area opens up; and no part of the intestines should come out from it, but if some do come out, it is little matter, and repair all hours; and nevertheless if it remains too long at this point, then the wound becomes enlarged or syphilitic until the intestines come out; and this happens due to the extension of the syphilis that is in the anus as we have said, because it is extended, then the area becomes softened and swollen and opens up; and its treatment is by cautery as we have said before; and sometimes it is treated with iron in this way: and it is that the patient lies often on their back between your hands, then cut the area of the rupture swollen from wide according to the quantity of three fingers; and then extract the syphilis that is under the skin that ensues, then take the rod and place it over the apparent area of the syphilis; and press it deep into the belly, then cut the two apparent areas of the syphilis on top of the head of the rod, and cut one and the other; then extract the head of the rod, and do not cut the syphilis nor extend the wound or anything else as I have taught you in the treatment of the rupture of the intestines; then treat it by the cure of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, cleanse it and dress the wound until it is healthy.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	Gangrene is contained and does not show itself in the wound, and cauterization is muted in this area, being closer to safety.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	due to softening of the skin around the anus
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin around the anus in some men becomes softened because the tissues inside are softened, and it is unpleasant to see. And when you want to treat it, make the patient lie on their back and cut away the softened skin from the natural skin. Then bring the two lips together with one stitch and if necessary, sew the excess softened skin at three or four places firmly. Then cut between the stitches and treat it like other wounds until it is healthy, and remove the sutures.
dou chastrement	of castration
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that castration is prohibited in our law, and therefore I would like not to speak of it in this book; and there are only two reasons why it might be necessary: one is for the doctor to respond when asked about it, and know its treatment; and the other because we often have need of castration for certain animals to aid us, such as goat and sheep and cat and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that castration is done in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one that we do by attraction, make the beast sit in hot water until the testicles are softened and hanging, then grasp them with your hand until they are relaxed and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of castration by cutting: it is necessary that you tie the beast and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory ligament, and cut each testicle once after you have properly bled them; leave a small piece of skin and tissue around the vessels; this method of castration is quicker than that done by attraction, because in attraction some part of the testicles may remain, causing the beast to desire lust; then dress the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	on Hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermafroditism exists in two ways among men: one way is that between the two testicles opens also like the figure of a woman's nature, where there is hair, and sometimes it tears during urination.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, who have on their pubis both a penis and two testicles
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for both men and women is to dress the joined parts together and treat them like other wounds; but in the second manner, for those men whose urine flows through the skin of the testicles, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	of tentingene (i.e., tentingene)
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigene is a joined wound on the natural part that is too ugly to see; some women have it as large as a hand, and this is its treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you cut away the excess of the tentigene with your hand or with tweezers, and dress it lightly; and do not go too deep, lest bleeding occur, then treat it with other treatments until it heals. And there is another wound that appears at the mouth of the womb, the anus, and sometimes protrudes like a cow's udder, and for this reason the ancients called it "cow-like disease.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you must cut it, as we have described the incision, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Correction is necessary when the nature of woman's body is not pierced, or if the hole is small; and it is natural at birth, or accidental due to illness that has occurred there; or it is caused by adhered flesh, or by a thin, thick, or dense membrane, and it extends into the marrow, or on the sides, below, or wherever it may be; and prevents conception, childbirth, sometimes causing infertility; and recognition of this condition is by examination of the vulva.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the blockage appears nearby, you should search with your fingers or your staff.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If there is a thin membrane nearby at two fingers' breadth, then act quickly and do as follows: place your two index fingers together, with the woman lying on her back, legs spread apart; then press the two labia firmly until the thin membrane covers the blockage; then take wool, dampen it in oil, apply it to the area, and let the woman lie flat each day so that it does not heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the sinew is hard and thick, you must scrape it like a leaf of laurel.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the boil is flesh-born, suspend it with hot water and scrape it; and have medicines that stop bleeding, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense mixed with egg yolk. Then apply a bandage of wide linen so that the wound cannot heal. And let this be done for a long time, then cover it with dry linen cloth. Then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	But when flesh-born matter comes in the wound, it must be scraped according to this manner, unless it is an inflamed abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an inflamed abscess that is in the wound, one should not touch it with iron.
des emorroides	"For hemorrhoids"
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that usually do not bleed, and when hemorrhoids are old they become hard. We have already mentioned in the division their likenesses, signs, and now I will say those that require treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and piles, when they are deeply buried in the marrow, and cannot be felt, then it is not cured by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the mouth of the anus, which can be felt, those can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you should put the woman in a cold house, then raise the altar with forceps, and grasp it at its roots with tweezers, then sprinkle powder of medicines that stop bleeding, such as acacia and dragon's blood and frankincense, and similar things; then place her feet at the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water. And if there is bleeding, then make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and gall nuts and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster with it on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops bleeding, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not so, then apply cupping glasses to the back and breasts without pricking; then take linen, and wet it in plantain juice or in buckthorn juice with old wine, and apply to the location.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess rests, then cure the location with ointment until it is clean; and that called "albathir" is red, resembling a bitter apple head, so you should cover it as I have described the telu; and then cure until it is clean.
des apostemes de la marris	Of boils of the belly
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses occur in the flesh, such as cancer and bony abscesses, herpes and boils, fistulas and hemorrhoids, hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, I must say in this treatise about the hot abscess that occurs in the flesh, which is not one of those that grow like boils; and if you wish to know the work of iron, look whether the abscess is hot at its beginning and filled with heat and fever, and becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hasten to pierce, but make it burn until the pain is alleviated; and then make the patient sit on a seat, and have two small seats where they can recline, and support their back and bring their feet together at the level of the knee; and let their thighs be spread apart, and put their arms under their knees, and tie them securely with a good tie; then suck out the bile towards the right side, and introduce the instrument with which one operates on the mouth of the bladder, about which there will come later its form; and it is necessary that when you are introducing this instrument, you first insert the reed to know the depth of the bladder, so that what enters from the instrument does not go deeper than it should, nor burn the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then cover the depth of the bladder with rags, so that the instrument does not hurt them; and it is necessary that they put the horn of the instrument above, and that they grease the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	When the abscess opens, and it is cut with a soft hand, then you must cover it at the head, with a warm linen cloth; and when the bowels are empty, then you must put moistened bandages in oil of rose or dried green oil into the wound; and place the bandage far from the wound, and put behind it clean linen soaked in water or myrrh cooked until boiled; then treat after two days with suitable ointment until healed; and sometimes lift the bandage and the wound by an enema of water and honey, then of water in which lilies and coltsfoot are cooked.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is full of matter, you must beware of cauterizing with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is first necessary that the midwife knows the form of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman straining downwards, and desires to smell the air: then the child hastens to come out. Know then that this childbirth is according to nature's form, and the waters issue from its head, with the afterbirth. And when you see these signs, it is necessary to press gently on her belly so that the child comes out quickly; for when it settles on its head, the afterbirth is with it, and the womb is cleansed of its superfluities by good cleansing. And one that comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it sometimes happens that [the dislocation] comes upon his feet, and the body or shoulder is fiery, and the hands, or it comes upon his belly, or sometimes, and occasionally they are turned over his neck, and by other evil forms; thus it is necessary for the bath attendant to be wise and skillful in these matters, and wary of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one must help [the patient].
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out naturally on its head and the woman is giving birth with difficulty, and her strength is weak, then let her sit on a stool or have women hold her up; and let the nature of oil or fenugreek be cooked, and then put the little spatumile between her thighs, of which this is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and tear open the membranes and scrape with its nail until the moisture inside comes out; and press on the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then the woman must be cleansed with a powder made of fenugreek mixed with oil of sesame; then she should inhale the fumes of costus and sneeze, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will be born.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands come out fiery, then you must gently and gradually push them back in; and if they cannot be put back in, then place the woman on a seat, and raise her feet high; then tip the seat onto the ground, making sure that she does not fall with the tipping; and if the hands still cannot go in and the child dies, then cut off the hands at the joint mentioned above and extract the child, and set everything back in place evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the childbirth upon its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes forth upon its feet, then lift it up gently; and then turn it a little by little until it is even; then take one of its feet and extend it gently.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When it jumps up to the thighs, then command it to grasp [itself], and make it sneeze with condition; if it leaps forth, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if he does not jump as we have said, then turn him bit by bit until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will be easy
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not leap forth as we have said, then take musk, aloe, and sesame oil, and melted gum, and grind them together in one mortar; and put this ointment on the nature of the woman inside and outside, then make her sit in hot water up to below the ribs; and when she is moistened below, give her a collar of myrrh, and put it below, and leave it for an hour; then make her sit on a seat, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and gently press her belly, for the child will now leap forth.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	place the exit of the child upon her knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, then the midwife places her hands softly and gently on him. Then she supports him on his neck, and let his feet hang down, and lies him softly on the bed. And folds her hands softly and gently, then takes the hands onto the belly, and removes the cushions from beneath until it is arranged downwards. And if the child does not move, take his feet and move them vigorously, then move your belly upwards, then place your hands there; and raise the child softly and gently; and command the woman to bear down until the child issues forth.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the exit of the child that comes from the side with one hand hanging
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to try to bring back the hand: if one cannot bring it back, then make the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, then make her lie down on the bed, and forcefully raise her legs. Then apply the mustard plaster that I have described; and if she does not give birth, then seat her on the chair, then attempt to bring back the hand. And raise the child according to its natural position, and make it sneeze, and command the woman to bear down until the child issues forth.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the exit of the child upon her neck, with its hands spread out and its face turned towards its mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the servant take his hand, then turn it little by little, and the eye lightly; and when it is even, so put upon the natural muscillaige of altee and oil, as we have said, then instruct her to move little by little; and when you have done this, then let her sit on the seat, and instruct her to sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner for all that remains of the afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When the fire comes in this manner to all of the membrane, then cut the membrane with your fingernail until the moisture is emptied; and if the child falls on its face and neck, then cut from the throat so that it is not retained, and the child dies; then put the child inside until you have placed it as it should be, and instruct the woman to sneeze several times: then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	about the exit of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are often born, and sometimes even three or four; this is not a rare thing, and it happens infrequently.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	There are two strange things, and they do not live long if unnamed; I know this, that they can be multiplied, and are hated by the thief who divides them, which is attached to the throat; and sometimes they also come out naturally like a tooth, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they come out screaming, treat them as we have said, and let the servant be skilled, and do what she does quickly and easily; and do thus as it is worth moving for healing.
de plusors enfans	about several children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the uterus one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, or more up to fifteen, and all are formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise physician, and it is necessary that the servant knows everything about this, because such things can happen; so do according to what is needed.
de l’enfant mort	about a dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman with a dead child or a pregnancy that is not coming out, as I said in the section on divisions, and there is no movement, and you are forced to intervene manually; then you must know if the woman is of good health, and does not have any accident, or if she fears death. Then the woman should be propped up on her back, with her hips tilted down and her legs raised. The servant should hold her thighs with both hands, or tie her to the bed so that she does not slip during the removal of the child. Then rub the mouth of the uterus with moist oils containing musk, fenugreek seeds and linseed, and then the servant should anoint their hands with these oils and musks. Then gently insert them into the uterus, and where they are inserted, press once to make sure it is fitting for this purpose. Make sure that if the child descends feet first, you insert the hook into its legs or hips on both sides; and it is necessary that she holds the hook in her right hand, placing the curve between her left elbow, and inserts it gently with all her hand, inserting the hook into any of these places we have mentioned until the space is empty. And this is the shape of the hook:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then stick against the other side once, or twice if you have need of it, so that the extraction is even; and then stretch them evenly while moving from one side to the other, for easy removal, and let the hooks be tooth-like for holding tightly.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if some part remains, then the surgeon may take some of his fingers dipped in oil and put them into that part, and pull on the other part; and if none remain, then place this hook higher up and do so until it all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other and cannot be pulled back due to tension, then you must wrap the cloth around it until all is out; then cut into the joint of the sole or at the side, and do similarly for the other hand and both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's head is large and it is too tight at the outlet, or has a sharp-pointed bone assembled there, then you must place the spatula spinosum between your fingers, cut off the point, and extract the bone; or bore it with the instrument called "almidach", the shape of which comes with the tools in the chapter that follows this one. Do likewise if the child has a naturally large head; and then pull out the bones with forceps, and if the head does not emerge even with great effort, cut it open until the moisture from the pit outlet emerges; and if it cannot come out, then cut it off piece by piece as you are able; and if it is swollen in the belly or below the ribs, then you must pierce through it until the moisture flows forth.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	"If the child is standing on its feet and the attraction is light, and the direction towards the mouth of the womb is easy,"
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	If it is stuck in the belly or breast, you must pull it out with a cloth wrapped around your hand; and cut the belly or breast until the moisture that's there flows away; and if other members are removed but the head remains, then put your hand deep into the marrow, and draw it up to the mouth of the marrow; then put in one or two onions, and boil them well; and if the mouth of the marrow is narrowed by a hot abscess that has come, do not work there, rather apply moist and greasy things; and use dressings, and such have been softened in warm water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	If the child is lying on its side and you cannot set it right, then treat it as we have said for a living child; but if there is no power left, then draw it forth in pieces, leaving nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And once you have done this, if hot abscesses come in the marrow, then use the dressings we have mentioned; and if blood comes flowing, let it be put into strained water, and apply other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	"I saw a woman whose belly was bitten by one child, then another came out on top of it and killed the other."
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	"After some time, an abscess formed in her cheek and swelled until it opened, and then there was a great flow of pus."
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	"I was called to heal her, but I thought for a long time and could not hold the wound closed."
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	"I applied a plaster with strong attraction, and after some days one bone came out, and later another one did as well."
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	"I was very amazed because the belly has no bones."
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	"So I thought that they were the bones of a dead child."
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I opened the wound and removed many bones until the woman was much improved. The woman lived for a long time afterwards, but occasionally a little bit of bone would come out of its place; and I recorded this chapter only because when masters find something unusual, they should know how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	"How to return the womb to its place"
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	"Next comes the figure of the press, with which books are printed; and at two turns around the two keys of the two lions."
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns should be more slender than the restraint and made of ebony or boxwood. The mouth of the wood should be two fingers wide, and the edges of the wood one and a half palms long. And there should be two joints of the same wood in the middle, each closed on one end with half a palm's length or a little more; and these two joints are placed in the mouth of the mortise to open it when the two horns are turned.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more slender and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood wood, resembling a pair of pliers. It has two joints on each end, one palm long and two fingers wide. When you want to open the mortise with this tool, make the woman lie down on her back, legs apart, then insert the two ends of the tool into the mortise together, holding the head of the tool under her thighs. Then open your hand according to the size of the tool, as you would with pliers, opening the mouth of the mortise until it reaches the desired width.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	"These instruments are all mounted and have many similar forms. When the master has prepared them, the faster he works, the higher they are raised for men because of their size."
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	"Do not disdain any instrument that you have not prepared, for their necessity cannot be excused."
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	If labor is prolonged during childbirth, then you should instruct the woman to hold her breath and then have her sneeze with a cloth on her mouth and nose; if she faints from this, it is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If this does not work, take a pot, make a hole in the lid, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the woman, such as calamint, rue, anise, camomile, celery, and centory; cook these herbs or some of them in water over the fire. Then place one end of a tube in the pot and the other end in the woman's mouth, holding it until the vapors enter her. Then have her sneeze as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	"If the afterbirth comes out quickly."
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	If she remains in this condition afterward and is not delivered yet, command the midwife to wet her left hand in sesame oil or musk from althea and then insert it into the woman's genital area. When she finds the secondine, grasp it gently and pull it straight down little by little so that the woman does not fall during extraction; but rather move it gently to the right and left, and then cut it. It will come out and separate.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the womb is narrow and tightened, we have spoken about sneezing remedies and herb fumigation. But if it does not yield from any of these, then ensure that you do not err in milking; rather, what is at the mouth of the womb should be tied to the woman's thigh, then perform a sitz bath with tetrapharmacon oil. She will then pass it and recover, and she will have heat. But nonetheless, when she passes, there may come a foul odor in her stomach and head, causing her distress.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	"Therefore it is necessary to perform fumigations appropriate for this [condition]; some of the ancients have tried fumigation with mustard and dried figs."
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	"The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman to retain the flowers [menstrual flow] and the afterbirth is this:"
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it resembles true sulfur in appearance. Place the refined head over the fire with wide mouths, and perform fumigation on the coals until the pitch is wasted, then begin again.
de percier lou fondement	"to pierce the anus"
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born without their anus being pierced, instead it is obstructed by a thin membrane. Therefore, the midwife must pierce this membrane with her thumb, taking care not to use a sharp awl, and guard against touching the wound. Then apply warm cloths soaked in wine and oil until healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	"And if you doubt that [the anus] will not open up again, then place a small tube made of lead into the perforation and leave it there for several days, removing it when the child is ready to go to bed."
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	"And sometimes this obstruction comes from a sudden wound or abscess; it is necessary to cover this sudden [wound]: if it is cured, then treat it as we have said for the lead tube."
de la fistule dou fondement	"of a fistula of the anus"
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that arise beneath the fundament are nodular, and growths that occur near the fundament defluxion, or in the space of the two buttocks, so there is one fistula or more; and when this nodule is ancient, it works, and increases moist, white or subtle bowels, and sometimes these fistulas persist; and they are known by those who have a discharge or windy noise when the patient has an evacuation, and sometimes some worms come out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	"And there are fistulas which penetrate as far as the bladder and as far as halfway along the penis; and they reach as far as the hip joint and as far as the thigh."
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the persistent fistula under the fundament, and not persistent; and it is that you place your two index fingers on the fundament, and insert a thin needle of brass or iron into the fistula when there is no torsion.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is torsion, then insert a thin probe of lead or horsehair until you feel the probe or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and no discharge or windy noise or worm comes out through the hole as we have said: know that it does not pierce; so hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	"And when the fistula is persistent as far as the bladder or as far as the passage of urine, then urine comes out and it cannot be healed by medications."
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it pierces as far as the joint of the thigh, then the coming tent is until there; if there is no tortuosity and the invention of pain around it, then it is that it leaves quickly, and medicine or ointment is useless; and in these Persian fistulas there is no cure except labor, and vanity of foolish physicians who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	For that which is not Persian and is not ancient, there is hope of health through iron, as I have experienced. And it should be that the patient lies on their back in your hands; raise the legs until they reach the thighs, incline them toward the belly; then insert a tent of brass or lead if there is tortuosity, until you know where the tent comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the fundament, then you must insert your two index fingers there, if you then sense that the tent has pierced; and if you feel between your fingers either the syphon or flesh, then know that it is Persian; do not work on it unless it can be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	Some say it is possible to heal certain wounds, but this rarely happens. And the aid given there involves heating a fine cautery according to the width of the fistula, as mentioned before; and place it hot into the fistula until it reaches the base; do this twice or three times until you know that the broken veins are burnt, which resemble an feathers quill; then dress with warm ointment until that vein breaks free, then apply a bandage with healing ointment between skin and wound.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If healed this way, it's good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If not healed this way, it cannot be otherwise. And if the bandage enters but does not reach the base of the hand that is at the base, and there is a thick covering of skin or fat between your two fingers, and you see the fistula where the covering of the heart comes out; then cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push the bandage ahead, and afterwards apply the cautery until it reaches the head of the bandage; and the bandage will be delivered, and fall away; then burn those broken veins that resemble a feathers quill, and leave nothing behind.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	"And if the skin is thin and cuts between you and your work, then cauterize it with fire or strong medication."
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the cautery of fire brings together two things: namely, the burning of these adjacent parts, and the staunching of blood and the drying up of moisture. Then treat moist wounds with butter or crushed plants until the place becomes soft, and let the burned flesh come out in this softness. Then dress the wound with bandages compressing hard flesh, and these medicines should be dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	"For when it is restored, then it is healed and does not return again."
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	"And if a fistula comes from deep within the anus and is far from the body, insert your two fingers into the anus and search for it."
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the wound, and between two skins or between skin and flesh where it is about to burst, there should be no force except through trust and hope, by administering one of these three methods: either cauterize it as we have said, or cut it until it reaches bottom, or if you can't do this, put tents on it and treat it as before; but don't go too deep lest you cut the tissue that holds the fundament, and let evacuation come forth without wanting to. Then dress it as we have said; perhaps it will be cured, or you may remove that covering and cleanse it after it has been cut near the fundament, either with a tent or some other pointed instrument. Then wash the torn flesh that is in the wound as much as you can, then strive to restore the wound and keep the fistula away from the fundament: this will be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this manner: when you insert the tent into the fistula, and it is located on the side towards the base near the skin above, then take a pierced tent at the head according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I twist one thread into two, and insert the tube along with all the thread into the fistula until it reaches the top
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it pierces into the margin of the base inside, then pull out the thread from that pierced tent, so that you insert your two fingers into the base; and pull the head of the thread, and bring the two heads together, and bind them tightly to each other, and leave them for one or two days; and tighten it sometimes until the threads cut through these skins that are between them and fall off; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not open on its own, then make an opening for it in all ways that you can, if it is not too deep
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not necessary to break open a fistula that is too deep, and then heal it as we have said until it is clean
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spine spatula used to open a fistula is very sharp at one end and cutting, but not sharp on the other end so that it does not cut what should not be cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: those that are inside the fundament, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and there is always blood issuing from them, and there may be one or more of them, and they defy the fundament and the head of the fundament; but those that defy so have a little moisture, and there is sometimes a little yellow water or some blood, and they have the color of flesh; and the treatment for those who have hemorrhoids inside the fundament, is that you instruct the patient to strain for going to the privy until the fundament pushes them out, and then grasp the threads with tweezers, or hold them with your nail, then cut them at their roots; and if the nails cannot hold them due to moisture, then grasp them with a thread, or cotton, or a piece of chamlet; and pull them out with two fingers, then cut them, and powder over some warm powders that are in place of cautery; or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cautery, then treat them with other treatments until they are healed; and if the fundament cannot push them out, then administer to the patient a biting and sharp clyster for washing what is inside the fundament so that it can come out openly; when the patient strains, and if the threads are outside the fundament, then treatment is easy; and it is that you grasp them with your nail or tweezers, and cut them, then treat them as we have said until they are healed, and that there may be no incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you stitch according to this manner: take one thread of wool and put it into a needle, then pull the thread upwards and make the needle pierce from the other side, then turn both ends of the thread underneath the needle, and let it be loose; and draw the thread tightly, then tie the knot, and remove the needle, and do so for all the others, and leave one to correct the superfluity of blood. Then place on the foundation a piece of cloth moistened in rose oil or cerote, and put it on the foundation, and instruct the patient that they rest; and then let them lie until they have fallen asleep, and when they have fallen asleep, then heal them with ointment and other remedies until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	Regarding the drying of phlegm in the foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is a drying of phlegm in the intestines, either due to constriction of nature or when the disease is old and medicines are ineffective
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	You must scrape off with the point of a spatula or your nail the scab that has formed on top, so that it does not become moistened. Then heal it until it is solid as it should be; and if it cannot heal, then start scraping again more forcefully than before until it is completely healed and the scab is removed. Then heal it until it is completely healed.
dou fremit	trembles
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ants are small creatures that appear before the body, and they move very deeply; sometimes they feel cold, and one feels them like a shiver of death, which comes to all parts of the body, but more so in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the treatment is: take a quill of an eagle's feather or a strong vulture's feather and place it upon the shivering sensation such that the circle surrounds the shivering entirely; then twist your hand around the entire feather until you grasp the shivering from its root and push it deeply in, grasping it from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	"And if you see, do this with a reed or iron rod in accordance with this form, and let it be thin below and tapering above:"
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	"Do not pierce it, so that you can hold the two [joints] together and press them tightly. And if you see fit, cauterize the trembling as is described in the chapter on cautery."
de la forme dou clistere	"of the form of the clyster"
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	"Sometimes a silver or steel clyster is made, sometimes one of molten brass or iron; and sometimes they are made of these small or large instruments, according to their size."
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	"Those that are used in the treatment of children and those who are weak and painful are small."
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	"The form of the small and large clyster is as follows: wide where the belly is tied in this manner:"
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is a blockage or the belly is tied up as you see it, and the head is pierced inside; and there are two holes on one side and one hole on the other; and the belly where medicine is placed in a beast's bladder or parchment, and is pierced all around with small holes, and there is one space between each hole, then insert strong thread of coarse yarn twisted into an X or wound around, and bind the belly like a goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie it at the instrument beforehand with a strong thread, then administer the enema; this is the form of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medication not be too hot nor too cold, and grease the head of the enema with oil or almond nut cream or similar substance, then insert it gently; then the minister squeezes with both hands until it is all squeezed out, then remove the enema, and the patient lifts their legs to the side, and if the medication wants to come out, let it come out as much as possible; and if it stays in for a whole night, it will be of greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if you perform a clyster in the case of diarrhea of the belly, and the medicine rushes out quickly, then recommence it until it is retained."
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the fundament or abscess, then let the enema be as thin as for a child; and this is the shape of the thin enema upon which the skin should be restrained:
des plaies	"wounds"
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	"We have already spoken in the division about the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments for hands and medicines according to their completion."
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	"I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made."
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by cutting of stone, and cutting with sword and knife, or lance or club or dart, or similar things; and they are made according to the places on the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or head, or thigh, or belly, or liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and will begin with simple head wounds, for the reminder will come in its own chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, you should take care if it's from a blow with a stone or similar things, and if the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you doubt the raising of a hot boil: immediately cleanse it with cold water especially if there is little blood coming from the wound, and let the cleansing be opposite to the wounded part; and have the patient abstain from wine and rich foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it will not cleanse itself, then thin down his diet and do not let him drink wine or eat meat; and place on the wound, if hot boils come, cotton moistened in rose oil alone, or in astringent wine. And if there is no hot boil, then place on the fresh wound with all its blood, without moving it through the air, powder which I will mention a bit later; and if the wound has moved, then place some ointments until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	"And if the wound is large, like a sword cut or similar ones, and its lips cannot be brought together by tying, then bring them together with stitches, as I will tell you about in the treatment of abdominal wounds, regarding stitching."
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone and inflamed, and barely adheres to just a bit, scrape it; then dress the wound with medicine, and replace hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as testicles and cooked wheat, also like poultry and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find putrefaction in the skin, and it does not reach the bone, scrape off all the corruption, and apply fire, then dress it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein that cannot be staunched by medicines alone, tie up the artery; and if you find it dislocated, bind it with a thread; and if this does not help at all, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	"And if these wounds are small and simple, their treatment is easy; and this is what you should do: put in this powder that seals before the air moves it."
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The manner of making the powder is as follows: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, grind it finely, and apply it to the wound, and bind it tightly until it adheres well and joins with all its blood; then tie it firmly, but do not remove the medicine until the wound is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	"Sometimes they do this with quicklime alone, when they do not have incense or dragon's blood, but the air has not moved the wound."
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the burn has moved the wound, especially in summer, then do not put this powder on it; but apply some digested ointments or poultices made of barley flour and water and honey, until it yields; then treat with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if bone fragments come with the wound and it is small, extract them with fine forceps; and I will tell you later about head fractures.
de la plaie dou col	"Regarding wounds on the neck:"
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	"If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one on the head, except that if the nerve of the neck or an artery is cut."
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, there is no other remedy than to leave them alone and not apply anything restrictive, for it harms the nerves and makes them retract; and do not apply anything cold to the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be warm, like warm water washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and cucumber washed likewise in sweet water, and other moist compresses in this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, it should be stitched and bound with bandages until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.
