And if the wounds are deep and have gathered blood and are full of pus, pierce them lower down; and if an artery is cut and there is a flowing of blood, open it up and ligate it and cauterize it if necessary. And if the spine of the neck or the heart is cut, and the conduct is guarded by which the flesh goes, then bind the heart to the windpipe of the neck, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape; and then bind it properly, and leave it for some days, then cure it with healing ointments until it is healed. And if the wound has made an impression on the bone, scrape it out; and if there are fragments of bone, draw them out all if you can, and those which you cannot have, leave them until the wound rots, and cleanse and dress the wound properly. And if the wound is fresh, powder it with the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	If there are bones and fistulas in the wound, treat it as I have said in its chapter
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	Chapter on wounds made by a spear or dagger
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a blow from a lance or knife and the wound is deep, observe whether air enters the wound when the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal. And if it is not deep but is fresh with all its blood, do not apply powder at the first hour nor bind it tightly so that no blood flows back downwards to reach the heart and kill the patient; instead, apply attractive ointment and tie it twice a day. And if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to draw out moisture, and make the patient lie on the wound for three days or four, or more; so that there will be no spasm nor harmful trembling of the heart. And when you see favorable conditions, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Then heal it with dressings and other treatments until it is healed. And if it cannot heal nor close, know then that there is a fistula; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, or worse on the front or back, so its cure is in front; if it's large, stitch it; if it's small, use powder. If it's close to the bone and has chopped pieces, search for the wound, and remove foreign bodies if they're infected; if not infected, let the wound rot until it discharges; other wounds on other limbs are judged similarly as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	on bursting of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the belly is large and medium and small; from a large wound sometimes the intestine or the nerve of the intestines comes out, causing intrusion into it; stitching is more difficult, and sometimes a smaller wound is worse than a larger one, because if one puts the intestines back in piece by piece, they are not put back in place properly. For this reason, a moderate wound is better, because it allows the intestine to be reset in its proper place rather than being moved around like others. Know that there are four ways to suture the belly: two common stitches occur in abdominal suturing, and two other stitches are common for other wounds on the body; however, these stitches are more specific for abdominal suturing, and I will explain each one clearly.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestine has been torn, it is not a difficult thing to reset, this can be done in one of two ways: either because the wound is small, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or one clean cloth in hot water alone, or boil in water with cumin and cyperus and spikenard, and apply the intestine until the swelling has gone; and sometimes use this restricting wine, and drink honey for relief.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling diminishing, moisten the intestine with water or decoction of mallows, for by this the entrance is enlarged somewhat; and if it cannot enter, then slightly open the wound with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is that which involves cutting, which no one should perform without great necessity; and this is the tool for breaking: cut within the curve and do not cut deep; here is the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines protrude, then replace them according to their natural form in their proper place if you have the ability, for this is valuable.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large and it is below the belly, make the patient lie on their back, with legs higher than their head. If it's under the belly, raise the head and chest more than the lower parts; similarly, if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, arrange so that the wounded part is higher than the other; thus must it be arranged for large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	In small wounds, first prepare what you're equipped with, then have between your hands one pitiful servant who will wipe away all the discharge with their hand and bring together the lips. This is the common way of suturing: take one or several needles depending on the size of the wound, then leave two fingers' breadth at the head of the wound, and insert a needle with good strong thread; pierce both sides of the skin with both sides of the sinew beneath it until you pierce through that part, then bring together both heads of the sinew in four places; then tie them together with doubled thread around the needle on both sides, then bring together both sides of the wound neatly, and leave two fingers' breadth at the head of the wound, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you did the first needle, and continue doing this according to how many needles you need until all the wound is closed. The needles should be medium-sized, between thin and thick, for too-thin needles cut all the flesh, and too-thick ones cannot enter well: therefore they must be medium-sized; also do not insert the needles too deeply into the flesh and skin lest they cut open the wound before it's stitched up; then cut off the heads of the needles so they don't harm the patient when sleeping, and put tents or bandages on the needleheads to keep them in place, leaving them until the wound is healed. This method of stitching with needles is more useful for small wounds, as one or two needles suffice there. The second method of stitching is common: bring together both sides of the skin and both sides of the sinew together with a needle with good medium thread; when you've pierced all four places together, then pull the needle back to where you started in the manner one sews cloth, placing the thickness of a finger's width between each stitch. This stitching is used by men, and I stitched up a wound that one man had in his belly which was cut by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm's width long, and two palms' worth of intestines were protruding, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I reset his intestines after it had been outside for 24 hours, and the wound healed in 15 days. I treated it, and it was free from infection.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the physician had judged that he would die, but it was a miracle. I did not treat it with any ointment, as I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine. Instead, I placed old cotton on the wound twice daily and washed it with honey water until it was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	I will tell you the two proper ways to stitch: take the needle and insert it from outside until it pierces inside. Once it has pierced through evenly, place the thread on the needle or tie it where you inserted the needle, then pierce it again from inside out. The technique of this stitch is like how furriers sew furs, leaving the thread once on one side and picking it up again on the other until the entire stitch is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of suturing, which Galen describes accurately, is as follows: some people assemble the two parts naturally and apply one end of the thread to the other end in this manner: insert a needle near one edge of the wound, pierce only that spot, leaving both ends of the thread; then turn the needle and pierce it from the outside until it reaches the inside at both ends of the thread; then pierce both through the outer layer to the inner layer at two other points on the opposite side of the wound. This is the correct method of suturing and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this word, and some testify that when sewing the belly, one should use two needles with thread in each. One needle should be placed on one side and the other on the other, like those who sew hides. Know that when a rupture is inside the belly, the stitching is more difficult than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, before the ars has moved it, then replace the intestine and the skin; then put powder of wormwood on it, and if the ars has moved, put some ointment that is present until the wound bows; and close the stitches, and let them be sewed the sifac and the mirach; then treat the wound as others until it is healthy; and if you do not have medicines, put on it immediately when it begins to swell, old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healthy.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	But in many dispositions where wounds are simple, you have no need for other medicine; and if you doubt that the wound does not communicate with the principal members, then it is necessary to moisten light linen in warm tempered oil or rose oil, and put it around the joints and under the armpits; and if there is pain or corruption in the bowels, which happens often, then cleanse it with black wine tincture, especially if corruption reaches the intestines; and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines called "jejunum" cannot heal when injured due to the thinness of its veins and the delicacy of the entire body, as well as its closeness in nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	If the intestine jumps out of the wound, push it back in like the intestines while it is fresh; and if it is old and has turned green or black, tie off the area that is black to prevent blood flow, as there are veins and arteries present. Then cut what is between the ties, and hold the two ends hanging from the bottom part of the wound until the intestine falls back into place, allowing for easier extraction; then close the wound.
de la routure dou boueil	of the wound's opening
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	If the intestines are torn and the wound is small, it can sometimes be restored in some people, as I saw one man who was pierced in the stomach by a lance; his wound was on the right side of the stomach, became inflamed, and turned into a fistula. The digestive contents and wind leaked out, but I treated it according to my ability, without ceasing until he was healed, with the site well joined together.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him bound, I doubted that the patient had ill in his belly; but there was no harm, and he remained in better condition, eating and drinking. And some surgeons said that if there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this manner: take large thorns, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the thorn has opened its mouth, place it on both lips so that it draws its mouth shut; then cut off the head, and this holds so that it cannot untie, then put another thorn afterward in the same manner as before until the wound is completely closed.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	And if the head is in the intestine and there is no harm to the patient, then one can tie the intestine with a thin thread of gut taken from an animal's intestine, like this: take the head of this gut that is very skinned, and then tie at the head of this gut a thin twisted linen thread, then insert the thread into the needle and cut the intestine, and draw it back together; and this manner of suturing with a thread is not futile but according to the path of trust and hope. And if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the larger intestines, there is no remedy nor health except for skillfulness.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know this: any wound or abscess that grows old is universally called a "fistula", and the same goes for one that is hollowed out and caves in.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is truly a broken and white nodule, where no pain is felt, and it is also hollow like the feathers of a bird; sometimes it opens clear and wide, sometimes thick; sometimes small, sometimes large. I have spoken about this in the section on wounds: any wound that does not heal has flesh because of one of these eight causes: either due to the thinness or evilness of blood or body; or because there is hard flesh inside and on its lips that prevents flesh from growing; or because it is too hollowed out; or because the area is obstructed, and the material is of poor quality; or because the medicine used for treatment was not good; or because corruption is in a pestilential manner; or because digestion is tardy by nature in that region and healing is delayed, or because there are veins or bones present. I have already shown all these causes, their signs, and their treatments using medicines in this section.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	But now I must tell you about the treatment of fistula that is performed by manual labor.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins and arteries, nerves, or the face, intestines, bladder, ribs, spine, or any joint of the hands or feet; and also those that affect the principal property of the member.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all fistulas of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is nothing but effort and ignorance. And if there is a fistula that does not extend to the location I mentioned, and you trust in its cure and recognize it, then take a tent of brass or iron, if the fistula is straight, use it to search for it; and if the fistula is crooked, search with a subtle tent made of lead, for lead bends around the twistiness. And if the fistula has many openings and you cannot search well by tents, then rinse it with a clyster through one of the openings, for moisture runs from one opening to another and cleanses it. Then cut towards your power, so that you know if there is bone or nerve inside, and how deep it goes, and ask the patient carefully about the pain they feel when you press on their hand, and where they feel it. And once you truly know where it is, whether it is far from a joint, nerve, artery, vein, or any of the places I mentioned earlier, then cut according to what I have told you, remove the fracture and rotten flesh inside, and then cure it until it is healed. And if the fistula is very deep in the right place, then cut as deeply as you can, then insert moist tents into hot medicine water, and put them up to the head of the fistula until the medicine eats away at the excess that remains at the bottom. Then apply warming ointments made from healthy flesh until it is healed. And if it is not healed by this method, cauterize it as we have said. And if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerve does not trouble the main member as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then cleanse it until all corruption is removed, then treat the surrounding flesh until it is clean; and if it is not clean, and returns to its former state, know that you have not yet reached the bottom: uncover and search until you reach the bottom, and remove all corruption, then restore it to its place; and if it is thus clean, that is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep, so you cannot reach it: there is no other remedy but to leave it to nature. And if there are some small corrupted bones and you can grasp them with forceps, then remove them with the appropriate instrument; and if there are many bones, remove them all, leaving none behind. And if moisture hinders you, without error or fear, cut away moisture and flesh, and release the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, then put on the wound something irritating to cause corruption, and leave it until the spot is corrupted all around the bones, and then they will come out more easily; and if it's a large bone, like that of the leg or thigh, then continue causing corruption until all the blackness is gone, then restore the wound; and if there is much corruption which comes near to the marrow of the bone; it must be cut down to the corruption, and then treated until it is sound. And I will tell you about a fistula that happened to one man in his leg, so that you may take example and aid from this in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was once a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to some cause that came from within the body, so much so that matter gathered in the leg and it swelled with a large abscess. There was no apparent reason to open it; but foolish doctors operated on it until the abscess opened, and they removed many matters from it, and it became a fistula, and there were many holes through which they poured boiling water and body moisture onto his flesh. Many doctors tried to treat him for about two years, and none of them had any skill in this art, so I was called upon, and when I saw the young man's leg and the medicines used to treat it, and what flowed out of the holes in great quantities, I saw that the young man's flesh became red and had a yellowish hue.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these openings, then sought all the openings, and found that one came against another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then hurried and cut into one of the openings until I discovered a part of the bone, which was corrupted and pierced, with corruption reaching to the bone within; I scraped off what appeared of the corrupted bone, believing there would be no other corruption but that which I removed; and began treating the wound with healing medicines over a long time, yet it did not heal. And then I resumed, discovering the bone as before, finding the corruption continued in the bone, which I scraped off and removed, intending to heal the area. But I could not do so until I cut around about a palm's width of the bone, and pulled it out entirely, then restored it with medicines; it was soon healed and sound, but still needed further work due to the patient's weakness, which he could not endure, and his fear of death.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood often occurred, but he was entirely healed, and in place of the bone grew hard flesh, and his condition was good with no harm or opposition at all, neither coming nor going.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated like this: Take linen, and stretch it at the head of the exposed bone, and command that it be held up high; and take another thicker lien of linen than the first, and tie it over the flesh which is on top of the bone, and hold the head so that you can pull away the rotting flesh below, and uncover the flesh above where you wish to see, so that the bone does not wound the flesh; and put a brand or hot stone under the bone to move away the rotting flesh; and this should be done until one can see and feel the corruption, and still again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is decayed and does not appear, and the decay is in the middle or in one part, then uncover all the flesh. Then place a brand beneath, and then use a chisel to span the decay from one part to another, with the chisel's length equal to that of the decay as we have said; and if the decay is at the joint, cut away the decayed joint and chisel the bone that contains it from the other side; and if the decay is in the continuity of two joints, there is no other option but to cut; and if the decay is in the hand's wrist or foot's ankle, that is very serious indeed, but nonetheless you must inquire about this decay how it appears; and cleanse it in all possible ways without harming veins or nerves; and know that many tools are needed for cutting these bones, according to their arrangement, appearance from above, thickness and fineness, size and smallness, hardness; and therefore one must prepare his instruments suitable for each kind of operation; and know that the work will show you the instrument you need according to your knowledge in this art and testimony of disease manners; so consider carefully the instrument you need according to what is necessary.
dou feu	Fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head putrefies either due to internal causes or due to lack; and when you have treated this corruption with medicines but they do not help, then you must cover that limb up to the place where the corruption starts, so that the patient may escape from death through this, or from the greater evil of loss of limb; and the sign is that the limb becomes black as if it has been burned by fire, and afterwards, the corruption spreads limb by limb, affecting the whole body. So act quickly, and if it is due to the sting of venomous beasts such as sea scorptions or snakes and similar creatures, cover the head of the two fingers, but do not let it spread up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it reaches the hand, cover at the joint so that corruption does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, cover at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, death is certain, and no external remedies however powerful can help. And do likewise when corruption comes to the foot: if it reaches the first joint, cover after the other joint; and if it reaches the foot, cover all the foot; and if it rises up the leg, cover at the knee joint. And if it goes above the knee, there is no other remedy than letting the patient die. The manner of covering or binding the limb is as follows: tie it above and below with cloths, and extend some servants one on each side of the lower tie, and others on each side of the upper tie, and cut away the flesh that is between the two ties with a broad knife until the bone is bare. Then cover with wool or oilcloth, and place linen cloths on either side so that the covering does not touch the healthy part, and bring no other injury or abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you operate, cauterize the spot immediately, or apply some constraining powders; then return to your treatment until it is complete, then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage, and care for it until it heals. And I will tell you what happened to a man in great peril: his leg became blackened as if burnt by fire, and this corrosion first appeared on his knee joint, spreading throughout the entire leg. When the man saw the corruption, he quickly cut off his leg and recovered; but many years later, the corruption reappeared at his hand's knuckle, and he came to me. I applied repulsive substances after cleaning his body, but the corruptions could not stop. He then wished that I amputate his hand, but I did not want to, as I hoped to repel the matter; and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he might die, for his strength was weak. So he completely despaired and returned to his land, quickly cutting off his hand himself and recovering. And I tell this story only so that others may know what to do in such a case.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	No comment.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	A boil sometimes appears in a fleshy spot and remains for such a long time that it forms a large gathering of skin; then it becomes round and pierces, and the skin jumps away, leaving the spot empty like a vessel. The skin above it is as thin as gauze, and it does not penetrate to the bone or nerve. Such an illness is called 'boil' and not 'fistula'; but if it extends so deeply that it reaches the bone inside, then it is called 'fistula'. And its cure is thus: if you have confidence that the skin will become corrupted and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, then perform a clyster thus...
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	When the bowel is deep, so let not flesh enter there; and if you cannot cover the chest below as you wish, arrange it in such a manner that the bowel moves to the lowest place where it is, for when the bowel is deep, so let not flesh enter there, and if you cannot cover the chest below as you wish, arrange it in this way: that the bowel moves easily downward, and leave nothing of the bowel; and take medicines consolidative to put on the skin, and stretch over the linen cloth that covers all the skin; then cut forcefully towards the opening of the chest a little wider than the first, since stretching soft ointment on the other cloth according to the quantity of the opening, and place it on the opening of the skin to alleviate the bowel, and do not remove the outer large cloth until after many days once; and that which is on the opening of the chest, often remove it to remove the bowel, and know what comes from the bowel, if it's venom or little or enough, or digested, or undigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been thus extended and you see the nature that jumps on the opening of the skin, know that the chest is already healed, and approaches health; and then untie it in the morning, or the third day, and when you untie the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast becomes painful and swollen after many days, know that the breast is not healed yet.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	Furthermore, if subtle poisons remain after a long time, do not despair of health, for recovery approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	If there are people whose wounds take a long time to heal or those that do well from the opposite treatment; and if undigested food jumps from the stomach after many days without the stomach hurting; and if the stomach takes a long time to digest and is distant, apply drying medicines in substance and virtue like diachylon ointment, for there is much vitriol in it, which is the last medicine. Take diachylon ointment made with rose oil and red vinegar of equal substance; then cook and use it. The same can be done with cooked honey when diachylon ointment is not available, or take myrrh and aloes and incense, grind them, make a powder, put it on the honey while it's on the fire, and then apply it to the cloth and press it onto the stomach. Sometimes aristolochia longa and celery root are administered, which is also like farina of cyperus and centory; use simples or compounds: grind them, make a powder, put it on the honey mentioned before, and use it. If the cure takes a long time and isn't cured by this treatment, know that the corruption has gone deep and has impressed upon the bone, the hard members, or the ligaments; then apply the cure for fistulas as we have said earlier.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the aposteme of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Pustule is a boil that arises beneath the nail of the little finger of the hand, or of the foot, or sometimes arises in other toes; and when it becomes elderly, and no attention is paid to it, then comes a thick boil, and runs and eats away so much that it reaches the root of the nail, and sometimes eats it all away; and the corruption goes as far as the bone, until there comes stinking pain, and the head of the toe is swollen, and the color is yellow.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	If the treatment does not help as we have said in the section on it, then you must cut away with iron all the excess that remains of the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is very helpful if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy. But if the nail presses on the flesh and begins to hurt, and causes a sore, then you must put under the nail that hurts the flesh, and lift it up, and cut away that subtle and thin flesh lightly, and put burning medicines on the remaining flesh to remove all of it; then treat with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it off and cauterize with fire, for as long as the corrupted bone remains there, it cannot heal; and if you see both being corrupted, cut off one first just like it was mentioned earlier, then treat until it heals; and if it's infected and inflamed causing great pain, you must heal it first; then cut the corner of the hip bone diagonally from above, making sure the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; if this happens, put something on it to soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain in the wrist
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	Some men are sometimes born with both feet joined together, sometimes they have bones between them, and sometimes there is a nail; sometimes they are born at the root of the joint, where their birth is in some toes.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those born with a web between their toes do not move it, and those born at the joint of the foot sometimes can move it; the cut for those who are fleshy should be made in this way: cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure; so be careful with him.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In one born with or having a deviated anus, it is necessary that you first cut the flesh roundly down to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable saw, then cleanse it until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The dislocations that occur at both hips come either by birth or from a wound, or from burns, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Then you must cut that adhesion so that the parts revert to their natural shapes; then place between two wet cloths or rags soaked in rose oil, so they do not adhere again; or place between two pieces of fine lead until the site is healed as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	"If one's elbow comes apart with the palm of his hand, then cut that bone just like so."
des vils	Of the wicked
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Warts are large veins entwined and filled with melancholic excesses that come from many parts of the body; and they occur more often in legs of those who walk and work and carry than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer to him a purge for the stomach and then the holy oil from the church.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cautery of iron is done in two ways: one is to cut them and draw out the black blood; the other way is to lift the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The cutting is done in this manner: First, raise the leg of hot water very strongly until the thick blood is subtilized. Then, press the leg of the patient from above the hip down to the part below the knee joint; then cut the vein at point I, or II, or III with a wide blade, then lift and pull out black blood by hand from one end to the other, as much as the strength of the patient can bear. Then, let it rest and instruct them to apply black cole plaster around their wound. And repeat the evacuation and cleansing when the veins are full, which harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The raising of the veins is done in this manner: Raise the leg of the patient, especially if it has much hair. Then place it in a bath, and raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red and the veins swell up. If you do not have a bath, heat it by fire first. Cut at the vein towards the long part of the knee's head, or below the ankle joint. Then cover the skin with an ointment, and scrape off the vein from each side until it appears upon touching. It will appear red and black, resembling a white thread when entering the skin. Insert a skewer underneath until it lifts up the vein. Then raise it with another skewer gently, as you did before. Cut again in another place above or below the third joint. Scrape off the skin over the vein until it appears. Then lift it using the skewer, as done previously. Make another cut if necessary, then pull and lift it until it comes out entirely. If you cannot pull it out, insert a needle with strong doubled thread, tie and pull it out. Insert it underneath the skewer, turning your hand from side to side until it all comes out. Ensure it does not break, for if it breaks, it cannot be pulled or lifted out, causing harm to the patient. Once completely treated, place moist wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound's location, and keep it clean until healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must cut it crookedly, but do not chop it; and draw it out as we have mentioned before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the vein is curved, and it does not cut evenly, so that it does not cut into the vein; and it should be thickly curved, for if it were thin, it would cut into the vein, but let it be thick as we have said.
de la voinne civile	Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein runs into the legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and on land where there is no moisture; and sometimes it appears elsewhere besides the legs, which happens due to rot that comes beneath the skin, like how a serpent and worms enter between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the sign of the beginning of this vein is that a very great inflammation comes upon the leg, then the place changes, and the vein begins to protrude forth like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the thigh opens, you must wrap around it a piece of lead from one and a half to two feet in length, and knot it, allowing the lead to hang on the leg; each time it leaks, wrap around the lead again, and knot it. If it is too long, cut off a part, wrap the remaining portion, but do not cut it at its root lest it returns into the flesh, causing an abscess and decay in that place, and causing bad illness. For this reason, it must be treated bit by bit until it reaches the top, leaving nothing on the body; sometimes this vein is as long as five or ten palms, and once a man came to me whose was ten palms long. When you cut it, insert one dart into the opening, pierce it to the bottom so that all of it comes out; empty the matter inside, then bring healing medicines to the place to prevent decay for some days, then treat it as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein is moistened, especially when it opens at the joint of the foot or on the foot, and much blood flows from it, causing it to swell; treat it therefore as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land 'cattle disease', because it often occurs in oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body, ascending and descending, and can be felt as it moves from member to member, until it reaches the skin where it causes swelling; and it is feared because when it travels through the body, it may reach the head, enter the eye by chance, and destroy the eye; and this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being treated and drawn out, one can only remove it while it is moving; therefore, tie the area above and below with a strong, tight bandage, then make an incision and draw it out until the worm dies if it is deeply embedded in the flesh. The greatest harm it causes is when it runs towards the eye, as we have said; and if you see it approaching the head near the eye, press down firmly on the eyebrow below it, then make an incision and draw it out. The patient should use bodily purification with medicinal solutions to dissolve corrupt humors, and avoid eating foods that cause corruption.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of pain which comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called in our land 'vakkiri,' and it is a pain that comes into certain limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; and I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and soon afterwards, I saw it move like a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything, as if it were quicksilver moving from one place to another; the pain departed from that spot, and fixed itself in the shoulder, and then a little while later it spread throughout her body, so much so that it reached the other arm; then she told me that it kept turning around her body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	"I wondered greatly how it could move thus from limb to limb, for I had never seen this illness behave in this manner."
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I had heard many times that pain could indeed move from one place to another, but I had never seen it happen as clearly as in this woman's case; and I thought that this was because the woman had a thin body and visible veins, making the movement of the windiness more apparent. This does not apply to those who are obese, however, with moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain which we have mentioned, then quickly place a hot poultice above and below it, and then cut until that constrained wind escapes its place; cauterize the area; and if you cannot see it with your eyes, cure it with those things that expel winds, such as fetid pills and pills of saffron, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	"Hemorrhoids are various in appearance and according to the parts of the body where they are found."
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	There are various kinds of them, some having large points and others small, some being barbed and others smooth; some have two angles, others have tongues, and some have pieces. And those that fall into any limb do so in two ways: either they strike the principal member itself, such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, kidney, intestines, bladder, and similar members
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls into any place in these members and the signs of death which I will tell you about afterwards appear to you: then you must be careful with the extraction of this arrow because many deaths come afterwards; but if this bad sign does not appear to you and the arrow is not deeply embedded, pull it out and dress the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the arrow striking the brain when it falls and pierces the bone, and leaps forth the sinew that is on top of the brain, is when there is darkness and suddenness and exertion and redness within the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and mixture of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps there is without fever from the nostrils or ears; and perhaps it loses speech and voice; and from the wound flows moist white matter like feathers, and also burns of flesh; and if these signs appear to you, then take care of the treatment, and draw out the arrow if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	And the sign of the arrow striking the heart is that it is near the left nipple, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; and perhaps the arrow moves like a bird's feather, and black blood flows out, and coldness and cold sweat come forth, and fainting: know then without doubt that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	"The signs of a hemorrhoid that affects the lungs include foaming without pain coming out of the wound, swelling of the throat, change in color of the patient, loud sighing, and seeking cold air."
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	"If a hemorrhoid appears on the chest covering near the ribs, there is much wheezing and pain and sighing, and all the shoulders move."
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	"And if a hemorrhoid appears in the stomach, digested food may sometimes come out of the wound."
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	"And if a hemorrhoid appears in the abdomen and dark feces come out of the intestines, then there is no hope of recovery or extraction of the hemorrhoid."
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	"And if a hemorrhoid appears in the bladder and urine flows out with feces and the patient feels strong pain, know that the wound is fatal."
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.
