"Other parts such as the face, neck, throat, shoulders, arms, backbones, thighs, buttocks, legs and similar parts are safe from hemorrhoids in many cases."
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	"When a hemorrhoid appears on a nerve or artery that is not venomous, as happened to me once so that you may do the same if necessary."
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to one that an arrow fell on his ear near the root of the nose. I tried it and drew it out from beneath the ear's fat without causing pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And pulled out an arrow that had fallen into the fat of the eye beneath the eyebrow. The arrow was barbed and could not be reached except for its tip towards the face. It was a large arrow like a Turkish bow, with all its iron light without ears. The eye was healed and no bad accidents occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And pulled an Arab arrow with ears from the throat of a Christian. I cut the barbs and carefully extracted it until it was removed, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And pulled an arrow from a man's belly where it had fallen, and thought he would die. But after thirty days his condition did not change; I cut into the arrow, engaged it, and pulled it out forcefully without causing any bad accidents.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to heal a man who has had an arrow fall upon his back, and the wound became hard; and the arrow remained inside him, without changing its natural position nor causing harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if you wish to heal another man who had an arrow fall upon his face, and the wound became hard; and thus remained without causing great pain.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And an arrow was shot at the king's prince, who had it fall into his neck, inclining somewhat to the right side; and the arrow was entirely buried when I was called for healing three days after it fell.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	With all care, I tried to find it and did not feel it; but he felt pain and discomfort under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought that it was from the tip of the arrow. I put on the place a plaster of atracentum and digestive herbs so that the area would not swell up; and the point of the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I placed the plaster on that day, and reopened the wound again, and the patient remained like this for a long time until he felt the arrowhead one day within his flesh; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied corrosive medicine to the wound for many days until it opened, and I tested it, feeling the tip of the arrowhead where it was stuck; then I continued applying the medicine to the opening of the wound until the head of the arrow became visible. It had been four months since the injury, and then the wound gaped so much that I could insert pliers into it, but I couldn’t pull out the arrowhead by moving it from side to side. So I didn’t give up and kept trying with various instruments until one day I was able to grasp it securely with well-made pliers, as described at the end of this chapter, and extract it, leaving the wound healed.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctors judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored; I then repaired it, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient became entirely healthy.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have told you the method of extracting certain arrows, so that you may base your treatment on what I have not mentioned, for books cannot cover everything; but wise masters compare even small things, and find new works and tools based on what is present or lacking in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows leave the limbs into which they are struck in two ways: either through the opening through which they entered or through another part; and those that exit through where they entered are called 'entering arrows,' and sometimes they exit suddenly.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out suddenly, leave it alone until the flesh around it is ripe and the exit is opened; likewise if it has struck bone and cannot come out, leave it alone for some days and move it gently each day; then it will come out. And if it does not come out, carefully cut all around it with a fine knife until the surrounding area is widened, and then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes as far as one of the brain's ventricles, and some of the symptoms that I have mentioned appear to the patient: then do not pull it out, but leave it there for a few days until it becomes even, because if the arrow reaches so deep, it is fatal.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not reach deep enough to be fatal, and the patient remains for some days without bad symptoms, then prepare to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if it is very deeply stuck and cannot come out otherwise, then you should administer compresses around it, as I have told you; then treat the wound until it is healthy."
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged in place inside the body so that it cannot be seen, then search for it thoroughly; and if you can feel it, pull it out with a suitable instrument. And if you cannot do so because of the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones, nerves, or veins involved, then make the wound larger until it is big enough. Then pull out the arrow if you can, but if it has barbs on which it holds, cut away the flesh that is stuck around it, two parts on each side that you can manage, and then break off or bend back the barbs of the arrow so that you can pull it out; be careful not to break the arrow while pulling it out, as this would cause greater injury.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	"And if you cannot pull it out all at once, leave it until the wound around it is clean, then pull it out, for extraction will be easier."
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood opposes you, then follow what we have said about treatment in its chapter; and beware of incising the nerve and vein, and find out how you can carefully pull out the arrow without risk, either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the position they were in when the arrow struck them, for this is the greatest help there can be, and if you cannot do so, then place them according to what signs indicate to you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	An arrow that comes from elsewhere, where some part of it is visible or the skin is swollen there: cut accordingly until forceps can grasp it, and then extract it: now it is removed.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	"And if it is stuck in the bone, turn your hand around it until it enters the bone, then widen the bone and pull it out."
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be extracted, leave it for now and then resume extraction until it comes out completely; and if the shaft of the arrow remains there, remove it along with the shaft. And if the shaft falls off and you see that pushing is necessary, then administer the hooking tool so that the tip of the arrow enters into the hook of the tool; and then push it out, and if the arrow has hooked itself, then insert the tool's point inward to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow has touched a bone, then you must cut away all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then treat the wound as it should be.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls into the leg or belly or bladder or side, and it is near, and you can cut upon it, then cut it open; and guard yourself from cutting the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then stitch up the wound if necessary; and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	"The shape of forceps used to treat blades is like the beak of a bird, as shown here:"
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	"And there are many kinds of them: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the blade."
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is like the feather of a bird for driving into the tip of the arrow.
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	"The shape of forceps for striking and holding is as follows:"
des voinnes dou cors communes	"for the common veins of the body:"
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	The veins that are visible are thirty-one in number, of which sixteen are on the head: two temporal arteries behind the ears called 'dous herbech'; and two arteries visible in the temples; and two veins in the corners of the eyes called 'aspires'; and one vein in the forehead; and one vein at the nape of the neck; and two jugular veins in the neck; and two veins above the mouth called 'augeherich'.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins commonly used are four in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it runs along the right side, which common people call "the vein of the head"; another is called "the fast", composed of the cephalic and the basilica, which ordinary folk call "the vein of the heart"; and the basilica is on the left side, which they call "the vein of the belly", it runs along the forearm and is the one that appears most obviously on the pit.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvation vein is the vein that lies between the little finger and the ring finger, which has two branches; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one runs below the bend of the pit of the left side, and the second is the saphenous vein on the outside of the right ankle; and the vein called "the nest", which is found at the ankle of the other side; and beneath these are three others in the other leg.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The veins that are behind the ears help with catarrh and headache. The method of letting blood is as follows: raise the patient's head and rub the area where the veins are located with a rough cloth. Then, have the patient tilt their neck back using a vise so that two veins appear behind the ears in two places at the top of the head. Press on these veins with your fingers until you feel the pulse beneath them. Then take a lancet and insert it under the vein up to the bone. Next, lift your hand upwards along the entire length of the vein and cut through both skin and vein using two fingers' width. Make the blood flow out until it is clear enough. Then bandage and tie it tight so that it stops bleeding. I have already discussed incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The letting of blood from the two arteries located in the temples is beneficial for old headaches, sudden migraines, chronic ophthalmia, and the flow of tears. The method is as follows: have the patient tilt their neck back so that both veins appear clearly. Feel the pulse beneath your fingers and then press down firmly. Next, lift your little finger on top of the vein and insert the lancet underneath it. Lift the vein up and cut it, as you did with the other two veins. Let blood flow according to necessity. Then release the patient and place your finger on the vein for an hour before applying cotton. Afterwards, bind it tightly and let it rest until it stops bleeding. We have already spoken about their cauterization and extraction at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bloodletting from the frontal vein is as beneficial as that from the temporal in cases of ancient face diseases, and for migraines and redness. The characteristics are such that the patient strains their neck by twisting until the veins appear; then they take the instrument called "fosseur", here is its form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point upon the vein and strike with your hand or something else, allowing blood to flow according to the amount you desire; then loosen the patient's neck and tie the vein until it is sealed, sometimes using a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, be careful not to tie the bandages too tightly; also heal it diagonally because the bone is nearby, and by chance the bandage might break if it's too thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bleeding from the two veins located in the arms aids the eyes, and helps with dizziness, redness, inflammation of the ear, and face diseases. The characteristics of their bleeding are such that the patient strains their neck by twisting, as before; then bleed them, with the incision being long and wide, but not deep, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the bandage is too thin, it might break; then allow blood to flow until you have enough, and then tie a cotton pad on top and tie it securely.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The juice of the vein of the nose is good for fever, and sudden madness, and diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes on the face, especially when it is chronic. And the qualities of this juice are that the patient strains his neck, then strains his nose with your left hand, and takes a long thin reed, and places it inside the lip in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well there, and the blood will now begin to flow; and do not go too deep, and make the blood flow according to your need, then leave it overnight, for it is quickly restored. And this is the form of the reed.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The juice of both eyelids helps in the extraction of a thorn, and the beginning of measles, and many diseases, and impetigo, and corrosion, and herpes, and eye inflammations. And its qualities are that the patient strains his neck downwards on both sides, as we have said; and let the master stand on top of the patient's head, and the patient sit on one seat, then open the vein of the long one a little widely, then draw blood temperately or as much as needed, then repeat on the other vein, then untie the bandage, and press gently on both veins so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, for the wound to be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	On the healing of limbs
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The treatment for veins above the lips helps with:
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of healing are such that you should make the patient sit before you, and restrain their neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right side of the lip and the other on the left, which can be recognized by their black color and the small black veins around them: therefore cut both of them, and if you do not recognize them or are in doubt, then cut the largest from each side, and do likewise for the two veins that are above and below, as this is one and the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	On healing under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The healing of the veins under the tongue assists after the healing of the cephalic vein, and is used for the narrowing of the throat, and diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth. The qualities of the healer are such that the patient should sit between your hands facing the sun, raise their tongue, and look under each side for a black vein: cut both, but do not go too deep, as the arteries lie underneath.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the arm which are commonly opened in two ways: either by pricking with a broad iron needle or with an olive-shaped, sharp-pointed one called "aneisil"; and they are broad and thin according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	"The shape of the flame of mirt is very well-known, and it is wide as you can see:"
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary for opening the hairy veins filled with thick, visible blood that contain thick and turbid blood; this is the form of the olive-shaped needle:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	"And it is more pointed and sharp, and is for cauterizing small veins where there is thin citrine blood."
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, aids patients with illnesses in the chest, neck, breast, and abdomen. The operator must perform a skillful incision and beware of the artery beneath it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he strikes the artery and blood begins to flow copiously, it must be staunched as I have said; and the needle should not prick but cut like an aiesil.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilisk does not open manifestly, then you must draw it out and change another one; or if you want any vein from it, or if you wish to heal in place of it the vein within the arm: it opens manifestly; and the edge against fire burns, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the place of healing, then before you draw out the arm, touch the place until you feel the pulse; then mark the place above, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein against fire; and be careful not to hit the artery when you see the place swelling, for that is the artery: avoid it therefore.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see something coming out above like urine from a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from the artery: hurry then, and put your hand on firmly, then remove your hand when the bleeding stops, which happens many times; bind the arm and leave it thus, and do not let the patient move it; and be careful, and do not let him move until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	"And if the blood does not stop and you faint, and a physician is not present, then cut the artery if it opens, because its head withdraws. Then stop the bleeding."
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take an escorce of fistice, and split it open, and take one half and bind tightly until the next day; if bleeding stops, good; if not, treat it as we have said with powders that stop blood; and such treatments do not harm in many situations due to the small wound's location and the strength of the arm's binding.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	When opening a vein in the middle, it helps to draw blood from above and below, because it consists of basilica and cephalic veins, as we have said. And the surgeon should beware of the nerve beneath, and if punctured too deeply, and the nerve is found, then swell and the wound may be harmed, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve often appears, but in some men it does not appear due to its thinness, thus you must cauterize it with the needle-shaped instrument; and avoid damaging the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	"And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut it lengthwise."
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The bleeding of the cephalic [vein] helps by drawing blood from the head and aids in cases of eyes; it is necessary to bleed into the olive branch vein or the mirror vein, for this is the safest of all veins, as there is neither nerve nor artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, it is necessary to seek the most convenient place and not worry if one fails at first, then one should begin again. And perhaps some places swell in certain people when bleeding happens for the first time, but it does no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	"The quality of cautery depends on your skill."
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it was never used except to maintain health and prevent future illnesses. And the bleeding should be done in one of the three veins located on the arm: namely, cephalic, basilic, or median basilica; and it should be done at the beginning of Lent when fasting, and in autumn and winter after meals, when signs ofpletion appear; and one should bleed on the first day or third day, after two or three hours into the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The salve given to the sick has no fixed time for application, but when needed by day or night, at all hours and times; it is not necessary to apply this salve to children until they are fourteen years old, nor to pregnant women until four months after conception, up to seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	"Nor should old people over sixty years old be cauterized."
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wishes to be salved in any way, it is necessary that they empty the bowels with a light clyster if there is much retained feces, so that the veins do not draw harmful impurities from the intestines into the principal members. One should not salve oneself while excessively full of food or drunk, until the effects have passed, nor those suffering from dropsy. And one should avoid salving after an attack of colic, vomiting, diarrhea, and multiplication of abortions in women, labor, vigilance, fasting, and similar things. Then refine the humors if the blood is thick, with foods and drinks and medicines, if you have the power to do so. Then enter a bath if nothing prevents it, to refine the blood, and salve yourself from the vein near the left arm pit on the third day, as we have said. And guard against work, effort, lust, and similar things that day. Be cheerful and joyful, and let the salver be taller than the one being salved. The salver should rub the arms twice or thrice, then squeeze the lien gently over the middle, for if it is too tight or loose, the blood cannot flow properly. Then moisten the salve with a drop of old oil, and place the knuckle of the left hand's index finger on the vein below where you wish to salve, so that the vein does not swell or split when struck.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	Because there are veins that flee like tendons from the sinew, and some such are filled with windiness, so that when heat is applied they withdraw and cannot open the vein, and thus one becomes disabled; and if it closes the vein, then the wound is too narrow, therefore the surgeons must be skillful in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens at first, that's good. If not, then begin again a little below or above hastily, if the wound is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the wound is swollen and the patient fears it, let it be for one or two days without binding the arm: perhaps an abscess may form; do not enter a bath, then resume the treatment if he pleases. And if the hole is small or blood flows subtly and you doubt that enough blood is issuing forth, then apply heat directly to that opening and work quickly before the wound swells, for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the vein swollen, do not resume cauterizing, and place a little oil balm over it, for it lightens the body's blood, and in this location oil is better than any other balm. And thus administer oil balm in every cautery of veins to stop the flow of blood; and likewise does it work for triacle and bowels of ox when placed on the location; so that blood becomes more subtle and spread out when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess forms there, which happens often, especially when it is not cauterized except at the time of opening the vein and the cut is small, then hurry and place over the location an espongestone moistened in warm water and wine, and hold it for an hour; and you must do this after the blood stops flowing from the vein. And if a black or green color remains at the location afterwards for some days, it will not harm. And if you see this, place over it something of aloes or myrrh mixed in juice of calamint, mastich, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there appears phlegm and swelling during the supporting of the basilica (vein): therefore put your hand on it, and if you find the wound soft under the pressure of your hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore be sure not to put on anything of those things that we have said, for perhaps the wound may close up the artery; but make one plaster dry to harden the wound, then cure it with another plaster until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw from each person according to the quantity of his strength and the color of his blood
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if it flows abundantly, let it flow until it becomes more subtle; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for one who is full and strong, and has need of bloodletting, that a larger wound be made for him, and the flame be wide; but for one who is weak, the opposite must be done, and he should be let less often, and he should be let by cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of letting is free from loss of blood and injury to nerves, and is worth more than that which is done with a long or wide let.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body fails at bloodletting, it is necessary to give him moistened bread in pomegranate juice; if he is overheated, let three or four times blood be drawn from him. And if he is of cold complexion, before the bloodletting let him eat moistened bread in musk syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints after losing much blood, then it is necessary that he inhales broth of meat, and fragrant subtle syrup, and uses the other things that we have said in the chapter on syncope for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to let out some blood from his arm and be supported again later, when he is weakened by much blood-letting, it is necessary that he should be supported a little at a time according to the quantity of his remaining strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to let out some blood from his arm after the first blood-letting and has a strong body, should be supported again seven hours after the first blood-letting or after nine hours.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to be supported on another part of his body, should be supported on the second day or the third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	If there is much blood inside the body which has already been heated and causes fever; then it is necessary to draw out a large quantity, and widen the opening so that it falls into a basin. Then, when you have corrected all conditions of fainting, place your hand on his pulse as he faints, ensuring that the blood does not fall back into the basin, for this happens many times when the person attending is negligent. And it is not necessary to tie up the arm or press too hard if there are no more veins to draw from, nor to make him extend his arm hastily, for this would be harmful; but let him bleed a second time until he has finished fainting. Or you can cauterize at the point of the flame until the frozen blood at the opening of the vein begins to flow out. Then place some salt soaked in water on it and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has swollen up, let it alone and do not compress it until the inflammation is eased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if there is necessity to draw blood a second time, then let it out in the same vein or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm are supported in place of those in the head because they are composed (i.e., contain many branches).
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of the cauterization is thus: the patient places their hand in hot water until the veins are reddened; then it should be bound moderately, so that the vein appears well; then cut now across, not wide nor long; and let the incision be large, and cauterize near the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot flow out, then place the hand back in hot water, and allow the blood to run into the water until you have enough; and if it is summer, do not place the hand again in hot water, for one places it more often in winter than in summer; and the cauterization of this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are neither artery nor nerve therein.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The cauterization of the saving vein of the right hand is beneficial for all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: constrain the hand, and place it in hot water until the vein swells, so that one may see it; and if you cut across, and cut it entirely all around, nothing will harm; and do not go too deep, as the nerves are all situated beneath the skin, and then place the hand back in hot water, if the blood is congealed in the wound, and cannot flow out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	"And when you have let out as much blood as is needed, then put oil and a bandage on the vein to heal quickly, and do the same for each vein."
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	"The cutting of the vein in the left hand is beneficial for the disease of the mouse (epilepsy), and do everything just as I have told you concerning the right hand."
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sap of the soapwort is beneficial for all illnesses below the body, such as those of the womb, and retention of flow, and illness of the kidneys, and of the old hips and legs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of its sap are such that when the patient places their foot in hot water and rubs the vein until it reddens, and binds above the ankle joint; for the vein is at the ankle, and many kidneys go through there; thus you should choose either the larger kidney or at the ankle, whichever moves more.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	"And if you cut it on the foot, beware of the nerves that are underneath, and cut across just like cutting with scissors; and let the wound heal cleanly."
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	"And if blood cannot flow out, then put the foot back in water and let the vein drain well."
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the sap fails the first time, then apply it again a little higher up, for the place is cold. Do not fear nerve damage, as we have said, and do the same on the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	"The location of the sciatic vein is at the outer ankle bone, and its cutting is beneficial for hip pain when it is caused by hot blood."
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its sap is such that the patient enters into a bath and strains above the ankle four times while twisting, for otherwise the vein will not open. And if it opens, then apply the sap in all possible ways and across; and it is better that you tie it off, for the place is dry, and it responds much to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, then cut any vein that is open on the back of the foot, near the little toe, and beware of the nerves; and make sure to wipe away as much blood as you see, and then untie the bandage, and put cotton on it and press it; now it is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	And regarding the application of cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	"Cupping is done in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking."
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping that is done without striking, there are two ways: either it is performed with fire or without fire. And the cupping that is done by striking and extracting blood is performed in fourteen places on the body, of which one is at the very top of the head; another is in the neck; and two others are on both sides of the neck; and the cupping under the chin; and the cupping of both shoulders; and the cupping above the ribs; and the cupping on both arms; and the cupping of both legs; and the cupping of both ankles. And this cupping does not draw blood, except for some small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore it does not weaken at all, as is done with veinletting. And it is not necessary to apply it, neither with fire nor without fire, in any illness caused bypletion, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if it is necessary due to diseases that one must belch,
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	"And when we see these signs, especially if it is during the month, we order them to cup after three hours of the day."
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The balm of the mouse helps with headaches... that come to the eyes, and it is not necessary for this to occur after evacuation from the whole body; and this ventilation takes place instead of the cephalic salve, and those who are cold by nature should not use it, nor those who have cataracts, as this causes them great harm; therefore old people should not use it, nor those with cold diseases on their head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	"And those who often cut themselves become forgetful, so it is necessary to place the cupping a little lower down for fear of forgetting."
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	Ventilation between the shoulders takes place instead of the salve for the head and basilica, and it is beneficial for the stretching of the breast, and splitting of the channel of the porcupine, and for coughing and bloating; but not too much should be applied, as if it holds too firmly it can cause dizziness in the stomach or heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	Ventilation between the second ribs of the neck is beneficial for headaches, and ophthalmia, migraine, and constriction; and for pain in the roots of teeth, and takes place instead of the basilica salve; but you must instruct the user to press their hand while applying it, so that they do not hit the artery or cause bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	"Cupping under the chin is beneficial for mouth diseases, gum decay, and similar conditions in the mouth, and it is in place of cutting both lips."
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	"Cupping on the shoulders helps with diseases caused by heat andpletion."
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The windings of the ribs are worth as much as three veins of the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins. Command the surgeon not to pierce too deeply, for the place is bare of flesh and full of nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The leech that is placed on the buttock is beneficial for hemorrhoids of the foundation, and for diseases below. It is necessary that the leech be large, and made of brass, so it can draw well; however, if it were delicate, it might break; and it makes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	**Line-by-line translation:**
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the cupping glass is as follows: first apply it empty, and suck temperately, and place it quickly, and move it evenly, and do not cease doing this until you see that the area is red and swollen, and appears the redness of blood; then stop, and remove the cups, and take care in the position of the body, for there are some who have thin flesh and clear pores: thus one should strike once only, and make wide wounds, but not too deep; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, then one must strike twice: the first time to refine the passage of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, then one must strike a third time; and when we wish to draw out blood drop by drop, it suffices to strike once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we wish for much blood, let us recommence often. And if the blood is thick, pierce deeply, and continue until the point suddenly reaches the heart. But it behooves those with thick and hard skin, and those with narrow pores, to oil the places of the cups with aperitive and dissolvent oil: if it is in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in winter, with cress oil, or lily oil, or camomile oil, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, use almond oil, or balsam oil, or aniseed oil, or something similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one being treated has tender flesh and wide pores, it is not necessary to apply oil there, but rather, after the bloodletting, wash it with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or pumpkin water, or porcelain water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture should rise using basil water, myrtle water, sumac water, and things of that sort.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have abundant excesses get up in the morning with old wine, or water from a spring, or decoction of anise or camomile, or similar things; and they should not let themselves be cupped before or during the bath, but after the bath for one or two hours; and they should not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that they warm themselves when they are about to be cupped and when they are being cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware those who are cupped if they are choleric, and if the blood is too thick and inflamed; for they should take cold things, such as pomegranates, endive, lettuce with garlic, and similar things; and eat small fish, and castrated animal flesh, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those with cold complexion should take honey syrup, and moderately fragrant wine that is between old and new, and eat pea soup, and small fish and birds, and drink more than they eat on the day they are cupped; and sometimes give trocisc or muscat to some men before or after cupping, to strengthen the main limbs; and let the blood be subtle, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	Ventouses placed without piercing are those used on the liver, womb, and for gout, as well as on the belly, buttocks, back, and thighs. These members cannot tolerate being pierced, and one only uses fire to draw blood from member to member, as we do when placing ventouses on the breasts during wet nursing; to remove viscosity from a limb, as we place ventouses on the belly and buttocks to reduce swelling; and to alleviate pain caused by blockage or stones, its attractive power may sometimes draw off the blockage or dislodge the stone from its place. Similarly, it does when placed on the liver and womb if there is retained wind. These ventouses are administered empty for sucking alone, but sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with hot water, such as in cases of pleurisy, and so one fills the ventouse with warm water or water in which appropriate herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cup administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And there are two of them wide and half a palm deep, and around the middle on one side there is a small hole like for inserting a needle, made of brass, soft in front so it does not cut the patient when placed on the limb; and in the middle there is a transverse rod of brass or iron to hold an inserted candle, and they come in various sizes according to the diseases and the age of those who use them; for the cups of children are different from those of old people, and of the thin from those of the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should place this cup on the limb thus: insert the wax or flax candle and put it across the rod that is in the cup so that the flame is at the bottom of the cup so it does not burn the patient; then place it on the limb with the hole we mentioned above, so that when needed, steam can escape, and remove the cup; and then remove the cloth as before and repeat this often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping procedure used for the disease of pleurisy, especially acute cases, there is no tube or hole, and it is not filled with fire except when it is full of air, and it is placed on the member alone; this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without fire are used cupping procedures only in members where one cannot apply cups due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places; also in places devoid of flesh, like the ears or nostrils, and others like them. The quality of using these is that when you find leeches that are in clear, sweet waters without any defect, take them; put them in a jar with sweet water until they become accustomed and have nothing in their bellies; then prepare the vein and cup, rub the member until it becomes red, and place the leeches on it; and when they are full and drop off, if it is a place where one can apply a cup, apply one, for this is very beneficial afterward.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If this is not so, then lift the wound gently, and then with water, very well, and then press it; and if the wound bleeds too much after the body of the veins, then moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and place upon it, until the blood is staunched; and if the blood is multiplied, then place powdered vitriol or gall, and similar things, until it is staunched; or you may place on the wound half of peeled fava beans, and leave them until they adhere to the wound, now it will staunch.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the veins do not take hold, then rub the wound with fresh blood, or prick it with a needle until some blood comes out, and then place them upon it, and as soon as they sense the blood, they will adhere; and when you see that they are full, then powder some aloe and celery seed, ground up, or ash, and now they will fall off.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	"Here begins the book of fractures"
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	"This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine and is a remedy for fracture and dislocation."
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that foolish physicians throw themselves into this chapter without ever having seen any of the old books or read any letter concerning it; and thus, knowledge is lacking in our land, for I found none who was good at it. And I know nothing except through the science of ancient books which I have studied so much that I have treated the science therein, and by experience, and by the habit of my life. And I have described for you in this chapter what is contained therein, and abbreviated it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of instruments arranged as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	"It is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the sums of our words and chapters where the wise devote their understanding and remain on the path of truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art and teach it to others."
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when fracture or dislocation or torsion or contusion occurs to anyone, you must promptly advise the patient on both sides, unless there is some impediment such as weakness of body or childhood or old age, or if the time is not very hot or too cold; and avoid eating cold foods, specifically cold drinks, and the flesh of birds and hares, and do not drink wine nor eat fatty meats, nor fill oneself too much with foods that congest the veins with blood, until you doubt a hot aposteme or an expansion of matter in the limb. Thus, the patient should return to their usual regimen that they had been following.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	"And when the fractured bone begins to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that promote growth and have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, eggs, fish, and similar foods, along with abundant wine."
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	"For with this kind of nourishment, muscle tissue is regenerated and healing occurs more quickly."
