Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the bones of the elderly and decrepit cannot be well reset or mended according to their nature due to weakness in the limbs, nor those that are too tender like the bones of young children. But there is a remedy: apply large splints that hold and join the limb together until it regains its former strength; do not break any part of the bone, and for this reason, it must be nourished with thick foods as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	"And know that fractures are diverse in many ways."
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	"For a fracture of the head is different from one of the arm or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all manner of fractures."
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	"There are fractures that occur suddenly, like when falling from a height, and others that occur gradually, such as carving a quill for writing."
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	"And there is fracture with wounding, and fracture with just a slight crack."
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And for each type of fracture there is its own device and appropriate tool in restoring it according to where the pain occurs. Fractures are known by the twisted appearance at the site, which can be clearly felt upon examination, and heard when pressing with the hand. When there is no twisting or sound upon touching and the patient does not feel much pain, then there is no fracture; however, there may still be some twisting, splitting, or minor fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	"So do not move the limb by hand but apply the medicines mentioned below and then gently immobilize it."
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the break which goes into a tree, and are the two parts dislocated, it is necessary to set them together evenly before an abscess comes; and if an abscess comes quickly, let it remain some days until the abscess quiets; then place it evenly on the move that you can easily move it smoothly, and know that the restoration of this one is easier than the restorations of those where there are pieces; then bind it as it should be hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bone is broken into pieces and is in two parts, whether it's a hand or foot, or for a small limb use your hand, or use two cords or one cord and your hand; and place the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the broken parts of the limb are separated, join them back together with all means at the movement you can, and make sure in your work that the patient does not get injury or pain; and fit the two ends of the bones well according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	"Moreover, one can feel it well with the hand if it seems not to be in its proper place; raise it gently and do not strain or press it too much as those who cause heat and tension in the limb through their work."
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in place, caution the patient well that they do not move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor turning nor in any other manner; and ensure the limb is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And when it feels no pain, then it is not in place, and it must be put into such a position that it feels no pain; and ensure it is set correctly, so that no crookedness comes when it is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	"Know that broken limbs vary in size, shape, and extent."
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	But for small limbs, such as arms and legs and similar ones: they must be wrapped in soft, thin linen cloths; and those that are large, like thighs and calves: they must be wrapped with a wide, strong bandage, because the wide bandage embraces the whole large limb and constrains it evenly on all sides so there is no tightening. Then tie it around with light pads, three or four turns according to the limb, and tighten your hand somewhat on the whole bandage. Then go above the break and tighten less so that the break can be slightly separated from the break; and soften the bandage bit by bit until you grasp much of the healthy area, then take another bandage and wrap it again around the broken area. Then return to the part below the break and tighten moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said above in the first binding. Then place between the bandages linen pads or cloths until it is all even, then tie everything together with one bandage on top, and then place your well-made splints upon it if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or abscess, then place over it something that soothes the hot abscess and removes the swelling, leaving it thus for several days; then press upon your elbow joints, using as supports half of a wide cane reed soaked in water, or wood used to make stakes, or date palm rachis, each according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But the elbow support placed on the fracture must be a bit thicker and wider than the others; and it should also be as long as necessary for the limb's size or thickness. Then press upon the supports just as you did at the first joint, then tie above with a suitable thread, as in the first binding over the breakage; draw tighter gradually, less often; and ensure that the threads are medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the works of foolish people who make their bindings from twisted linen cords, this is a great mistake, because the binding cannot be even if it is too fine, and it should not have less than two fingers' breadth between each support.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the edges of the stars after binding in sound places, then place underneath them lint or woolen bandage so that he does not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When there is a wound with the fracture and the bones are broken, I will speak of its treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that one must not bind all broken members with stars on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	When the limb is large, it is not necessary to put on bandages for more than 6 or 7 days, or even longer according to your certainty about the heat of the swelling. Here is the method of ancient plasters used to heal fractures, dislocations, and twists: take flour that sticks to the walls of the mill, mix it with plenty of eggs, and apply this mixture - not too thick nor too thin - and use it; this is the common way to make a plaster that restores fractures in many cases, especially for women and children, as it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of emplaste restoring fractures and dislocations and distortions: Take aloes and ladanum and fennel and asarabac and tragacanth and myrrh and aloewood, all together nine parts; mastic three parts; aloechy three parts; and make powder of them, and mix with plenty of eggs; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this emplaste, for it has good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is useful to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method for plasters useful in twists: take mugwort and wormwood each 10 drams; myrrh and aloe each 9 drams; acacia 6 drams; bolus armeniacum 10 drams, grind well, mix with water or plenty of eggs, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method for the emplastering of joints and bones displaced from their places, alleviates pain occurring, and sharpens bone setting, and for fractures: take new linen, wet it in warm water and oil cooked, then apply to the place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore (the dislocation), but is good for soothing a hot boil, and properly removes pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plaster that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earth peony leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plastering for the healing of bone fractures and to soften the swelling around the boil.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of mallows, camomile, violet flowers, wheat flour, each one part; grind and mix with wine, and if the limb is inflamed, mix it with diluted coriander water or water, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of plaster stronger than the first one, when a hard boil comes to the healing of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of mallows, linseed, balm, melilot, celery, violet and camomile flowers, each one part; grind, mix with salt water or fresh water or wine according to the warmth of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not apply anything to a broken limb for restoring strength besides wax and oil ointment; he says it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And according to Galen, one should apply slightly warm dry substances like myrrh, aloe, frankincense, and similar things to a broken limb for restoring it, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to treat injury and pain is to take mastic, chewed barley grains or chicken feathers, and silkworms, crush them together with equal amounts of salt, and make an ointment from the mixture.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, after a little while, undo it [the bandage] and make sure the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; if not, do not undo it for many days. And if pain comes at that place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry up, undo it, and remove the dressing immediately; and take a light cloth, and a moist sea sponge, and dip it in water, and lift it to the place until the itching stops, and the pain is eased. Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put dry wool, soaked in water or rose oil, on top, and tie it on with a knot, until you are sure of a hot abscess. And let the inflammation of the member subside, and let the pain be removed, then start the tying again gently, and a little bit of dressing, and do not pull too hard as before; and continue until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the blister is hot, red, painful and swollen, has disappeared completely, and you still need ointment and bandages, then resume them again as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If no improvement is seen in the limb from what we have said, do not attempt to dislocate it until after 3 or 4 or 5 or 7 days; sometimes wait up to 20 days, as long as the bonesetters' fracture starts to heal and the flesh begins to close over; then you may attempt to restrain more firmly than before, and encourage flesh growth. But if the joint appears drier than necessary, know that nutrition cannot reach it; therefore apply warm water compresses whenever you dislocate it, doing so every third day, and slacken the bandage a little. By this method, nutrition will quickly come to the limb and remedy what foolish physicians do when they improperly reset limbs.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the various kinds of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many kinds of fractures there are, with diverse shapes, and their causes are distinguished. For there are fractures caused by the impact of a sword blow, which shatters the bone all the way down to the marrow beneath it, like a hatchet in wood; and for this reason, this type of fracture is called 'hatchet-like'.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword cuts the bone from above without piercing it, and this manner of fracture is called "absolute"; and wounds from these two fractures are large or small in size.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is percussive impact, such as striking with the butt of a rock, falling onto stone, or similar events.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture that approaches the membrane beneath the bone or above it, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And there is a wound that is pressed into the bone as fine as a horse's hair, and the crack is small, and for this reason it is called 'capillary' fracture. And if the wound is made by striking with stone or falling or similar cause, and causes a piece of bone to enter inward, and the place is raised like when coppersmiths strike on cauldrons; then the stones enter therein.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often in those with moist porous bones, such as the head of a child. And it occurs in all these types of fractures that small pieces are dislodged like stars.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all kinds of fractures by their withdrawal from the bone, and by careful examination, and by corrupted flesh that lies upon them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	A hairline fracture is recognized by the fact that when the bone is exposed and rubbed gently, the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In treating a fracture, beware of possible complications such as vomiting blood, loss of consciousness, and extension of the limb, pallor, fever, eyes protruding or turning red, etc. If any of these occur, recovery will not be without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not observe any alarming complication, and you hope for a good outcome, then begin the treatment
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the injured person first comes to you, especially if it is wintertime, remove the bone within fourteen days after the injury.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is summertime, hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the membrane beneath the bone does not become corrupted and the complications we have mentioned do not occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone fracture reaches the membrane that covers the brain, then you must cut open the broken part thus: and take hold of the patient's head with great care, and uncover the bone in all possible ways, gently revealing the wound's figure; and if bleeding or hot swelling appears during bone exposure, help as needed. Then fill the place with woolen pads soaked in rose oil, allowing the wound to rest until the heat subsides and you are sure there is no more bleeding. Then begin removing bone around it in two ways of operation: one way is by narrow cutting in front.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	"And then I add another cut larger than the first."
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	"And the second way is that you have many different cuts, some narrow and others wide, pointed and made of tin, and work lightly so as not to injure the head."
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	"And if the bone is hard and rough, then you must pierce it around beforehand before administering cuts with trephines so that they do not go too deep and pierce through the soft bone. The point should have a margin or circle on top to prevent it from going too far into the bone; and you should have several trephines so that each one fits properly onto the radius of the bone, allowing for all types of bones."
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	"The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are that you place a trephine on the bone and turn it with both hands until you know that the bone is pierced. Then move the trephine to another spot a little later and do this all around, then cut away the space of bone between the perforations with scissors as subtly and lightly as possible so that you can easily remove the bone by hand or with any of your tools such as forceps; be careful not to touch the cerebellum or cerebrum."
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced the bone and scraped it, then it is necessary that you reset the sharp edge that remains of the bone with all other similar instruments to an incisor, but it must be thinner and more subtle than the others; and if there remain any small bones or scales, remove them gently with the tools; then treat the wound with dressings and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	"And another way of operating is that which Galen recommends, which is quicker; he praises it highly, and this is his opinion."
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	"Firstly, you must uncover a part of the bone where the fracture is most visible. Then, once this part has been uncovered, place the lenticular trephine on top of it, as shown below:"
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side only, for the part is sharp on both sides, so that the cutting edge faces towards the bone; then strike gently with a small hammer, so that you break the bone evenly all around, and be careful of the cloth beneath it; if it adheres to the bone, remove it gently, for it can be removed without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	"And if the bone fracture does not reach the flesh, and the bone is cut only on one side with small fragments remaining, then you should remove this roughness. Use a fine rasp in various quantities to best fit the work and shape of the fracture."
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	"Use coarse rasps first, then finer ones, until it is smooth."
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	"For each of the other cuts and fine fractures, you must adapt your approach according to its direction; this is something that cannot be learned from those who have studied this art."
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the sinew is exposed, it is necessary that you take one cloth of linen, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled into two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth; and do this as gently as possible so that you do not burden the sinew, then apply a bandage above it, but do not tie it too tightly, only enough to moisten the wound; and leave it thus for one or two days until the swelling is reduced, then untie it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, iris flour, frankincense powder, aristologium, and similar things; and make a powder of these things and place it on the wound, and apply warm medicinal ointments without biting; and ensure that the wound is always clean, leaving no ointment nor allowing flies to gather on the brain cloth, for when flies gather upon the brain cloth, they will corrupt and poison it, causing great harm to the patient; for when something irritating is placed on the sinew, it becomes necrotic above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	"Therefore, if any bad accidents occur to the patient, as we have said, be very cautious and doubtful without doubt."
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackness appears on it due to the medicine applied there, which may have such power, then you should take one part of honey and three parts of rose oil and mix it with one drachm of gum; then apply it to the face; then follow the usual methods of treatment until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one alone, for they are two bones; and the lower one is cartilaginous and does not break unless struck or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two bones is broken, then place your little finger or a hollow reed over it and insert the break evenly into the space between your index finger and thumb, pressing gently until the bone returns to its natural shape; do this carefully so that the patient does not feel pain from your actions.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose and your finger cannot reach it, then you must place a small wooden stick against it to hold it steady.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in two pieces, then do likewise; and hurry to reset it on the first day if possible. If not, after the seventh or tenth day when the swelling has subsided, then wrap a bandage of linen cloth around the head of the bone where the break occurred.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you set one bone against another on the opposite side, if there is a fracture there; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the holes of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some physicians say one should grease the tents with butter and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem good to me that they should be greased with butter and changed every day. Rather, they must be greased with a mixture of egg white and flour powder, then leave the tent until the bone is firm and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes feathers from a goose are used instead of bandages, and if there is one soft cloth around them, the fracture will stay in place and the patient will feel better; now do what you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if any swelling comes to the nose while you are working on it, then put cerate or cotton moistened in rose oil or in a drop of diachylon there.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no abscess forms there, then apply a plaster made of ground sesame seeds and incense powder, mixed with egg white. Then place light bandages on top without tying them tightly. And if the fracture is small but shattered into many pieces, extract it using appropriate tools, then sew up the wound and treat it according to usual care for such things; binding, suturing, etc., using appropriate plasters and ointments. If there are no wounds inside the nose, then treat with tents and insert splints of lead until healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	de la routure de la mandibule
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is broken underneath and there is no wound outside, and the fracture is only apparent and not broken in two pieces except for small fragments inside, then it is easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary that if the fracture is on the right side, you put your two index fingers in the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is on the left jawbone, then put your two index fingers of the right hand inside gently and hold it with your other hand from outside and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is displaced in two pieces, then you must apply traction from both sides until it is even and aligned.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement of teeth or fracture, then tie them with a thread of gold, silver or silk, then put cerate on the broken jawbone and put a double cloth over it; then put a large well-made bandage or a piece of leather the same size as the jawbone, long and wide according to the jawbone, and tie it under the chin that you can see, and command the patient to rest and chew light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, then untie it on the third day and then put back in place what has changed; then put a plaster made of flour with egg yolk or sesame flour after removing the cerate; then put light linen over the plaster, and if the plaster dries up and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it is well; many times it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come, then apply what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is both fracture and wound together, be sure that no piece of bone has been taken out. Then carefully extract it with appropriate instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it with fire according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And when you have removed all these fragments, and none remain, then stitch the wound, if it is wide, and apply one of the suitable emplasters to cauterize, so that it may heal."
de la forcele	"with great strength"
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceful blow strikes several times before, toward the shoulder, and the break is in one of three ways: either it is broken and dislocated in two places, with fragments, which is easiest to reset; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the treatment is when the break is without wound, that you have two assistants: one holds the arm that feels the force of the break; and the other extends the neck towards the part. Then place the break evenly in your two hands, so that the form is as it should be, neither twisted nor crooked.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place under the shoulder of the patient a round pad made of cloth or wool, and it should be thick according to your need. Then stretch and lift the forceful blow, and hold the pad with your hand so that you can set the break evenly as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the forceful blow outward because it comes from deep inside, then the patient must lie on their back with their shoulders hanging down, and place a medium pillow under the shoulder. Then have the assistant push the shoulder downward until the bone of the forceful blow is lifted up.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then align the break with your two hands, and if it is misaligned, you must cut upward. Then pull out the fragments gently, and if the bone cannot meet due to any obstacle, then use one of the chisels that you have to scrape it away. But place this instrument under the forceful blow to ward off the sinews.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it resembles a spoon, and is not raised, and should be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and have two heads, as you see, and one should be wide, and the other narrow, like the width of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of hot abscess, then cut the wound, and if the opening is small, or you doubt hot abscess, then cover the wound with cloths and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot inflammation comes, then soak a bandage in rose oil mixed with honey and vinegar and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	To reset the bone without wounds or cuts, you should place on the bone the plaster made of ground millstone and egg white, and put light bandages on top, and place a splint under the armpit if needed; then take a very large bandage about a palm wide, and place a double cloth over the bandages and plaster; then take a subtle belt three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage so that the ends of the bandage hang down; and place the belt on the break, and wrap the bandage around the neck, and under the healthy armpit, and under the injured armpit; and tighten each part, and when you see that the binder holds the break well, and you clearly see that the belt does not move over the broken bone, then wrap it every day, and when the ligaments relax, then bind it more tightly; and make the patient lie on his back, and place a small pillow under the armpit to lift the shoulder up; thus relieve the pressure of the break by relieving the tension of the shoulder, or tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless something bad happens, for up to 20 days; then restart the plastering if necessary, and tighten it and leave it like that until it is healed; and it will be healed in the most part within 28 days, and in less time with some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Regarding the break of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the shoulder bone is broken or displaced, it cannot be felt except by touch; then arrange it according to the shape of the break and reset it according to its natural form in every way you can. Then place flour mixed with egg on the joint along with light bandages, and cover it with a double cloth. Then place a wide, thin board slightly larger than the shoulder over it, and if there are any hairs beneath the board on some part of the shoulder, fill those hairs with linen wicks so that the board lies evenly. Then bind it firmly all around with a large bandage so that the board does not move from its position. Check the binding each day, and every time it loosens, tighten it again. If the board has shifted from its place, reposition it evenly, and have the patient lie on their side. The shoulder will be reset in 20 or 25 days. Once this period is complete, remove the bandage, but be sure that it's not an easy bone to dislocate lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone sticks out in front and there is nothing under it to support it, then cut it off and do what we have said for healing hot inflammation in cases of shoulder dislocation.
de la brisure dou pis	Regarding the break of the arm
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The flesh is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; however, it often breaks at the back.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it sags downwards, and the patient feels great pain, loss of appetite, faintness, and sometimes vomiting blood; and the cheeks appear hollow at the site of the broken bone.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the healing of this break is as follows: have the patient lie frequently on their back with a pillow between their shoulders. Then press down on the shoulders and bring together the ribs of the two sides at the hands using all possible care to make the bone figure straight. Then place plasters and dressings on top of a thin strip of salt or light wood, wrap it in a cloth, and tie it onto the broken bone so that it does not move. Wind the wrapping around the back and bind it firmly, checking the dressing every hour. If it becomes loose, tighten it again. If it needs to be untied due to corruption, itching, pain, or inflammation, do so quickly and remove the plaster. Then redo the plaster and binding as needed until the bone is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Regarding the break of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that rib fractures only occur in the thick parts near the back and at the front of the chest, and they only bend when they are brittle. The pain is felt sharply with each breath two fingers' width from the spine.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment for this is that you set the break evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply a splint, and bind it with a bandage if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib fracture is angled inwards, the patient feels intense pain and sharpness like that of pleurisy, because the bone is pressing on the lung. The patient may have chills, faintness, and vomiting a large amount of blood, which indicates serious condition. In ancient times, this was considered very dangerous.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	"Moreover, there are those who say it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly to reduce displacement."
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	"We do not do this, unless highly skilled physicians have come and seen it firsthand."
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	"And if it has come, then heal it."
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	"And they said that one should apply cupping jars to the place to draw out the moisture strongly, and this seems reasonable. However, there is doubt as to whether the cups will actually draw out the excess fluids due to weakness of the body."
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	"And they said that one should cover the place with wet wool in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to hold it evenly in place. Then treat it with the cure for pleurisy using meat and medication."
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear due to the bone protruding through the skin, causing doubt for the patient, then one must cut over the site of the broken rib and place an instrument underneath to guard the lung; and then one should trim the bone and gently pull it out, and then sew up the two lips of the wound if it is large, and apply splints until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes suddenly, place moistened cloths in rose oil on it and apply them to the spot. And treat the spot with what is necessary for an abscess, and have him lie constantly on his side where it is.
de la brisure dou col	Here's how you can ask about "la brisure du col" (the fracture of the neck) in Old French:
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes breakage occurs at the bones of the neck, rarely does it bend; likewise at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone and you want to know if he will recover or not, take note if his hands are softened, swollen, and numb, and he cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many situations, and if he moves them and feels when they are stretched or pricked, know that the bone joint is saved, and that the patient will be cured with treatment.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if he will recover or not, take note if his feet are softened, and if the accidents that are in hands are also on the back, and windiness and excretion come forth without will; and when one lies him down on his belly, excretion comes forth without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he lies on his back to saddle himself, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Such are the mortal ones: do not labor in their care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not occur, then the condition is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that if there is a hot inflammation, you should apply rose oil or oil of mallow seed to the spine until it is cooled down. Then apply a comforting and drying emplaster, secure it with a linen bandage, and command the patient to rest; and they should not sleep on the part where they feel pain until they are recovered.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is dislocated, you must couch the patient on their back. Remove the displaced bone and then bring together the two lips of the wound if it is large by sewing them up with a suture. Then treat it with ointment for wounds until healed. And if the joint of the bone is broken, which is called the “joint of the cow,” you should put your left hand pouch in place of the bone and support it with your other hand using all your strength. Then apply the emplaster and bandage if necessary, bind it tightly, and if there are displaced bones, open them up and remove them, then treat the wound until healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Regarding the fracture of the thighbone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It happens rarely that the thighbone is broken, and if it does happen, there will be a slight loss of consciousness at the head. The wound opens up lengthwise and slopes towards the knee, causing pain and sharpness in the area where it has been broken. Swelling occurs where the bone has snapped.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you should extend your hand over the break until you are able to locate it. Know what type of fracture it is and its shape. And if the fracture is only at the top, then bring the fracture into alignment so that it is in its natural position.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is lengthwise or slopes inward, have the patient lie on their stomach so that you can see the alignment of the fracture clearly.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And once you have aligned it, apply an emplaster and then place a splint made of wood or bone. Bind the fracture tightly so that it does not move, and support the area below the hips until the alignment is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if there is an inflammation around the wound, do not touch it until the inflammation has subsided. Then apply what was mentioned earlier and return to the reduction of the fracture, binding it as necessary if there are no complications. This is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Regarding the fracture of the humerus
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The humerus is the bone between the elbow and the shoulder joint. If it is broken, it should be reduced in one of two ways:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie two joints with two strings,
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	"And the other manner is thus: place the patient on their back, and have them raise their hand to their neck. Then command two ministers: one shall grasp what is above the fracture at their hands, and the other shall grasp below at just one line, each stretching according to their part."
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too strong, then restrain the ligaments below and above the fracture, and extend each of the ministers to his part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, then you must place one ligament in the middle under the saddle, and another towards the elbow, under the fracture; and likewise if the fracture is towards the elbow, then you must place the ligament lightly without effort until the fracture is even on its place and on the elbow; then set the fracture evenly as it should be, and bind it if an abscess appears.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	"And if inflammation occurs, do not bind until it has subsided for seven days. Apply a damp linen cloth moistened in axle oil and rose oil until the inflammation has decreased. Then bind as follows: place the splint on the fracture, bring the arm up to the sling, and place your hand on the shoulder or breast. Place the bandage and bind over the sling and arm so that the arm is in line with the stars, unless something prevents it from doing so, or if the bone has been moved."
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	"And if you suspect that the bone is not setting properly, use stars and place a larger and stronger one on the fracture than the others. Place two fingers' width between each star, and let each star be so large that it extends three fingers beyond either side of the fracture. Then bind over the stars as I have described at the beginning of this chapter, binding more firmly and not allowing any separation."
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the setting of the splints and the binding as we have said in the time when you restore the broken limb, and if you doubt the hot abscess, then leave it tied for seven days as we have said; then examine each ligament every three days to ensure that there is no itching or swelling at its place, lest nourishment cannot reach the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it is necessary, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents occur, then untie him only after 3 days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, with his hands on his stomach. Place one pillow full of wool evenly under the shoulder, and watch every hour of the day or night that the figure of the broken limb does not move, or that the ligatures do not soften. Then apply the ointment by the power of medicine, and give him the food we mentioned earlier in such a way that at first it is subtle; and when he begins to recover, make it thicker.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	It is customary that the shoulder and leg should be reset 40 days after; then one must untie him and administer baths and ointments to set the limb straight.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the dislocation is ugly and jammed in, let it remain 50 days or two months before untieing.
de la brisure du bras	Here is a summary of the instructions given for reducing and immobilizing a broken arm:
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones called the "fuscile," one of which is small and guides the wrist; the other is large and located beneath it near the little finger. Sometimes only the large bone breaks, or sometimes only the small one does, but sometimes both break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the little bones are broken, restoration is easy, and healing; but when the big ones are broken, healing is bad, and more grievous than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the little bone is broken, then it needs to be gently stretched out and made even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	But if it's the big bone, then it needs to be stretched more forcefully; and lay it out on the cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and let the little finger hang lower than the other fingers, and have the patient cross themselves over themselves, and put the cushion in front of them higher up so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then extend the minister's left arm to the part below his hand or elbow, and another minister to the other above it.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	Then let the master put it back together according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces missing, then place each one back in its proper position; and if there is any bone that cannot be grasped by the hand, and you are unable to restore it to its place, then saw through it and join the bones together, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if there is also an open wound with the fracture, I have spoken about that in the chapter on open wounds; take care accordingly.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	But if at the beginning of restoration wounds appear hot, then apply a bandage made of cerote cloth soaked in rose oil and white wax, not too hard nor too soft; and tie the bandage gently on top so that the hot wounds are appeased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the fat, and place the emplaster of powdered millet with abundance of egg, then place the splints, ensuring that the one for breaking is stronger and somewhat wider than the others; and know that it should have six splints on the arm in various arrangements: whether the break is in one bone or two; and bind tighter above the break than elsewhere, and always looser as you go along, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the bandages that are placed on the break be soft and moist, not hard or harsh; and let the thread with which it is bound be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	Reward the limb and the bandage after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident happens to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you should wash the limb with warm water until that itching is appeased; and let the limb rest not too tightly.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin the strapping, and if the ligaments are softened and the bone dislocated, and similar things, then adjust it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take care that the swelling does not come to the limb because it is too tight, then you should soften it a little and leave it thus for a few days until the swelling has gone down, then tie it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	But if none of these things we have mentioned come to the patient, do not untie him for up to twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Or whoever around him then let him hang his hands on his neck and keep them even, and guard against movement and dislocation, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in thirty days or thirty-five, and sometimes in twenty, according to the compositions and temperaments of the humors.
de la brisure de la main	Chapter on the Fracture of the Hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that at the back of the hand and the back of the wrists there are few fractures, but many twists occur there.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or twisted, then let the patient sit cross-legged and sit upright before him evenly; then place his hand on the table, and extend the fractured bones, and align them correctly with the help of the surgeon until they are properly joined together; then apply the plaster and splints, if there are no wounds, then apply a bandage according to the size of the wound; and wrap it in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	"And if the break is on the outside around the belly of the foot, make a bandage of cloths and command the patient to bind it to their broken foot; then bind with a long cloth strip, and let the knot be soft as large as the sole of the hand, and bind it tightly."
