Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	"And if the break is on the front, then you must place a bandage above it and another below in the sole so that the hand is open and straight; then bind it all around the hand, and secure the knot between the two."
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	"And if the break comes on any of our fingers, if it is the thumb, then set it equal as it should be; and bind it with the sole, and if you see fit place a small straight bandage to raise the broken part, and do not move it. And if the break is on another finger, such as the index or one of the others, then set it equal, and bind it with the healthy finger that follows; or bind them all together in one bandage, whichever is better, or place a bandage like that on the thumb, and take care in the healing and arrangement of hot poultice, and treat what comes from it as I have said."
de la cuixe brisie	"for a broken thigh"
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and it can be seen when it turns front and back; and its restoration is done by binding one bandage above the break and another below."
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	"And the patient lies on their face, then each helper extends their bandage to their side evenly; and this is when the break is in the bone."
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the thigh, then one of the ligaments should be towards the knife, and the other ligament below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And likewise if it is near the knee, then let the ligament be by the knee, and let the extension be below; then let the surgeon set the bone even with both hands until it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the splint, and tie it up, provided no abscess occurs.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	"And if there is a hot poultice, let it cool down and then return to your task and care; the bandaging is done in this manner."
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap the fracture with a hard doubled bandage twice or thrice, and let the excesses remain; then twist the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and insert a long thread between the hip and the leg, below the knee joint, and bring the ends of the thread upwards; then wrap the leg and hip with the bandage again, then place splints on the fracture, and place one splint on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and hip with soft cloths to make the pressure even; then begin to tie firmly three or four times on the fracture; and when higher up on the fracture, it is less tight; then turn to the two ends of the thread that you inserted between the leg and hip, and tie three splints that are above, then return downwards to the end of the thread until you reach near the foot; and make it tight so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus; until there appears neither inflammation nor swelling nor anything similar.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	"And if something comes from it, untie it and address what comes as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone sticking out, then remove them if possible; and if not possible, then cut open the space and extract it; and treat it as we have said until it is healed."
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	"And sometimes the thighbone breaks in such a way that splints are placed on it, like in the case of the arm; nonetheless, with this kind of treatment, the patient does not limp."
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	"And know that the thighbone is restored in one week, or a little less or a little more, depending on the different constitutions."
de la ruelle dou genoil	"of the crease of the knee"
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know this: In the groove of the knee there is little breakage, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, then it is only a fracture or hole, and this happens in all wounds, and without wounds, which everyone knows.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the reset is done by placing what is round on its two sides until it can be moved together; then put the bandage, and put a round splint if you need one, and bind it as necessary; then check all the arrangements that we have mentioned in other fractures, such as heat and similar appearances; then apply to each accident whatever is needed until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know this: The leg has two bones, of which one is rightly called the "fibula," and the other is called the "tibia"; and all birds have a similar breakage when it comes to the arm, and therefore their restoration is just like that of the arm, and the work is all the same. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg twists in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the fibula is broken, it twists forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, great pain is felt and it is clearly visible; and it turns downward.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore apply traction, place it evenly, and tie the splints evenly; but nevertheless, if the fracture is ugly with many pieces, then traction should be lighter and gentler, and raise according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, then take two strips of flexible wood that wrap around the leg on both sides and are long from the knee downwards; then wrap these two strips with two bandages above and below, and tie them in the middle as well, so that the leg cannot bend to the right or left at this joint, and this is good. And some arrange a splint of wood the length of the leg, and place the leg on it to prevent movement, and this is done properly when there is a wound near the fracture; and move the leg every day to see if there is heat or other accident; then treat it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the fractures of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but sometimes a fracture comes to the bones of the foot and to the toes, and there is only shaking in many positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture of the bones of the foot, and you see these bones protruding one over the other, then place your foot on the ground like someone who wants to walk, and then place your foot on theirs where the bones are raised, and press until they return to their places; then apply the splint and dressings, and put a small table with two holes under the sole of the foot, and then bind it tightly around the foot, and wrap it with bandages and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the bandage, for you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the toes are broken, restore them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place a splint along the length of the broken toe and a little wider, then place that table I spoke of under the foot and bind it tightly; and if there are two or three or more broken toes, then place a splint on each toe according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the table under the foot; and let them stand on top of the table so that they touch the sole of the foot well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And do not forget the other things I have said about other fractures, and treat each accident according to its need.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Of the fracture of the bone of the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the woman's hip bone is broken, make her sit wide-legged, then incline her toward the back part, and have her held from behind. Then fill the socket of the woman with cotton, packing it as much as one fist. Then raise the woman up, bit by bit, and slowly the cotton will come out until it reaches the entrance of the socket, and the bone will return with the fist. And when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton. And after she has urinated, replace it, and do this for about seven days or so: then the break will be healed. And if you wish, take a sheep's bladder, tie a tube at the hole, and insert the whole bladder into the socket. Then blow into the tube forcefully until the bladder is full inside; then the socket will return to its proper place. Then fill it with cotton, and leave it like that for some days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the little finger of man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said regarding the thighbone. Such fractures are not hidden from one who applies study and practice, and understands my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture indicates in many cases the correct path for restoration; therefore, understand this.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's craw and put the penis into it; then wrap bandages around it and leave it for three or four days or so, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	Of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with wound, especially if it is large, such as the bone of the hip or shoulder or similar, that he be cauterized immediately, so that the cauterization which we have described may testify to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healed, then apply the plaster of vitriol, or whatever else you have, and then begin to reset the fracture at that same hour, or on that day, if there is no inflammation.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if inflammation is present, then leave the reduction until a new day, until the inflammation has subsided, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would thereby cause harm.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone which has been broken appears above the exposed heart, then it is necessary that you put it back together lightly with your hands, using slight traction.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if traction does not allow you to align the bone ends with your hands, then use this tool made of iron, which is 27 or 28 inches long and its width corresponds to the size of the wound; and for that reason it is necessary for the surgeon to prepare three or four of them, according to what he needs in each case of fracture, and they should be round and somewhat thick so that they do not bend under pressure on the member where you are working, and they should have a pointed end at the front, and be thicker in the middle, as follows:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called 'palainche', therefore the curved head of the bone should be placed on the protruding bone; press once until it returns to its original position, ensuring both sides are even.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is slight and tools cannot grasp the bone well, you must chop off the head of the bone until tools can hold it firmly.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you are unable to reduce the bone as we have described, then cut off a piece of an appropriate tool, such as a chisel or scalpel, with all your might; then remove the rough edges and small splinters that remain on the bone.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	When the bone is reset but the patient still feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you ensure it is in its natural place, then moisten a cloth in black stiptic wine and apply it if it is summer. Do not use cerote or other oily substances on the wound as they cause decay. Then provide support after resetting the bone, leave the wound uncovered, cut away the surrounding skin according to the size of the wound, and ensure that the wound is not constricted with the fracture; many foolish physicians have done this causing harm or death to patients. Make sure the bandage is softer and more flexible than usual for other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad accident may come of it, as we have said, and you find pain at its location, do not place hot coals on it; but wrap hard cloths around it instead.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when after one or two days you see that the wound has begun to suppurate, then remove what you placed on it before any wine, and apply healing ointment to it, such as tetrafarmacon ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary to dress the member twice a day, in the morning and evening, until it is united and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the member be positioned in such a way that the bowstring runs smoothly downward.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass and the bone still cannot heal but continually swells up again, know that there are small pieces of bone present which cause this pain. Therefore, you must probe the wound with a tent and remove all these unwanted pieces that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula appears at the location, or another type of corruption, then you must treat it according to what is said in this chapter earlier.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, like the hip or shoulder bone, and other similar ones of large limbs, do not attempt to pull it out because many times death results. Rather, leave it alone until it rots, perhaps it will fall off by itself after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if you are able; but if you cannot, then leave it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Chapter on fractures that occur on the union
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Many times, after the healing of a fracture, especially when it is near a joint, the appearance of the limb is unpleasant to see, and sometimes the member cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore be careful if the nail is fresh: you should administer stypptic medicines such as aloes, frankincense, myrrh, and sarcocolle, acacia, and similar others. Take some of these things or all together and combine them with stypptic wine or with egg yolk or with mustard; put them on the wound in poultices and tie it tightly, not untied for many days; then remove it and begin again another one until the node has been removed. Or you can apply a well-made piece of lead; for the property of lead is to remove all swellings from the limbs. And if the node has already turned into hardness like stone and needs to be removed, then cut it open above and remove the excess apparent matter. Or you can have it shaved by some barber until it is removed, then treat it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Chapter on members that are weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone has been restored and afterwards the member remains weak and thin, this happens for many reasons: one reason is that it was tied too tightly, and not tied as it should have been. Or because there were too many bandages, and the nourishment could not reach the member. Or because of excessive bleeding. Or because of too much movement, not at the right time. Or because there was little blood in his body, so he is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is to make the patient eat well and exercise his body so that blood is multiplied in him. And administer baths, give him joy and amusement. Then apply pitch on the member so that it attracts great nourishment, and frequently anoint it with warm water until nourishment reaches the member, and return it to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	Chapter on members twisted after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration,
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the dislocation is removed by rubbing continually and for a long time with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And arrange movement of the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	"And if the tortuosity is hardened and calcified like stone, so that it needs to be cut away with iron, then one must cut through it up to the bone with a fine, light scalpel. And take care and apply oneself in the treatment."
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	"Here begins the book of dislocations."
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	"A dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its proper place, preventing it from moving; the limb is misaligned and the patient feels great pain and injury."
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	"When dislocation occurs in someone, it must be reduced without delay."
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	But if one waits, the place swells up, and sometimes it cannot be reset well; therefore one should not move the limb when it is swollen: many times it causes spasms and other pains; nevertheless, when this happens, make the patient lie down, then leave him until the inflammation has subsided; then raise the limb with warm water and oil, then gently reset it, and care for each limb as it comes back into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	"And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations from head to foot."
des mandibules	"of the jaws"
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	"It happens rarely that the jaws become dislocated within themselves, and there are two ways in which both can be dislocated: either they are somewhat displaced from their proper places and softened somewhat; or else they are completely dislocated and hang down towards the chest, preventing saliva from entering the mouth, so that he cannot keep his mouth closed nor speak clearly."
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	"If the dislocation is slight, it can be reduced by several methods."
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, then you must reset it quickly, without delaying; and in such a way that the assistants hold the patient's head, and the surgeon places one hand with a pouch into the root of the jaw dislocation inside the mouth, if the dislocation is on both sides; and the other two hands should be free to apply pressure evenly; and instruct the patient to soften his jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the master makes it even until it returns to its place
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the return is difficult, especially if it's both jaws at once, then apply hot water and oil so that they move easily; do not force the return, as we have said
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are reset evenly, and the mouth of the patient closes well without softening, then place moistened cloths in wax made from rose oil and wax, then lightly bind with soft linen; and let the patient sleep on their back, with their head between two pillows so that it does not move to either side or strain itself to chew, but take light food until the pains are gone and the jaw is healed; and then they may chew what they wish easily, and need not trouble opening their mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well healed and sound.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be properly reduced within an hour and are not returned to their places, then fever and trembling will ensue, and sometimes diarrhea and possibly vomiting of clear bile may occur
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see these signs, know that it is a lost case; and many times the person dies within eight days
de la forcelle	Of lockjaw
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	Lockjaw cannot be dislocated from the side inward and is sometimes dislocated downward; this can be felt
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the resetting is such that the patient lies often on their back and extends their arms; then press it firmly with your palm, and it will return; then place the emplastrum and the bandage, and bind it; and the shoulder which is towards the side cannot dislocate again; if it does not, and if it dislocation happens any time, then reset it to its place as we have said; then place the emplastrum and the bandage, and bind it, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed; and similarly is reset the shoulder blade when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder dislocates in only three ways: one is when it dislocates towards the side of the hip below; and the second is at the part of the breastbone; rarely does it dislocate above, but this happens little; nor does it dislocate behind due to the shoulder, nor inside due to the nerves. And often it dislocates downwards towards the hip, especially in those with a lot of flesh, for they jump quickly and dislocate hastily; while those who have less flesh, it jumps hardly at all, and returns hardly at all.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes some people suffer a blow or fall and the shoulder becomes swollen with a hot inflammation, and they think that it is dislocated because of this
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore you must examine it to make certain, and then begin treatment
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that dislocations are recognized when they occur downwards towards the hip, and there is a difference between the affected shoulder and the healthy one, which you will find manifestly different. You will find a hollow at the head of the shoulder, and below the hip touching the head of the shoulder as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot bring their hand near to their neck nor move in any way. And likewise, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you will find it manifestly upon touching it. This manner of dislocation is difficult to reset when it is old or if the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is for the practitioner to raise the patient's hand upwards and then place their fists underneath the socket and pull up forcibly with the joint until it returns to its place
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in a few days afterward, then the patient should be bathed in warm water; and let him be gently rubbed with mollifying and soothing ointment, such as a decoction of mallow and fenugreek and melilot in water, and let it be applied. Then let the patient lie on his back, and place under his shoulder blade a pad of even wool, not too soft nor too hard. Then the physician places his heel on the pad, and gently lifts the head of the shoulder, and pulls the hand of the patient; and another servant holds the head of the patient so that it does not move down. That shoulder comes back straightaway, and if you wish to reset it according to this manner: have present a man who is taller than the patient; let him stand upright beside the patient's side, and place his shoulder under the patient's shoulder blade, and lift the shoulder up, so that the patient hangs from the arm. And another servant pulls the hand of the patient downward toward the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, attach something heavy to him, and the dislocation will return.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the reset is also done in another way: and this is to plant a long stick firmly in the ground, such that the head of it is as level with the pavement as possible; but not too thick nor too thin. Then place it under the patient, but ensure he has soft clothes underneath, and let the patient lie down along the length of the wood; then stretch out his hand downward on the other side properly, and the joint will quickly return to its place. And if it does not want to return despite all these things that we have said, do this treatment: take a stick of two spans in length and four fingers in width, which has a flat head for entering deeply under the armpit, as shown here:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	And then place cloths over the top of the stick so that it does not bruise the patient and place it underneath the socket of the affected shoulder. Then extend your arm over the stick and attach the sling to it and to the elbow of the hand, then place the arm on a rung of a ladder of the same width and let the hand hang downwards and allow the body to hang on the other side; the joint will return now
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is back in place, however it may be, then you must place underneath the socket a wool pad of equal size and then apply the plaster prepared with powder from the millstone, with incense and egg white all over the shoulder and around it, then press it firmly underneath the socket and twist the bandage on the plaster and tie the hand to its neck in this manner
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that they eat little, so that the member is comforted because it will heal more quickly. And then later after five or six days they should eat more and move around, and if it becomes firm again without becoming softened, then it is healed
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come or for another reason, then you must apply cauterizations at three points, as shown in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	"And if you do all this and after seven days the joint still does not stay in place, and he cannot raise his arm above his head, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be set back in its proper place."
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"If a dislocation occurs toward the elbow, breasts, or behind, it is made by forceful movement and stretching of the hands, and another ligature must be administered; treat until it is healed."
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	"And if after healing there comes stiffness in the limb and delay in movement, then the patient should use it many times until that stiffness is alleviated and returns to its original state."
de la dislocation dou coute	"of dislocation of the neck"
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	"Know that the joint of the neck is dislocated by force and returns by force; and if it is dislocated in all directions, especially front and back, and the dislocation has not been reduced, because one can see and feel it well; and it is dislocated according to each figure."
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick limb with the healthy one, you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	Because the joint is dislocated, it cannot bend the arm or touch the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	"And it is necessary that you reduce it before any swelling occurs, for if swelling does occur, reduction will be difficult and perhaps not possible at all, especially when the dislocation is toward the back; this dislocation is worse than others and causes greater pain, and there may even be death."
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	"And the reduction is when it can be done so that you extend your patient's hand with both of yours; and let his arms be spread out, and place the joints of your hands on either side and above and below the neck, and press the joint into the patient's wrist or palm root until it returns to its proper place."
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	"And if the dislocation is toward the front, then it returns when you fold the hand onto itself and press firmly on the root of the palm where the neck is dislocated."
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not return to its place, apply strong extension; and two assistants extend the arm, while another assistant holds it still during extension; then turn the arm on each side, having wrapped around a long and wide doubled cloth; and when the physician has joined the joint with their hand, they should anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint back into place until it returns; and once it is in place, apply a dry compress with egg yolk, press it firmly, and bind the arm to the patient's neck, leaving it on for several days before removing it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	"And if the joint is firmly fixed in its place, then untie the bandage and leave it alone. And if you see that the joint is not yet well set, then start again with the compress and the bandage, leaving them on for several more days until it is firmly in place. Then remove them."
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if the patient feels pain after the joint has been reset and it moves again, bathe and rub it gently, pressing until it is soothed. Then apply a poultice of grease from a mutton, leaving it on for one day and night before removing it, then place the limb in warm water; when it sweats, rub the joint moderately, then reapply the poultice, then return to the bath. Repeat this process two or three times until the patient is healed; if necessary, apply a moist hot compress of fern with butter, pressing it on.
li dislocation de la main	Dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	"The dislocation of the hand is easy to reduce compared to other joints, but it must be done promptly as soon as it occurs before swelling sets in or heat comes."
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the resetting is such that you place the sick hand on a table, and extend the minister's hand, and the doctor places it evenly, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes it until it returns completely. Then you must look to see if it is in its proper place; then the patient places the back of their hand on a table for extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then the patient places the back of their hand on the table, and the doctor puts his hand on that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, then that's good. If not, then press with soothing plasters until it stops and leaves it thus without starting again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot endure it and you cannot put it in its place after several days, then the joint remains twisted; but it does not harm the patient except that his hand is lame and he cannot grasp anything. Then know that the nerves are cut or the artery. There is no other remedy than cauterization nearby for this case.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	"And when the hand is in place, apply the compress that we have described, then bandage it and leave it for five days before removing it and leaving it alone."
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if the hand cannot move properly and there is some pain, then apply hot water compresses and rub it until it is healed."
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of hand finger dislocations
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	The shoulder joint is dislocated equally on both sides, sometimes at the back of the palm or at the front; then the joint is pushed back into place with your pouches until it returns, then support the head of the joint and tilt it towards the side where it was dislocated; leave it thus for two days, then align it properly on the third day; and tie it up as we have said, releasing it on the fourth day and moving it, then tying it back up again; do this frequently until it becomes firm; and do likewise if it is dislocated at the front of the hand, doing as you did before until it is healed.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Of dislocation of the shoulder blade bone__
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine of the back or neck is dislocated, or there are many dislocations, there is no remedy, for the sick person dies quickly.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the sign is that the patient cannot hold back his excretions voluntarily, and many times some limb is weakened, either both thighs or both arms or one; and many times the spine moves in four places; that which moves at the rear is called 'gilbositez': its treatment is that if gilbositez has come from childhood: then there is no cure nor healing for it.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or percussion or similar things, the ancients have ways of treatment with grand words, but they are not always greatly beneficial; but I have abbreviated it according to my intention, and have made tools in various manners.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the gibbosities which come to the chest before, none has health; and also that which comes directly on both sides, and one cannot cure except that which properly comes to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient be laid out evenly on his face, and have a restraint underneath him so he does not bruise himself; then place one stake at the head firmly in the ground, and another at the feet, and tie one rope under the buttocks of the patient, and another at the hips, knees, and ankles; and two ministers shall hold the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two stakes; and they should be closed tightly, as we have said, and the doctor shall place his palms firmly on the spine until it yields.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this treatment, then take a board of three arms in length, and place it below the skin, and let the patient lie on their side, and put the head of the board beneath the skin, then place the middle of the board upon the spine; and the physician puts his feet upon the other end of the board, and presses hard until it returns to its place; and if you see fit, do so with a turn that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And it is that you drive two stakes into the head of the patient's arm, one on each side towards the feet, with a span of space between each stake above and below; and there should be a hole in each stake where the turner corresponds, and the stakes should be firmly in the ground so they do not move; and between each pair of stakes there should be one turning stake upon which the turner lies, with two small stakes of a span in length for turning the turner; and then tie the rope that is between the stakes to the turner towards the head, and the other rope towards the feet at the other turner, and each minister turns his turner with all the ropes, and the master aligns the spine as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, then place a desiccating plaster with abundant egg, and then the dressings, and then the needle of a tablet of three fingers in length, that it may pierce the spot of the gibbosity and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a linen bandage, as we have said, and use the patient's subtle nourishment until he is healed; and if any matter arises at the end of the healing, then it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines along with the needle that we have mentioned above; and sometimes one administers a piece of lead, and sometimes the appearance comes in the rear spine of the back, and one thinks it is dislocation; but this is the bone that appears, for which one should not be presumptuous: perhaps it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	"Displacements of the hip joint
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	"Know that the hip joints and shoulder joints only suffer dislocations, unlike other joints which can also experience fractures. The hip joint is dislocated in four ways: inward and outward, forward and backward; but more commonly inward than outward or forward and backward."
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation within is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the sick knee opens more widely than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot bend his knee in the fire; and the place which is swollen with heat near the hip indicates this.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	"And the sign of one whose dislocation is outward is that these accidents are opposite to those mentioned before."
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	"And the sign of one whose dislocation is forward is that they can stretch their leg well enough; nevertheless, they cannot bend the knee without pain, and if they try to walk, they cannot do so without difficulty, and they may retain urine, and the angle may be swollen, and when they walk, they tend to limp on the heel."
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	"And the sign of one whose dislocation is backward is that they cannot extend or bend their knee, and their leg appears twisted compared to the other one, and the angle is softened, and the hip bone is located below the ribs."
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	"The treatment for this type of dislocation is to wait and see if the dislocation is old, and if it remains in its position without causing any harm, then there is no need for treatment, and one should not make assumptions about it."
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	"And for those whose dislocation is recent and of the four types mentioned earlier, one should quickly reposition the joint by pushing it inward and outward, and moving it to the right or left; hopefully it will return to its proper place, and no further treatment will be necessary."
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must prepare the assistant strongly, and hold the leg strongly with two hands, or tie it firmly above the knee; and another assistant extends his hand upwards in such a way that he places his hands below the buttocks, then pulls gently with a soft lien on the hip; and another holds the end of the lien; and all extend simultaneously up and down until the patient is lifted off the ground at once and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	"This method of traction is suitable for all four types of dislocation, and if the joint returns to its proper place, as we have said, then that is good."
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then you must apply treatment according to its likeness. When the dislocation is at the hip joint, then you must raise the patient up on their sound side, then place the lien on the root of the hip and the spot below the angle, then pull the lien upwards towards the angle and the thigh; then another assistant takes his arms, embraces the large bone of the sick hip, and extends it strongly backwards: now it will return to its place. This method of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot fasten it in the manner that we have described, then it is necessary to bind the two feet of the patient together with a soft strong rope across both heels and both knees, and let the limb of the sick person extend two fingers more than the other; then hang him from the top of a pole, and let there be two arms' length above the ground. Then command one minister to embrace the top of the thigh, and have another minister hanging with the patient, who embraces firmly the thigh, for now the joint returns hastily.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is at the back, then the patient lies down as we have said in the case of those with goitre, and tie the rope properly around the sick leg and also around the foot; then put two sticks, one at the head and one at the feet, and then stick one stick between the thighs of the patient in this way; and let there be many wet cloths around so that the patient does not blister. Then extend each minister towards him, and the physician puts his hand equally with the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, then put upon [the limb] a bandage, and press it as we have said in the case of pleurisy, and let the patient lie on the sound side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	"And when the dislocation is forward, quickly extend the affected leg as described earlier. Then place the surgeon's hand on the angle of the affected joint and press with the other hand while extending it downwards towards the knee."
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is to the front, then it is not necessary for the patient to extend downward or rise up from the ground; rather, he should be positioned as if his hip were dislocated to the front, as we have described concerning childbirth on two hips; and let him lie on his face, with the bandage extended as we have said before, and press upon the joint at the table; it will be ready when the patient extends his legs, and they are even. Then bring together the thighs, place the splint, and bind it with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and let him rest for three or four days, then untie it and replace the splint. And if you see that they are even, then bind them again as before and leave it on for three days. Then untie it and let the limb go gently until the member is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of knee dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The kneecap can dislocate in three ways: namely, inward and outward, and backward; it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the sign is that you instruct the patient to bend their leg at the hip; if it does not fit with the hip, know that it is dislocated. And the reduction of all this is that you make the patient sit up straight and extend their leg as much as they can; place your back against their thigh and put their foot on yours; then take their knee in your palms and pull it between your thighs, then bend both sides of the knee strongly; and another assistant extends their foot until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it fits easily with the hip; then place the bandage on it, make the leg fit with the hip, and bind them together tightly for three or four days, then untie it; and do not let the patient walk until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not in place, then extend it strongly, as we have said in the treatment of hip dislocation, until it is aligned.
de la dislocation dou talon	"About dislocation of the ankle"
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	"The ankle is sometimes sprained and sometimes fully dislocated both inside and out."
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and it appears bent at the part where it was dislocated; the reduction should be gentle, and one should gently extend the limb with one's hands when it is merely moved.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated entirely, then you should make the patient sit up straight, and have your assistants hold the leg firmly with both hands above the ankle; then pull the foot toward you with your right hand twice, then with your left hand twice, then stretch it upwards, and gently place the foot up high; and do this twice as described, pulling out and stretching the foot; if it returns, good; if not, start again because it will return; and if it cannot return thus, make the patient lie on their back on the ground, and firmly plant a stick in the ground between their thighs, and tie cloths around it so that the patient is not hurt; then an assistant should hold the thigh, and another assistant should stretch the foot with both hands or with a rope tied to the heel; then each assistant should pull evenly, and the stick should always be between the patient's thighs to hold the patient while stretching; then the doctor should gently reset the dislocation with their hands, and another assistant should hold the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is ready, then put the plaster and bandages on, press firmly, tie the foot to the leg, watch carefully the nerves that are behind the ankle joint, so that the binding is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the binding loosens, press it again; then untie it on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient from walking for four days; and if he walks before this time, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"If inflammation sets in after the dislocation has been reduced, treat it as we described earlier until it is healed."
des dois	"about the toes"
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	"When the toes are dislocated, they should be gently extended without force, and this is an easy task."
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any joint of the foot, then you must make the patient sit on a flat surface or on two tables perfectly straight, and place your foot on what opens out from these joints, then press firmly with your foot until it returns to its original position; and when it is even and nothing opens up, then put under the sole of the foot a board with two legs, then press firmly and leave for three days, then untie him; and let him rest until he is well.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Concerning wounds and dislocations together:
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When injury comes with dislocation and you wish to restore it, many times the patient dies: therefore be not presumptuous in your care unless you are wise in the art and have long practiced it, and if you are compassionate and cautious, not hasty; and at first use things that soften heat, and leave the patient in God's hand if there is no hope of healing; but when there is hope, then set the limb in its place before the hot swelling comes; and when the limb is in place, then apply things that soften heat, and treat the wound with drying ointments as it should be done. But if bones are broken or small ones dislocated, then set them, and do as we have said for simple injuries. And guard against entering a path of fear, according to what I have said, for this will move you according to your Creator, and for the preservation of your armor and body.
Amen	Amen
